1401 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


NO. 01-91-01053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


850 S.W.2d 294; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 955



April 1, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
April 1, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of February 4, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1117.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 577. 906.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing overruled


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On motion for rehearing, appellant sought review of a conviction from the District Court of Harris County (Texas) which denied his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Charged with a criminal offense, appellant filed a motion to suppress evidence alleging that police illegally stopped his car without probable cause and then questioned him without proper warnings. The trial court conducted an evidentiary hearing on the motion September 10 and recessed the hearing until November 1 in order to allow the state to produced documents requested by appellant. On November 1, appellant filed and delivered to the state in court his memorandum of law raising nine new grounds to suppress evidence. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal of appellant's conviction, the court affirming, holding the complaints raised for the first time in the memorandum of law had not been preserved for review under Tex. R. App. P. 52(a). Appellant filed a motion for rehearing, which the court overruled. Pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.01, § 2 (1989), the court noted, new matters not raised or filed seven days before the hearing could not be allowed except by permission of the trial court for good cause shown. Because appellant did not seek such permission and did not show good cause, the court held, the new matters were not properly before the trial court.


OUTCOME: Holding that new matters raised in appellant's memorandum of law on his motion to suppress had not been preserved for review, the court overruled appellant's motion for rehearing and affirmed his conviction.

 

1402 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tyrone v. State


No. 2-91-326-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


854 S.W.2d 153; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 901



March 31, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. TWO OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE HON. HARRY HOPKINS



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed as it pertains to guilt. We reverse and remand the portion of the judgment relating to punishment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Criminal District Court No. Two of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted appellant, on a jury verdict, for sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(a)(2)(A) (1989), and sentenced appellant to prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(a)(2)(A) (1989). Appellant sought the court's review asserting that § 22.011(a)(2)(A) was unconstitutionally vague, that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on accomplice witness testimony, and by allowing evidence of unadjudicated extraneous offenses under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1993). The court held that a defendant could not successfully challenge a statute for vagueness when it clearly applied to his conduct. Here, the evidence established that appellant penetrated the victim's vagina, conduct which was clearly proscribed by § 22.011(a)(2)(A). Further, because appellant's victim, as a minor, could not legally consent to statutory rape, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.14 (1979), which required corroboration of accomplice testimony, did not apply. Judgment of guilt was therefore affirmed. However, where evidence of unadjudicated extraneous offenses were admitted during the punishment phase of trial, and where the court could not say without a reasonable doubt that error did not contribute to appellant's punishment, judgment of punishment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: Judgment of guilt affirmed where the statute under which appellant was convicted clearly applied to his conduct, and where because appellant's victim was a minor and therefore could not consent to statutory rape, accomplice witness testimony was not required. Judgment of punishment reversed and remanded where evidence of unadjudicated extraneous offenses was erroneously admitted during the punishment phase of appellant's trial.

 

1403 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


EnRE Corp. v. Railroad Comm'n of Texas


No. 3-92-497-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


852 S.W.2d 661; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 907; 127 Oil & Gas Rep. 147



March 31, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 491,378, HONORABLE JOE B. DIBRELL, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which dismissed its suit for judicial review of appellee railroad commission's order assessing civil penalties and requiring appellant to plug four oil wells. Dismissal was based on appellant's failure to comply with Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 81.0533(b) (Supp. 1993) requiring prepayment of the penalty as a prerequisite for judicial review.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Texas railroad commission ordered appellant corporation to plug four wells and to pay an administrative penalty. Appellant timely complied with all the prerequisites for judicial review of appellee's order except one: appellant failed to make a cash deposit or post bond to cover the penalty assessed, as required by Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 81.0533(b) (Supp. 1993). The trial court dismissed the case based on appellant's failure to comply with § 81.0533(b). On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's ruling and remanded for judicial review of appellee's order. The court held that the prepayment provision of § 81.0533(b) violated the open courts provision of the Texas Constitution, Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, by unreasonably restricting access to the courts. The court likewise stuck down the forfeiture provision, Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 81.0533(d) (Supp. 1993). However, the court found that the manner of judicial review set forth in Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 81.0533(e) (Supp. 1993) did not violate appellant's right to a jury trial as guaranteed by Tex. Const. art. I, § 15, because judicial review of administrative orders was not constitutionally mandated.


OUTCOME: Concluding that the penalty-prepayment and forfeiture provisions authorizing the dismissal of appellant corporation's suit were unconstitutional, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for judicial review of appellee railroad commission's order.

 

1404 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Dallas/Fort Worth Int'l Airport Bd. v. City of Irving


No. 05-92-00559-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


854 S.W.2d 161; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1712



March 31, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 162nd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-4298-I



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants airport board, joint board of two cities, airlines, and delivery company sought review of a judgment from the 162nd District Court, Dallas County (Texas ), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee cities and holding that appellees' local ordinances were not preempted by federal or state law. In addition, the trial court held that appellants did not have the power of eminent domain over the host cities.


OVERVIEW: Appellants airport board, joint board of two cities and airlines sought review of the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee cities finding that their local ordinances were not preempted by federal and state law and that appellants did not have the power of eminent domain over them. The court affirmed the judgment. There was no express preemption in the federal legislation of any local control over construction and expansion of major public airports. In addition, the court held that the local law could not be preempted based on safety because safety was not a main concern in expanding the airport. Furthermore, the Federal Aviation Administration, in approving the project, plainly stated the local ordinances involved were not preempted. In addition, the local ordinances were not preempted by state rules because appellees were home rule cities and there was no legislation limiting appellees authority with regard to the airport expansion. Finally, appellants did not have the power of eminent domain over appellees host cities because appellees power of eminent domain was not preempted with unmistakable clarity in clear and compelling language.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that appellants failed to show that federal or state law preempted appellees' local ordinances. There was no implied or express language in the federal or state legislation preempting appellees' control over construction and expansion of major public airports. In addition, appellants lacked eminent domain over appellees because appellees' power of eminent domain as host cities was not preempted by legislation.

 

1405 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Otwell v. State


No. 2-91-341-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


850 S.W.2d 815; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 898



March 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 5 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Jake Cook



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trespasser challenged his conviction for criminal trespass, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (1989), by the County Criminal Court No. 5 of Tarrant County (Texas). Appellant alleges that the criminal trespass statute was unconstitutionally applied to him because he claimed that his activities were protected by U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Appellant trespasser belonged to a church group that fed homeless people at a building and a park owned by the City of Forth Worth, Texas. One Sunday the city leased the building and the park to a private for-profit group and the church group was informed that no other group could use the building on that Sunday. Appellant returned to the building on the day of the lease to protest the exclusive use of the park and the ignoring of the plight of the homeless. Appellant was arrested for criminal trespass, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (1989), and asserted that his rights under the U.S. Const. amend. I were violated. The court disagreed and held that the property was a nonpublic forum on the day of the lease because the private for-profit group's use did not embrace any indicia of a traditional public forum. As such, speech could be restricted as long as regulations were reasonable and did not attempt to suppress expression because of appellant's opposition to a speaker's views. The record showed that the trespass statute was applied without discrimination and not for the primary purpose of suppressing appellant's speech; thus it did not violate appellant's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant trespasser for criminal trespass. Appellant was denied relief because his freedom of speech rights under the federal constitution had not been violated.

 

1406 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Burgett


No. 2-92-322-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


850 S.W.2d 267; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 906



March 30, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 97TH DISTRICT COURT OF CLAY COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE HON. ROGER E. TOWERY



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we dismiss the appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal challenged the decision of the 97th District Court of Clay County (Texas) that denied his application, filed before trial, for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in denying the writ because it failed to adequately consider his U.S. Const. amend. VI speedy trial claim and that there was no or insufficient evidence to support its findings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal before his trial for delivery of a controlled substance filed a pro se application for a writ of habeas corpus that claimed he was denied his right to a speedy trial under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The trial court denied the motion and appellant argued that pre-trial habeas corpus relief was the only appropriate remedy to correct his violation of the speedy trial rule. The court agreed with appellee state that habeas corpus relief was not proper because appellant's adequate remedy at law was by a direct appeal from the denial of a pretrial motion to dismiss, after a trial on the merits. The court stated that a pretrial appeal was not necessary to correct the denial of the right to a speedy trial despite the prolonged delay suffered by appellant. An appellate court reviewing this type of claim was better able to assess the relevant facts after they have been developed in both a pretrial hearing and the trial itself. In light of that, the court dismissed the appeal, holding that the denial of the right to a speedy trial could not be challenged through a pre-trial writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal of the denial of a pre-trial writ of habeas corpus. Appellant criminal was denied relief because the court held that a pre-trial writ of habeas corpus was an inappropriate remedy for denial of appellant's right to a speedy trial.

 

1407 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Todd v. Planned Parenthood


No. 05-92-01113-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


853 S.W.2d 124; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1417



March 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 68th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-09293-C



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, estate representative and decedent's beneficiaries, sought review of the summary judgment awarded by the 68th Judicial District Court of Dallas County (Texas) in favor of appellee health care providers on the basis that appellants' medical negligence suit for wrongful death and survival damages was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, estate representative and decedent's beneficiaries, filed suit for wrongful death and survival damages alleging negligent medical care on the part of appellee health care providers in failing to diagnose, test, and treat the decedent's cervical cancer. The alleged torts by appellees took place about three years before suit was filed, while decedent's death occurred two years after the alleged torts and about eight months before suit was filed. The trial court awarded summary judgment to appellees on the basis that the suit was barred by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01. Appellants contended that the limitations period was rendered unconstitutional with regard to their case under Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, the open courts provision. The court held that the open court provision served to prevent the legislature from abrogating common-law causes of action only. Appellants sought to recover in wrongful death and survival actions, which were purely statutory. The open courts provision was inapplicable to statutory causes of action; therefore, appellants were bound by the absolute two-year limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment awarded by the trial court to appellee health care providers because the open courts provision was inapplicable to the purely statutory wrongful death and survival action brought by appellants, estate representative and decedent's beneficiaries; thus, suit was barred by a two-year statute of limitations.

 

1408 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Martin


No. 09-92-009 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


851 S.W.2d 905; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1181



March 25, 1993, Delivered  
March 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 221st District Court. Montgomery County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 91-12-04068 CV. Lee G. Alworth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor child, represented by next friend, sought review of the judgment from the 221st District Court. Montgomery County (Texas), which entered summary judgments in favor of appellees mother, father, and step-father of the minor child on appellant's claims of negligence and gross negligence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor child was injured when the motorcycle on which she was riding with another crashed. She was riding without a helmet and without permission of appellee mother. Through a next friend, appellant brought suit against appellees for negligence and gross negligence relating to appellant's riding a moped owned by appellees mother and step-father, and failing to provide a helmet for appellant to wear while riding the moped. The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of appellees. The court held that parental immunity prohibited the suit against appellees, and that appellant's cause of action did not fall into a recognized exception to the parental immunity doctrine. The court also held that the fact that appellee mother had insurance coverage was not admissible on the issue of her negligence, per Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 411 and Tex. R. Civ. P. 38(c), and the existence of such insurance did not vitiate the parental immunity doctrine. The court also held that appellant failed to demonstrate a breach of any duty owed to appellant, or that appellant's motorcycle accident was foreseeable by appellees, since none gave her permission to ride the motorcycle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment of the trial court in favor of appellees mother, father, and step-father. The court held that parental immunity bars appellant minor child's suit against appellees, because her cause of action did not fall into any recognized exception to the parental immunity doctrine. The court also found that appellees breached no duty to appellant, and appellees could not have foreseen the accident.

 

1409 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Marchal v. Webb


No. 01-92-00897-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 792



March 18, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
March 18, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn by the Order of the Court May 13, 1993. Substituted Opinion Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1377.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-019737. Mark Davidson, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the decision of the 11th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee physician on the basis that the statute of limitations barred the medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient brought a medical malpractice action against appellee physician. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed judgment in favor of appellee, because there was an absolute two-year statute of limitation on medical malpractice actions under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1993). The court held that appellant's injury occurred on the date of either of the two surgeries and that it was incorrect to apply the date of appellant's last visit to appellee as the trigger point for the statute of limitations. The court held that appellant failed to plead that the application of the statute of limitations to her would be unconstitutional. The court held that the open courts doctrine would not benefit appellant and that she could not prevail on the issue of fraudulent concealment because the letter she wrote to appellee showed she had knowledge of an injury.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee physician was affirmed because appellant patient's medical malpractice action was barred by the two year statute of limitations. The limitations period was triggered on the date of either of the two surgeries performed by appellant and not on the date of appellant's last visit to appellee.

 

1410 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. Vitek


NO. A14-92-00592-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


849 S.W.2d 882; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 695



March 11, 1993, Rendered  
March 11, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 152nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-28627.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and civil service commission, sought review of an order from the 152nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted a summary judgment in favor of appellee employee and reversed an order entered by appellant civil service commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellee employee filed grievances seeking back pay for performing functions of a position that paid more than the title he was given. A hearing examiner for appellant city conducted a hearing and concluded that appellee's grievance was fully justifiable. Appellee then requested appellant civil service commission (commission) to review the record. Appellant commission reviewed the record and remanded to the hearing examiner to determine if appellee had performed the work and that if he was performing the work longer than 90 days he was entitled to back pay. The hearing examiner answered that appellee did perform the work. Appellant commission subsequently filed a second ruling that denied appellee back pay. The district court reversed and granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held the first order issued by appellant commission was a final order that created a property right. The court found that the fact that the order was conditional did not fail to make it final. The court held the second order of appellant commission defied the finality of its earlier ruling and was entered improperly and without jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employee. The court held that an earlier order by appellant civil service commission was a final order that created a property right for appellee, and a second purported order issued by appellant civil service commission was improper because it attempted to divest appellee of his right to back pay.

 

1411 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Maloy v. Lewisville


No. 2-92-177-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


848 S.W.2d 380; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 620



February 26, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 211TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Sam Houston



DISPOSITION: The order of temporary injunction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owners of adult stores, challenged an order of the 211th District Court, Denton County, Texas, which restrained them from operating their businesses in violation of appellee city's ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, owners of adult stores, argued that a temporary restraining order issued to prevent them from operating their businesses violated the state's equal rights amendment, Tex. Const. art. I, § 3a. The court found that appellants did not argue in the lower court that appellee city's ordinance was unconstitutional. The court also found that the parties did not try that issue by consent; thus, the trial court did not err in failing to find the ordinance unconstitutional. The court also held that appellant's claim for a stay of the injunction pending review should have been granted, but the failure to grant the stay was not erroneous since it was not reasonably calculated to cause an improper judgment. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the injunction was not directed to speech, but toward compliance with a zoning ordinance which was content neutral.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the temporary injunction against appellants, owners of adult stores, because the trial court did not err in finding appellee city's ordinance unconstitutional.

 

1412 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Pharr v. Pena


NUMBER 13-91-356-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


853 S.W.2d 56; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 593



February 25, 1993, Delivered  
February 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 25, 1993. Rehearing Overruled May 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged a judgment from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which found in favor of plaintiff property owner in an inverse condemnation case and awarded damages against defendant city for an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation under Tex. Const. art. I, § 17 after defendant city denied plaintiff property owner's request for rezoning.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city notified plaintiff property owner that plaintiff could not build a junkyard on property that was subject to defendant's annexation powers. Plaintiff subsequently sought rezoning of the property in order to allow operation of a junkyard, which was denied, by defendant. Plaintiff filed an inverse condemnation action claiming that the denial of his zoning request was an unconstitutional taking of his property without adequate compensation pursuant to Tex. Const. art. I, § 17. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiff. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that plaintiff had not met the burden of proving that defendant's zoning ordinance was an unreasonable exercise of its police powers where defendant's decision was based upon aesthetic concerns and surrounding property values. The court also held that plaintiff also failed to prove that the junkyard was entitled to be treated as a pre-existing non-conforming use because the use was not lawfully existing at the time that the city first exercised its authority to annex the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of plaintiff property owner for an unconstitutional taking of property. The court held that plaintiff did not prove that defendant city's denial of plaintiff's zoning request for purposes of operating a junkyard was unreasonable and that plaintiff failed to prove a pre-existing non-conforming use of the property.

 

1413 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Berry Property Management v. Bliskey


No. 13-91-658-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


850 S.W.2d 644; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 627



February 25, 1993, Delivered  
February 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled March 36, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 214th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: As modified, we affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties sought review of the decision of the 214th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which entered the verdict of the jury in favor of appellee in her action alleging negligence and deceptive trade practices.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sued appellant and other owners and managers of her townhouse for negligence and deceptive trade practices. Most defendants settled leaving only appellant in the lawsuit, which alleged that appellant was negligent in handling its residents' keys and violated Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.43 (1987) by failing to provide door locks as required by statute and warranted by the lease appellee held. Appellee alleged that these acts caused her sexual assault and related injuries by an individual who used a key and information in the possession of appellant's management to enter her home. The jury found for appellee. Both sides filed timely post-verdict motions and the trial court entered judgment on the verdict awarding appellee compensatory and punitive damages. The trial court overruled appellant's motion for new trial by operation of law, and appellant challenged the judgment. Appellee also brought cross-points regarding the calculation of attorneys' fees. The court modified the judgment eliminating post-judgment interest on attorneys' fees but affirmed the remainder of the judgment, finding it was supported by the evidence and determined by a sufficient number of jurors.


OUTCOME: In appellee's suit against appellant, owner and manager of appellee's townhouse, for negligence, the court affirmed the judgment for appellee, finding that there was sufficient evidence to support the finding that appellant's negligence in handling keys led to appellee's assault. However, the court modified to judgment to reverse prejudgment interest awarded on attorney's fees.

 

1414 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Nesby


No. 3-92-116-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


848 S.W.2d 872; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 553



February 24, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE PROBATE COURT NO. 1 OF TRAVIS COUNTY. NO. 58,856, HONORABLE GUY HERMAN, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heir sought review of an order of the Probate Court No. 1, Travis County, Texas, which granted appellee claimant's bill of review to set aside a judgment that declared that appellant was sole heir of decedent and distributed to appellant all property belonging to decedent's estate. Appellee claimed to be the illegitimate child of decedent.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died intestate. Appellant heir, decedent's daughter, was declared sole heir and was granted all of decedent's property. Eight years later, appellee claimant filed a bill of review, claiming to be decedent's illegitimate child. The probate court ordered a new trial to determine whether appellee was decedent's heir. Appellant sought review of the probate court's order, arguing that the probate court erred in retroactively applying a statutory amendment after decedent's death, that the original judgment was voidable and not void, that appellee's claim was barred by the statute of limitations, and that the probate court failed to apply the proper standard for a bill of review. The court reversed the order of the probate court. The court stated that statutes that were in effect at the time of decedent's death were unconstitutional as applied to appellee. Because of this unconstitutionality, however, appellee was entitled to petition the court for a determination of heirship at the time of decedent's death. Since the statute of limitations was four years for contesting heirship, appellee's claim was barred since the claim was filed eight years after the original judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the probate court granting appellee claimant's bill of review. The court stated that the statutes in place at the time of decedent's death were unconstitutional as applied to appellee. However, because the statutes were unconstitutional, the statute of limitations began to run at the time that the original probate court entered its order. Appellee filed his bill four years after the limitations period had run.

 

1415 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


La Porte v. Prince


No. 10-92-076-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


851 S.W.2d 876; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 591



February 24, 1993, Delivered  
February 24, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 125th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court # 83-66592



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality sought review of a judgment by the 125th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which granted appellee former employee actual and exemplary damages in a wrongful termination case. Appellant claimed that that the trial court erred by not granting it a directed verdict on the defense of governmental immunity, by awarding exemplary damages, and that insufficient evidence existed for the submission of evidence to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellee former employee was injured on the job while in the employ of appellant municipality. Appellee pursued a workers' compensation claim against appellant, and appellee was subsequently fired. Appellee filed suit against appellant, claiming that under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8307c, he was wrongfully terminated. The jury found for appellee and awarded actual and exemplary damages. Appellant sought review, claiming that it was entitled to governmental immunity, and that the jury erred in awarding exemplary damages to appellee. Appellant also argued that the trial court wrongfully excluded evidence. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8309h a municipality was subject to the provisions of the Texas Workers' Compensation Act and therefore, appellant was not entitled to governmental immunity. The court further held that exemplary damages were properly awarded because appellant engaged in willful and malicious conduct toward appellee, and that remittitur of the exemplary damages was not warranted because appellant's damages were reasonably proportionate to the injury suffered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of judgment to appellee employee. The court held that the workers' compensation act allowed appellee to pursue a cause of action if he was fired for pursuing a workers' compensation claim, and that the workers' compensation act applied to appellant municipality and did not grant it governmental immunity. The court further held that exemplary damages were warranted because appellant acted willfully toward appellant.

 

1416 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Barnett v. Plainview


No. 07-92-0234-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


848 S.W.2d 334; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 540



February 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 64TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HALE COUNTY; NO. 88-01 A24004CV; HONORABLE JACK R. MILLER, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipal judge challenged the decision of the 64th Judicial District Court of Hale County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, municipality and its representatives, on his removal from office.


OVERVIEW: Appellant municipal judge was appointed to position by appellees, municipality and its representatives. Appellant was removed from office and he brought suit against appellees. The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed and found that appellant was not an employee at will because the charter provision stating the judge serve for a length of time decided by the council was limited by statute to a minimum of two years. Although removal was prior to the end of the two-year period, the court held that the charter and ordinances expressly gave appellees the power to appoint the judge, the objective of which was to establish the office and qualifications, and that incidental to that power was the implied power to remove the judge if his performance was unsatisfactory. The court found that a municipal judge of a home-rule city whose position was created by a city did not have the protections of judges of courts established by the constitution or created by the legislature; therefore, appellant was not entitled to a hearing with all the formalities required to remove district court judges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellees, municipality and its representatives, and upheld the removal of appellant municipal judge from office because the charter and ordinance gave appellees the power to appoint appellant to the position and to remove him if his performance was unsatisfactory.

Liggett v. Blocher


No. 01-92-00961-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


849 S.W.2d 846; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 485



February 18, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
February 18, 1993, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former patient sought review of the judgment of the 164th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which entered summary judgment for appellee physicians in appellant's action for medical malpractice on the ground that appellant's action was not timely filed under the statute of limitations set forth in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4509i, § 10.01 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant former patient was incarcerated for attempted murder after injuring a nurse while in the care of appellee physicians. Appellant filed a medical malpractice action against appellees. Appellees filed a motion for summary judgment, alleging that appellant's action was not timely filed under the statute of limitations set forth in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4509i, § 10.01 (1993). The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. Appellant argued that the limitations period should have been tolled, under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. § 16.001 (1986 & Supp. 1993), as appellant was of unsound mind and that, therefore, §10.01 was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that § 16.001, a general tolling statute, was not applicable to appellant's medical malpractice claim, as § 10.01 prohibited its application, and that § 10.01 was not unconstitutional, under Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, as there was nothing in appellant's affidavits in response to the summary judgment motion to create a fact issue on an impairment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial court did not err in granting summary judgment to appellee physicians in appellant former patient's medical malpractice action, as the statute of limitations set forth in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act was not tolled by appellant's alleged mental impairment, and the application of the statute of limitations was not unconstitutional, under the Texas Constitution.

Colson v. State


No. 07-92-0004-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


848 S.W.2d 328; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 486



February 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 12, 1993. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 137TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 90-410,803; HONORABLE CECIL G. PURYEAR, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the 137th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas) that convicted appellant of theft of property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the offense of theft of property. Appellant sought review of the judgment with seven points of error. Appellant attacked the sufficiency of the indictment arguing that the trial court erred in not quashing the indictment because it failed to allege that the property was appropriated "unlawfully" nor facts necessary to the same conclusion. The complaint arose because the state did not adhere to the accepted practice of following the statute to allege that appellant "unlawfully" appropriated the property. Within the indictment were allegations charging that property in the custody of a law enforcement agency was explicitly represented by a law enforcement agent to appellant as being stolen and he appropriated the property believing it was stolen by another. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The indictment imparted sufficient notice to appellant that the appropriation alleged was unlawful. Further, because appellant did not explain to the trial court, nor offer a reason on appeal, why the absence of "unlawful" from the indictment impacted his defense, it cannot be said that the claimed notice deficiency prejudiced his substantial rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of theft of property because the indictment was sufficient and appellant's other contentions were not met with favor by the reviewing court.

Bible Baptist Church v. Cleburne


No. 10-92-033-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


848 S.W.2d 826; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 491



February 17, 1993, Delivered  
February 17, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 249th District Court. Johnson County, Texas. Trial Court # 249-237-89.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of February 10, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 446.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church sought review of the order from the 249th District Court, Johnson County, Texas that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellant's nuisance action filed after its building flooded with raw sewage from a sewer line owned and operated by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant church sued appellee city after its building flooded with raw sewage from a sewer line owned and operated by appellee. The trial court granted summary judgment based on appellee's sovereign immunity. The court reversed. Although a municipality was generally immune from liability for its torts in the performance of governmental functions, it could be liable for the creation or maintenance of a nuisance in the course of the non-negligent performance of such functions. If the nuisance was caused by the negligent performance of a governmental function, the municipality was protected from liability because of governmental immunity. Appellant also asserted a cause of action under Tex. Const. art. I, § 17 for the taking, damaging or destruction of its property for public use. Because fact questions existed about what caused the backup, whether appellee intentionally or negligently failed to correct the cause of the backup, whether the condition rose to the level of a nuisance, and whether appellee intended to take acts which resulted in the taking, damaging, or destruction of any interest in the property, appellee was not entitled to summary judgment on this cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of summary judgment that was based on appellee city's sovereign immunity in appellant church's nuisance action. The court found that questions of fact existed as to whether the condition rose to the level of a nuisance, and whether appellee intended to take acts which resulted in the taking, damaging, or destruction of any interest in the property. The court remanded the action for trial.

 

1421 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Roberts v. State


NO. 2-92-086-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


849 S.W.2d 407; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 442



February 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended February 11, 1993. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. L. Clifford Davis



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 3 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of attempted murder, found that he exhibited a deadly weapon during the commission of the offense or immediate flight therefrom, and sentenced him to 15 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder. The jury affirmatively found that defendant used or exhibited a deadly weapon during the commission of the offense or during immediate flight therefrom and sentenced him to 15 years imprisonment. Pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1993), the jury charge was required to include a parole instruction because the judgment contained an affirmative finding of a deadly weapon. Although defendant did not object to the omission of a parole instruction from the charge, on appeal he cited it as error requiring a reversal. The court affirmed. The error was a charge error, not a statutory error. Where defendant did not object to the omission at trial, the appropriate standard on appellate review was whether the error was so egregious and created such harm as to deny defendant a fair and impartial trial. The omitted instruction was intended to benefit the prosecution by increasing the length of sentences, and its omission did not harm defendant. The facts supported the sentence defendant was given, and the error was not so egregious and did not create such harm that defendant was denied a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of attempted murder and sentencing him to 15 years imprisonment was affirmed. The error involved in the trial court's failure to give a parole instruction was not so egregious as to deprive defendant of a fair trial.

 

1422 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bible Baptist Church v. Cleburne


No. 10-92-033-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 446



February 10, 1993, Delivered  
February 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn February 17, 1993. Substituted Opinion of February 17, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 491.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 249th District Court. Johnson County, Texas. Trial Court # 249-237-89



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church challenged the decision of the 249th District Court, Johnson County (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellee City of Cleburne in appellant's action for damages to its building caused by the flooding of raw sewage from appellee's sewer line. The issue was whether summary judgment was properly granted for appellee on appellant's claims for nuisance and for an unconstitutional taking of its property.


OVERVIEW: The district court granted summary judgment for appellee City of Cleburne on appellant church's claims for nuisance and for an unconstitutional taking of its property due to a flooding of its building from appellee's sewer. On appeal, the court noted that, generally, a municipality was immune from liability for its torts in the performance of its governmental functions. Appellant argued that its claims for nuisance and for a taking under Tex. Const. art. I, § 17 fell within exceptions to the governmental immunity doctrine. The court held that appellee could be liable if the nuisance arose out of its non-negligent performance of its functions. The court indulged every reasonable inference and resolved all doubts as to the existence of a genuine issue of material fact in appellant's favor. The court held that, because fact questions existed as to what caused the sewer backup and whether it rose to the level of a nuisance, summary judgment was not proper. Proof of a non-negligent nuisance could provide a basis for recovery for an unconstitutional taking under Tex. Const. art. I, § 17. Summary judgment was not proper on that issue, either. The court reversed and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for trial. Appellee city could be held liable if the nuisance arose out of appellee's non-negligent performance of its functions. Proof of a non-negligent nuisance could provide a basis for appellant church to recover for an unconstitutional taking of its property. Because fact questions existed as to what caused the sewer backup and whether it rose to the level of a nuisance, summary judgment was not proper.

Dallas v. England


No. 3-92-243-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


846 S.W.2d 957; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 451



February 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 484,697, HONORABLE LAWRENCE L. FULLER, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and police chief, challenged a decision from the 200th Judicial District, Travis County (Texas), which found Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.06 (1989), criminalizing private, consensual relations between adults of the same sex, unconstitutional and enjoined appellant city's policy of not hiring lesbian and gay applicants. Appellee job applicant challenged the trial court's order finding that the state was immune from suit.


OVERVIEW: Appellee job applicant was denied a job as a police officer because she admitted to being a lesbian during a job interview. Appellee successfully challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.06 (1989), which criminalized consensual relations between adults of the same sex, and obtained an injunction against its enforcement. Appellants, city and police chief, sought review. Appellee challenged the finding that the state was immune from suit in her action. The court found, based on its decision in a 1969 case, that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 65.011 conferred on the district court jurisdiction to entertain a challenge to the constitutionality of the statute and to grant an injunction against its enforcement. The court also found that the state was immune from suit without its consent, but that a suit seeking relief from a government official's conduct was not one against the state. Finally, the court determined that appellant police chief's claim of qualified immunity was not before the court because that issue related to a claim for damages and not to a claim for injunctive relief. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all respects.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the trial court had jurisdiction to rule on the constitutionality of the statute criminalizing consensual relations between adults of the same sex, the injunction was appropriate because appellee job applicant satisfied the two equity requirements for injunctive relief, and, although suit could be brought against a state official, the state was immune from suit without its consent.

Saunders v. Titus County Fresh Water Supply Dist. No. 1


No. 6-91-111-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


847 S.W.2d 424; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 447



February 9, 1993, Decided  
February 9, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 276th Judicial District Court. Camp County, Texas. Trial Court No. 87-336.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of January 12, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 34.



DISPOSITION: The motion for rehearing is overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owner sought relief from the judgment of the 276th Judicial District Court of Camp County (Texas), granting title to a right-of-way to appellee water district, taken under its power of eminent domain, and denying appellant's motion for a new trial on the matter.


OVERVIEW: Appellee water district instituted eminent domain proceedings against appellant land owner to acquire a strip of property for a private road. The proceeding was undertaken after appellant refused to convey the right-of-way to appellee. The trial court entered a judgment in which appellee received a fee simple title to the land and appellant received payment. Appellant sought relief from the condemnation. On appeal, the court found that the district court had jurisdiction to review the substantive issues of the case once appellee determined that the taking was necessary to serve the public. This jurisdiction was not lost when the original reason for a condemnation changed as the case was never tried on the theory of a new purpose. The court found that the trial court erred in denying appellant's motion for a new trial as appellant had no power to condemn appellee's strip of property to create a private road, either expressly or by necessary implication, from the statutes defining its eminent domain power; any implication to the contrary arising from the statute would violate Tex. Const. art. I, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment condemning a strip of land across appellant land owner's property and set aside the condemnation of the land in question as no provision in any statute granting appellee water company's eminent domain authority permitted condemnation of property for any purpose other than public use.

Ex parte Luster


NO. 2-92-192-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


846 S.W.2d 928; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 347



January 28, 1993, Decided  
January 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 2, 1993. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 371ST DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. R. E. Thornton



DISPOSITION: The denial of the relief requested in Luster's application for writ of habeas corpus is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the pretrial denial by the 371st District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), of appellant's motion for writ of habeas corpus. In his challenge, appellant contended that the statutes, under which he was indicted for investing funds to further the commission of aggravated manufacture of a controlled substance, were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, indicted for investing funds to further the manufacture of a controlled substance, petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, which the trial court denied. Appellant sought review, arguing that the statutes under which he was charged were unconstitutionally vague because the word "further" was so broad and elastic that it made the same conduct criminal under several sections. The court affirmed the denial, finding that the statutes sufficiently identified the proscribed conduct so as to put appellant on notice of what was forbidden. In affirming, the court overruled appellant's argument that the law was vague because the same conduct would violate more than one provision, finding that different punishments authorized by more than one applicable statute did not detract from the notice of what conduct was proscribed. The court also overruled appellant's argument that he had no notice that financing the purchase of phenylacetic acid was unlawful because that chemical was not a controlled substance, finding that the chemical was a precursor of, and therefore included in the definition of, controlled substance in Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.103(3), (5).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's motion for writ of habeas corpus, finding that the statutes under which he was indicted were not unconstitutionally vague because the law sufficiently put him on notice that financing the purchase of phenylacetic acid, a controlled-substance precursor, was a proscribed act and the fact that other provisions authorized punishment for this act did not detract from the notice that it was forbidden.

Bexar County Appraisal Review Bd. v. First Baptist Church


Appeal No. 04-89-00543-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


846 S.W.2d 554; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 538



January 20, 1993, Delivered  
January 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 224th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 84-CI-20348. Honorable Carolyn H. Spears, Judge Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of October 10, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3155.



DISPOSITION: APPELLANTS' MOTION FOR REHEARING DENIED; JUDGMENT AFFIRMED AS REFORMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appraisal board sought review of the judgment entered in the 224th District Court, Bexar County (Texas) in favor of appellee church in a property tax exemption case, finding that appellees' parking lots were exempt from property taxes. The current court's finding that the evidence was legally insufficient was reversed and the case was remanded to the current court for consideration of points of error not reached.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appraisal board challenged the judgment that held that parking lots owned by appellee church and leased to a realty company were exempt from property tax. This court's original ruling that the evidence was legally insufficient was reversed and the case was remanded to consider other points of error. This court affirmed the judgment but deleted the attorney's fees award. A parking lot may qualify as a place of religious worship under the exemption provisions of Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. §§ 11.11 et seq. (1992). The exemption did not violate Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2 or U.S. Const. amend. I as it did not differentiate among religions and it extended the exemption to various other groups. It did not establish religion. Attorney's fees were not available under Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. § 42.29 as the suit was to establish an exemption and not to rectify an excessive appraisal. They were also not available under the declaratory judgment statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 37.009 (1989) because they were not otherwise authorized by statute. The evidentiary challenges were overruled as admissible under the state of the pleadings and the trial court's broad discretion.


OUTCOME: This court affirmed the judgment that awarded appellee church a property tax exemption for its parking lots because it did not violate the constitution and reversed the attorney's fees award as they were not permitted.

Moreno v. State


NO. 01-92-00715-CR; 01-92-01106-CR, NO. 01-92-00716-CR; 01-92-01108-CR, NO. 01-92-00717-CR; 01-92-01109-CR, NO. 01-92-00718-CR; 01-92-01107-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


845 S.W.2d 467; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 74



January 14, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
January 14, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 230th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 636274 and 646740, 636275 and 646739, 636276 and 646738, 636277 and 646741. Joe Kegans, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders denying Habeas Corpus Relief reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, indicted for drug-related offenses, sought review of orders of the 230th District, Harris County (Texas), in which that court refused to reduce bail pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.151. The trial court had previously refused to reduce bail pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.15.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were apprehended in the same raid and were indicted for drug-related offenses. Bail was set at $ 200,000 for one appellant and at $ 500,000 each for the remaining three appellants. After a hearing, the trial court denied all habeas corpus relief. Appellants perfected appeals, praying that the court set bail at $ 10,000 under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.15. Subsequently, the state failed to announce readiness to prosecute within 90 days of appellants' indictments, and second writs were filed requesting a personal bond or reducing the amount of bail required, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.151. The trial court again denied habeas corpus relief, and appellants filed second appeals. Upon consolidation of the appeals, the court noted that the state had admitted that it did not announce its readiness to prosecute within the required 90-day period under art. 17.151. Because the state failed to make its proof of a prima facie showing of readiness, art. 17.151 required that appellants be released either on personal bond, or that their bail be reduced to an amount they could afford to pay. The order below was reversed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying habeas corpus relief to appellants was reversed. The court found that the state failed to announce its readiness within the required 90-day period; as such, the applicable statute required that appellants be released either on personal bond or by reducing their bail to an amount they could afford to pay. Bail was ordered to be set in each case at $ 10,000.

Rogers v. State


No. 09-92-167 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


846 S.W.2d 883; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 476



January 13, 1993, Delivered  
January 13, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 252nd District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 60759. Marvin Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 252nd District Court, Jefferson County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated possession of a controlled substance and assessed an enhanced punishment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated possession of a controlled substance and was given an enhanced sentence of 35 years of confinement. On review sought by appellant, the court affirmed his conviction. The court held that appellant failed to prove that a sign reading "drug impact court," denoting the specialized docket, was an unconstitutional persuasion to convict. The court held that the state did not need to eliminate every reasonable hypothesis other than guilt to prove the mens rea of the offense. The court concluded that the state established that appellant intentionally or knowingly possessed the cocaine where the evidence showed that appellant was putting his belongings in a bag that also contained the cocaine. The court held that the impact court was a constitutionally permissible extension of the district courts. The court found that appellant failed to object to the fruits of the warrantless search of the athletic bag found near appellant, and thus waived any constitutional error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of aggravated possession of a controlled substance. The court held that appellant was tried in a court of competent jurisdiction, that he waived his objection to the admission of the fruits of a warrantless search, and that there was sufficient evidence to establish that he knowingly and intentionally possessed the cocaine.

Jackson v. Sharp


NO. 3-92-184-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


846 S.W.2d 144; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 39



January 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-11441, HONORABLE JAMES R. MEYERS, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax debtor sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Jarvis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), which granted the plea to the jurisdiction filed by appellee comptroller of public accounts for the state of Texas, and dismissed appellant's declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 159.001-159.206 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant tax debtor was arrested for possession of more than seven grams of a controlled substance. In response, appellee state comptroller froze appellant's bank accounts for failure to pay the taxes due for possession of a controlled substance, as required by the Controlled Substances Tax Act, Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 159.001-159.206 (1992) (Act). Appellant's suit challenged the constitutionality of the Act. Appellee filed a plea to the jurisdiction, citing Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 112.108, which prohibited declaratory judgments as to the constitutionality of a tax assessment absent strict compliance with tax code requirements. The trial court granted appellee's plea and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the order of dismissal, holding that § 112.108 allowed a taxpayer to assail the constitutionality of a tax assessment only upon strict compliance with the statutory requirements of the Tax Code. The Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act did not repeal the jurisdictional requirements of the Tax Code; and § 112.108 deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief to a taxpayer, such as appellant, who failed to comply with those jurisdictional requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order dismissing appellant tax debtor's declaratory judgment action, holding that The Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act (the Act) did not repeal jurisdictional requirements of the Texas tax code, and that the Act deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief to a taxpayer, such as appellant, who failed to comply with those jurisdictional requirements.

Saunders v. Titus County Fresh Water Supply Dist. No. 1


No. 6-91-111-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 34



January 12, 1993, Decided  
January 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn by Order of the Court February 9, 1993. Substituted Opinion of February 9, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 447. Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 276th Judicial District Court. Camp County, Texas. Trial Court No. 87-336



DISPOSITION: We reverse the judgment and set aside the condemnation of the strip of land in question.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged the judgment of the 276th Judicial District Court, Camp County (Texas), which allowed appellee water district to condemn a strip of her property for a roadway.


OVERVIEW: A third party brought an action against appellee water district for cutting off access to his property. Appellee instituted eminent domain proceedings, seeking a right-of-way across appellant owner's property. The trial court entered judgment that appellee received a fee simple title to the strip of land and that appellant received $ 3,840 for the value of the property taken. The trial court denied appellant's motion for a new trial and appellant sought review. The court found that the trial court had jurisdiction to determine, de novo, the authority to condemn, because appellee's governing board made a determination that the taking was necessary to serve the public, by settling the other owner's lawsuit. The court reversed and set aside the condemnation that was an unlawful taking for a private use. The court held that appellee had no statutory authority to condemn appellant's strip of property to create a private road in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and set aside the condemnation because appellee water district violated due process by its unlawful taking of appellant owner's land for a private use.

DeVautour v. Quintos


NO. B14-92-00176-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 14



January 7, 1993, rendered  
January 7, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 164th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-50394-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of an order of the 164th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, doctor and physician's association, on the basis that appellant's survival and wrongful death causes of action were barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife brought a survival claim and a wrongful death claim, asserting that husband's death was the result of medical malpractice. She did not name appellees, doctor or physicians' association, as parties to the action until more than two years had passed since her husband died. The court held that pursuant to the statute of limitations set forth in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1991), and Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(b) (1986), appellant had to bring her claim against appellees within two years after the husband's death. The court affirmed the awarding summary judgment to appellees because appellant did not name appellees as defendants within two years of her husband's death render her claims time barred. The court further held that appellant failed to establish that a fact issue existed regarding appellee doctor's fraudulent concealment. Appellant had a reasonable opportunity to discover all causes of action and bring suit before the expiration of the statutory period. The medical records clearly provided a reasonable opportunity to discover all asserted causes of action against appellees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment that the trial court awarded to appellees, doctor and physician's association, in appellant wife's claims for survival and wrongful death. Appellant was barred from recovering against appellees by the applicable two-year statutes of limitation and because she failed to establish that a fact issue existed regarding fraudulent concealment.

State Farm Fire & Casualty Co. v. Price


NO. 07-91-0245-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


845 S.W.2d 427; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3231



December 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled January 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 251ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF RANDALL COUNTY; NO. 33,071-C; HONORABLE PATRICK A. PIRTLE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed from the judgment of the 251st Judicial District Court of Randall County, Texas that decreed defendant monetarily liable to plaintiff insureds under a homeowners insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insureds' home experienced settling and cracking damage while their homeowner's insurance policy with defendant insurer was in force. Plaintiffs made a claim under the policy. Defendant denied the claim, because of an exclusion in the policy for settling damage not caused by plumbing leaks. Plaintiffs brought an action for breach of contract and claims under the Deceptive Trade Practices--Consumer Protection Act (DTPA), Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 1741 et seq., and Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21. The trial court found that defendant was monetarily liable to plaintiffs under the policy. The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that because defendant failed to timely object to the insufficient notice of the trial setting, it did not preserve the error for review. What caused the settling damage to plaintiffs' home was a jury question, and the jury was entitled to determine which expert witnesses it believed. The court concluded that the discretionary treble damages provision of the DTPA meant that the mandatory treble damage provision of Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21 a violation of due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court for plaintiff insureds, because the discretionary nature of the treble damage provision of the Deceptive Trade Practices--Consumer Protection Act meant that the Insurance Code's mandatory treble damage provision was not a violation of due process and equal protection. The jury was entitled to choose which witnesses' testimony it believed.

National Farmers Union Property & Casualty Co. v. Degollado


NO. 3-91-239-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


844 S.W.2d 892; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3178



December 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 17, 1993. Released for Publication February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BELL COUNTY, 169TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 117,659-C, HONORABLE STANTON B. PEMBERTON, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an insurance company and an attorney, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bell County, 169th Judicial District (Texas). The trial court awarded appellee worker total and permanent compensation benefits arising out of his workers' compensation claim against the insurance company for injuries suffered in the course of his employment. His attorney sought review of the portion of the judgment awarding attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee worker was employed as a day laborer and was injured when a 250-pound metal form fell on him. Appellee sustained severe injuries and underwent abdominal surgery. After numerous complications and additional hospital stays, appellee returned to work despite the fact that he was still weak from his injuries. He then suffered a stroke from which he never fully recovered. At the trial, the primary point of contention was whether the original injury caused appellee's total incapacity. Appellant insurance carrier argued that the stroke was the sole producing cause of disability. The jury agreed with appellee that the original injury was a producing cause of his total and permanent incapacity. In affirming the judgment, the court ruled that once appellee proved that the work-related injury was a producing cause of his incapacity, the insurance company was liable for the entire disability to which both the injury and the stroke contributed. The court also ruled that the trial judge was authorized to award attorney fees and to divide the fee between appellee's two attorneys.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court awarding appellee total and permanent compensation, on the ground that ample evidence supported a finding that appellee's incapacity was permanent in nature. The court also ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it apportioned the award of attorney fees between appellant attorney and the lawyer who succeeded him and actually tried the case.

Lopez v. State


NUMBER 13-91-479-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


846 S.W.2d 90; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3144



December 17, 1992, delivered  
December 17, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Motion for Rehearing January 28, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 332. Rehearing Overruled January 28, 1993. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Having carefully examined the record and all of appellant's claims we find no reversible error. The judgment of the trial court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a conviction from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Hidalgo County (Texas), which convicted her of barratry and assessed a $ 300 fine, court costs, and thirty days in jail, probated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged and convicted of barratry. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that the jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that potential client did not request any communication from appellant, nor did she designate someone to do so for her. The court held that Tex. Penal Code § 38.01(11) (1992) contained no statutory exceptions for the state to negate in the indictment. Appellant's plea to the indictment after the amended version was read was effective to join the issue. The court found that the evidence showed that appellant was offering the attorney's legal services to potential clients, thus showing indirectly that she too sought an economic benefit. The court concluded that appellant did not object to the relevancy of alleged hearsay testimony. The charge as given adequately protected appellant's right to have the jury determine whether or not potential client or someone acting on her behalf requested the communication. The barratry statute was not subject to an overbreadth claim because appellant failed to show that she was engaged in protected speech activity. The court held that the statute was not impermissibly vague as applied to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment convicting appellant of barratry because there was sufficient evidence to show beyond a reasonable doubt that potential client did not request any communication from appellant and she did not designate anyone to do so for her. The evidence showed that appellant offered these services for economic benefit.

Ellis County State Bank v. Keever


No. 05-91-02114-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


870 S.W.2d 63; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3327



December 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand May 24, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3060.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 44th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-5837-B



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, and Reversed and Rendered in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank and appellant bank associates challenged the judgment of the 44th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which was entered in favor of appellee debtor in appellee's malicious prosecution action against appellants.


OVERVIEW: Based on appellant bank associates' testimony, appellee debtor, who was in bankruptcy, was indicted for hindering a secured creditor. That indictment was later quashed. Appellee sued appellant bank and appellant bank associates for malicious prosecution. The jury awarded appellee actual and punitive damages. Appellants challenged the judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, and reversed in part. The evidence was sufficient to show that appellants acted without probable cause and with malice in instituting criminal proceedings against appellee, and that appellants presented false testimony to the grand jury. Appellee's doctor's testimony was sufficient to support the award of future medical expenses for appellee's post-traumatic stress disorder. The jury was properly instructed that all factual issues were to be determined by the preponderance of the evidence standard. The award of exemplary damages was supported by the evidence and was not the result of the jury's passion or prejudice. The award or prejudgment interest on future damages was authorized by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-1.05, § 6, but the award of prejudgment interest on punitive damages was improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and reversed in part the judgment entered in appellee debtor's favor in his malicious prosecution action against appellant bank and appellant bank associates. Sufficient evidence supported the jury's findings. Prejudgment interest on future damages was proper, but prejudgment interest could not be recovered for punitive damages.
