Ex parte Matthews


NO. 01-92-00447-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3001



December 3, 1992, rendered and delivered  
December 3, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn January 21, 1993. Substituted Opinion of January 21, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 96. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 594707. J. KYLES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed for want of jurisdiction


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged denial of her pre-trial application for writ of habeas corpus, from the 208th District Court, Harris County, Texas, arguing that her perjury prosecution was equitably estopped, that the statute tolling the limitations period was unconstitutional, and that the preindictment delay in the case violated both the U.S. Constitution's due process clause and the due course law of the Texas Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of denial of her pre-trial application for writ of habeas corpus, contending that her prosecution for perjury was barred by equitable estoppel, that the statute tolling the statute of limitations was unconstitutional, and that the preindictment delay in the case ran afoul of both the due process clause of the U.S. Constitution and the due course law guarantee of the Texas Constitution. On appeal, the lower court judgment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that denial of a pre-trial writ of habeas corpus could be appealed under certain circumstances, such as when the defendant was accused of violating a facially unconstitutional statute. With respect to the instant case, however, the perjury statute in question was facially valid. Accordingly, the court found that it did not have jurisdiction to review appellant's unconstitutional challenge to the indictment.


OUTCOME: Denial of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus was affirmed as the court determined that it did not have jurisdiction to hear appellant's challenge because the perjury statute under which appellant was indicted was not facially unconstitutional.

 

1439 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Waters ex rel. Walton v. Del-Ky, Inc.


No. 05-91-01064-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


844 S.W.2d 250; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3258



December 2, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 134th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F89-15293-G



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, decedent's surviving sister, sought review of an order of the 134th District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee nursing home in appellant's survivorship, deceptive trade practices, and breach of fiduciary duty claims against appellee following decedent's death from injuries sustained when falling out of appellee's second story window.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with appellee nursing home that the limitations period had expired when appellant, decedent's sister, brought her survivorship suit following her brother's fall from a window at the facility. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01, provided that no health care liability claim could be filed, regardless of the complainant's legal disability, unless initiated within two years of the tort; thus, appellant's or decedent's unsound mind could not toll the statute. And even though § 10.01 did not abolish fraudulent concealment as a basis for extending limitations, appellant failed to show appellee's intention to conceal the injury, given that she was timely advised of the incident. Thus, no factual issue for summary judgment purposes was raised. And because appellant still had 22 months after discovering the injuries to sue, § 10.01 did not unconstitutionally deprive her of access to the courts. Further, § 12.01(a) barred express warranty causes of action based on the care appellee was to provide. And because appellant's breach of fiduciary duty claim was a recast health care liability claim, the expired limitations period also applied to that claim.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed granting summary judgment to appellee nursing home in survivorship, express warranty, and breach of fiduciary duty claims by appellant, decedent's surviving sister, following his death from window fall, as appellant's or decedent's unsound mind, appellee's alleged fraudulent concealment, or open courts doctrine did not toll limitations period, and as warranty and breach of fiduciary duty causes of action were also time-barred.

Criswell v. Ginsberg & Foreman


No. 05-91-01078-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


843 S.W.2d 304; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3260



December 2, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 160th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 82-14622-H



DISPOSITION: Reverse and Render


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 160th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), that required him to turnover his cause of action against appellee to the appellee in partial satisfaction of a judgment, arguing that application of the turnover statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 31.002, was unconstitutional in depriving him of property without due process.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered appellant to turn over a cause of action asserted against appellee to the appellee in partial satisfaction of a judgment that appellee held against appellant. Appellant challenged the trial court's turnover order, arguing that application of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 31.002 was unconstitutional as applied to him under these circumstances. In setting aside the trial court's turnover order and rendering a judgment that appellee take nothing, the appellate court concluded that appellant had a cognizable common law cause of action against appellee and that appellee's reliance upon the turnover statute resulted in its being able to extinguish the cause of action against itself. By requiring appellant, as a judgment debtor, to turn over his cause of action against appellee to the appellee, the judgment creditor, appellee became the holder of a cause of action against itself, and appellant was effectively deprived of his right to seek adjudication of his cause of action without receiving any value in return for it.


OUTCOME: The trial court's turnover order was set aside and a judgment was rendered that appellee take nothing. By ordering appellant to turn over to appellee the cause of action that appellant had against appellee allowed appellee to extinguish the cause of action and constituted the deprivation of appellant's property right without due process of law.

Brooks County Cent. Appraisal Dist. v. Tipperary Energy Corp.


Appeal No. 04-92-00136-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


847 S.W.2d 592; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3287



November 30, 1992, Delivered  
November 30, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 79th Judicial District Court of Brooks County. Trial Court No. 4,572. Honorable Walter Dunham, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxing entities challenged the judgment of the 79th Judicial District Court of Brooks County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayers in their action seeking a refund of taxes for the years 1985 through 1987 on the grounds that appellees paid taxes for the same piece of property for the same years. Appellants also challenged the denial of their motion for summary judgment by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of trial court granting summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayers. Appellees moved for summary judgment claiming that they were entitled to a refund because they erroneously paid taxes on another's behalf as a result of an honest mistake. Appellant taxing entities did not dispute the fact that appellees erroneously paid taxes for the same piece of property, but based their motion for summary judgment on other grounds, which the court rejected. The court held that a payment made without knowledge of all relevant facts was not voluntary. The court also held that appellees were not required to file a "protest" under Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 41.01-41.70, 42.01-42.43 (1992) to exhaust their administrative remedies. Further, the evidence demonstrated that appellees applied for a tax refund, thus complying with Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 25.25(c) (1992). Moreover, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 31.31 (1992) authorized a mechanism for obtaining a refund even if the payment made by the taxpayer matched the amount shown as "due" on the bill. Finally, the court held that appellants' estoppel by rendition argument was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting summary judgment on behalf of appellee taxpayers and denying appellant taxing entities' cross motion for summary judgment. Appellants did not dispute the fact that appellees erroneously paid taxes for the same piece of property for the same years, and the court rejected the other grounds upon which appellants based their refusal to refund the excess taxes.

Toungate v. Bastrop Indep. Sch. Dist.

November 25, 1992, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision from the District Court of Bastrop County, 21st Judicial District (Texas), which rendered summary judgment against appellant in an action alleging intentional infliction of emotional distress and challenging the constitutionality of appellee school district's hair length rule.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's son, a student in appellee school district, had a ponytail in violation of the school's hair length rule. As punishment, the student was placed in a separate classroom, isolated from the student body, and taught by a substitute teacher. Appellant filed an action against appellee for violation of the Equal Rights Amendment (ERA), Tex. Const. art. I, § 3a, and for intentional infliction of emotional distress. She sought an injunction, a declaratory judgment, and damages. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment on appellant's claims for actual and exemplary damages because sovereign immunity barred those claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted in favor of appellee school district in part, finding that that appellant mother's exemplary damages claim was barred by sovereign immunity. The court reversed in part, finding that appellant's constitutional and statutory claims required a factfinder's assessment of the evidence.

Bowie v. State


No. 09-91-152 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


841 S.W.2d 963; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3190



November 25, 1992, delivered  
November 25, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law #2. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 153272. Harold Plessala, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the County Court at Law #2, Jefferson County, Texas, which convicted him of the misdemeanor offense of disorderly conduct for noise. Appellant claimed that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.01(a)(5)(1992) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court, which convicted appellant criminal defendant of the misdemeanor offense of disorderly conduct for noise because it found that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.01(a)(5)(1992) was not vague. The court examined appellant's argument that the words "makes unreasonable noise" were overly vague. The court found that the word "unreasonable" was widely used and well understood. Therefore the court determined that the statute clearly and precisely delineated its reach. Furthermore, the court found that pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.04 (1989) the police properly warned appellant that she would be arrested for her loud and disturbing communication if she did not cease the disturbance. Appellant was arrested after she was warned; thus, the court held that she had fair notice of the proscribed conduct. The court held that § 42.01(a)(5) was not unconstitutional because it was not vague and when read in conjunction with § 42.04 it did not encourage arbitrary and erratic arrests and convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that convicted appellant for the misdemeanor offense of disorderly conduct for noise. The court held that the disorderly conduct statute was constitutional because it was not vague.

San Antonio v. San Antonio Park Rangers Ass'n


Appeal No. 04-91-00531-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


850 S.W.2d 189; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3305



November 25, 1992, Delivered  
November 25, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 225th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 91-CI-07944. Honorable Carleton B. Spears, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: CAUSE REVERSED; WRIT OF MANDAMUS DISSOLVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a writ of mandamus issued by the 225th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which held that defendant was required to bargain collectively with plaintiff, the San Antonio Park Rangers Association, because park rangers were, as a matter of law, policemen who were entitled to collective bargaining pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5154c-1, § 5(a) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the San Antonio Park Rangers Association, filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel defendant city to bargain collectively with its park rangers. Pursuant to Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 5154c-1, § 5(a), policemen were granted the right to organize and bargain collectively with their public employers upon adoption by a city. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5154c-1, § 3(2) (1987) defined "policeman" as a sworn, certified full-time paid employee, whether male or female, who regularly served in a professional law enforcement capacity in the police department of any city, town or other political subdivision within the state. The trial court found that park rangers were policemen who were entitled to collective bargaining with defendant under the statute and ordered defendant to bargain collectively with its park rangers. The court reversed the trial court's finding and dissolved the writ of mandamus. The court reviewed the statutory language and the legislative intent of the statute and ruled that the term "policemen" in the statute excluded the San Antonio Park Rangers Department and that the park rangers had no collective bargaining rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's writ of mandamus that compelled defendant city to bargain collectively with plaintiff, the San Antonio Park Rangers Association. The court ruled that park rangers were not policemen under the definition of the applicable statute and that they were not entitled to collective bargaining with defendant.

Trapnell v. Sysco Food Servs.


NUMBER 13-91-367-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


850 S.W.2d 529; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2948; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,485



November 17, 1992, delivered  
November 17, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Motion for Rehearing February 25, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 629. Rehearing Overruled April 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 94th District Court of Nueces County, Texas. (Tr.Ct.No. 86-3057-C)



DISPOSITION: We sustain that portion of the trial court's summary judgment holding that limitations bars suit by Benjamin Trapnell and Polly Ann Haugh against Univar, Van Waters, and McKesson. Accordingly, appellants' sixth point of error, which complains that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment against these parties is overruled in part. Summary judgment was improperly granted against all other defendants because collateral estoppel does not apply, and there is a question of fact regarding whether each of the three foods present on Susan Trapnell's plate are suspected of containing sulfites actually caused or contributed in causing her death. Points of error one through five are sustained. Judgment is accordingly REVERSED in all respects against all defendants except Univar, Van Waters, and McKesson; judgment is AFFIRMED for these three defendants with respect to their defenses against the adult plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband, child, and mother of the deceased, sought review of the judgment of the 94th District Court, Nueces County (Texas), which awarded summary judgment in favor of appellees, manufacturers and distributors, in a products liability death action.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, husband, child, and mother of the deceased, brought wrongful death and loss of consortium actions against appellees, manufactures and distributors, after deceased died as result of ingesting several food products containing sulfites. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, holding that each food product did not cause the injury and that collateral estoppel, the government contractor defense, and limitations applied. On review, the court reversed the summary judgments, except those based on limitations. The court found that: collateral estoppel did not apply, because the issue of whether sulfites were present was not, inter alia, fully and fairly litigated and because preclusion would have violated appellants' right to a jury trial; a question of fact existed regarding the comparative causation of each food product; the government contractor defense was not proven, because summary judgment evidence did not include evidence supporting any of the elements of that defense; and the statute of limitations was a bar to appellants, husband and mother's causes of actions for wrongful death and loss of consortium but not for appellant child's.


OUTCOME: The court reversed all the summary judgments in favor of appellees, manufacturers and distributors, against appellants, husband, child, and mother of the deceased's, causes of action for wrongful death and loss of consortium, and affirmed in part the judgments based on the statute of limitations. The court ruled that there was an issue of fact regarding causation and that collateral estoppel and the government contractor defense did not apply.

State v. Sandoval


NUMBERS 13-91-505-CR, 13-91-521-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


842 S.W.2d 782; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2950



November 17, 1992, delivered  
November 17, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled December 17, 1992. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court at Law No. 1 of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: As the charging instruments fail to adequately describe the manner of procurement, the orders of the trial court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the County Court at Law No. 1 of Hidalgo County (Texas) that granted defendant attorney's motion to dismiss two charges of barratry, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.12(a) (1989), upon an indictment and information that alleged defendant had procured another to solicit for him certain employment to prosecute suits and collect claims.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attorney was charged by indictment and information with two counts of barratry, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.12(a) (1989), for allegedly procuring another person to solicit for him certain employment to prosecute personal injury suits and collect claims. Defendant moved to dismiss on several grounds. Without specifying the grounds therefor, the trial court granted the motion and dismissed the charges. The state appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that the charging instruments were defective in that they failed to allege with sufficient definiteness the manner and means that defendant procured another to solicit employment. At the same time, the court also ruled that § 38.12 was not overbroad and the term "procure" was not vague. The statute did not infringe upon free speech rights and did not contain an unconstitutional mandatory presumption with respect to intent because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 2.05 made all presumptions permissive. The charging instruments sufficiently alleged the requisite intent to obtain economic benefit and they were not required to identify by name the persons solicited, since procurement was the forbidden act, not solicitation.


OUTCOME: The dismissal order was affirmed because the charging instruments failed to allege with sufficient definiteness the manner and means of procurement; however, the statute did not violate defendant's free speech rights or contain an invalid mandatory presumption, the term "procure" was not unconstitutionally vague, the charging instruments adequately alleged intent, and identification of the persons solicited was not required.

Cannon v. Lemon


NO. B14-91-01061-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


843 S.W.2d 178; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2875



November 12, 1992, Rendered  
November 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 212th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89CV0761.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix sought review of an order of the 212th District Court, Galveston County (Texas), that granted the motions to dismiss of appellee landlord, appellee manager, and appellee management company, as well as appellee manager's motion for summary judgment, in appellant's survivor action that in part alleged violations of Tex. Prop. Code Ann. §§ 92.255 to 92.256.

Armstrong v. State


NO. C14-91-00822-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2878



November 12, 1992, Rendered  
November 12, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 122nd District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89CR0344.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction, which was entered, following a jury trial, by the 122nd District Court of Galveston County (Texas) for the felony of theft by receiving stolen property.


OVERVIEW: At appellant's first trial for the felony offense of theft by receiving stolen property, a mistrial was declared due to manifest necessity when the lower court discovered appellant's counsel had been disbarred. At his second trial, the jury found appellant guilty. Appellant sought review and was allowed to proceed pro se. Appellant alleged numerous points of error. Appellant alleged the state failed to prove venue, but the court found that appellant had waived the point of error because, at the punishment stage, appellant admitted he was guilty. Appellant contended that he was denied counsel of choice at his second trial. However, appellant was not entitled to be represented by counsel who had been disbarred. The lower court did not abuse its discretion by granting a mistrial due to manifest necessity then it learned that appellant's counsel had been disbarred. Thus, jeopardy had not attached at appellant's first trial and his retrial was not barred by double jeopardy. Appellant's allegation that the state violated Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.01 was without merit. Appellant's second indictment was proper and appellant was not charged with a new crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for theft by receiving stolen property after ruling that appellant waived his challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, appellant was not entitled to have a disbarred attorney as counsel, and double jeopardy did not bar appellant's second trial.

Goins v. State


NO. 01-91-00788-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


841 S.W.2d 527; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2898



November 12, 1992, rendered and delivered  
November 12, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 595,456. CURT STELB, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to the offense of fleeing and was sentenced and fined. He was subsequently indicted as an habitual offender for the offense of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle (UUMV). Both charges arose out of the same events. Appellant's first prosecution for UUMV ended in mistrial. At the second trial, a jury found appellant guilty, found enhancement paragraphs to be true, and assessed punishment at life imprisonment. Appellant challenged the judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court was not required to submit appellant's special plea of double jeopardy to the jury as no evidence supported the plea. Double jeopardy did not bar appellant's prosecution for the offense of UUMV because fleeing and UUMV were not the same offense under the Blockburger test. The State's indictment did not rely on appellant's conduct of fleeing to establish an essential element of UUMV. Due to his failure to make a timely objection, appellant waived his right to challenge the wording of second enhancement paragraph. Appellant's right to a speedy trial was not violated, and he could not rely on Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02, which had been declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle (UUMV) and his sentence of life imprisonment. Double jeopardy was not a bar to appellant's prosecution for the offense of UUMV, appellant waived his right to challenged the wording of the second enhancement paragraph, and appellant's right to a speedy trial were not violated.

Najera v. State


NO. A14-91-01093-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2860



November 5, 1992, rendered  
November 5, 1992, filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 573,320



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a conviction for murder from the 262nd District Court of Harris County (Texas). Defendant raised several errors, including an error by the trial court that submitted an instruction to the jury on parole that exceeded the authority given to the legislature in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4 (1992) under the state constitution as amended, pursuant to Tex. Const. art. IV § 11(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to the murder of a baby left in his care. He shook, beat, and struck the crying baby. He made the confession after his rights had been read to him and after choosing not to exercise his right to have an attorney or to terminate the police questioning. A jury found him guilty of murder. Defendant raised several errors, including that the trial court erred in submitting an instruction to the jury on parole, arguing that it exceeded the authority given to the legislature under the state constitution. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that an instruction, which tracked the language of the parole statute did not exceed the scope of the authority granted by a constitutional amendment. The amendment provided that the legislature should have authority to enact parole laws and laws that required or permitted courts to inform juries about the effect of good conduct time and eligibility for parole and mandatory supervision on the period of incarceration served by a defendant convicted of a criminal offense. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4 (1992) and Tex. Const. art. IV § 11(a) (1989).


OUTCOME: A conviction for murder was affirmed because an instruction to the jury that tracked the language of the parole statute did not exceed the scope of the authority granted to the legislature by a constitutional amendment.

Henderson v. Wietzikoski


No. 10-91-173-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


841 S.W.2d 101; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2802



October 30, 1992, delivered  
October 30, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 77th District Court. Limestone County, Texas. Trial Court # T-114-A



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, alleged biological father, sought to reverse an order of the 77th District Court, Limestone County, Texas, and to assert his claim of paternity and his request to be conservator for his alleged child whose father was presumed to be the husband of appellee, the biological mother.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the alleged biological father of a child who had a statutory "presumed father," the husband of appellee biological mother, sought to maintain a suit to establish his paternity. The trial court held that appellant had no standing. On appeal, the court held that Tex. Fam. The court held that the Texas Equal Rights Amendment was more extensive and provided more specific protection than both the United States and Texas due-process and equal-protection guarantees. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for a trial on the merits of the suit to establish paternity alleged by appellant, the alleged biological father of a child who had a statutory "presumed father," the husband of appellee biological mother.

Eaglin v. State


NO. C14-92-00105-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


843 S.W.2d 153; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2777



October 29, 1992, rendered  
October 29, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 20, 1993.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 01/20/1993
Subsequent civil proceeding at Eaglin v. Baggett, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33998 (S.D. Tex., Sept. 9, 2005)
Writ of mandamus filed, Reserved by In re Eaglin, 2014 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 23 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 15, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 579299. Michael McSpadden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 209th District Court, Harris County, Texas that convicted him of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 after he entered a plea of nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a plea of nolo contendere to a charge of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 after the trial court denied his motion to suppress identification and motion in limine on extraneous offense. In the judgment outlining the terms of appellant's plea, the trial court noted that there was no agreed recommendation as to appellant's punishment. A judgment of conviction was entered, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed. Under Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1), appellant waived all nonjurisdictional defects, including claimed deprivations of federal due process, by knowingly and understandably entering a plea. This rule, known as the Helms rule, did not apply only if there was a negotiated recommendation as to punishment and the punishment actually assessed exceeded the recommendation. Absent an agreed recommendation as to punishment, the Helms rule applied, and appellant waived all points of error raising nonjurisdictional defects.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction, upon his plea of nolo contendere, for burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault was affirmed. Appellant waived his right to challenge any nonjurisdictional defects, including claimed deprivations of federal due process, by knowingly and understandably entering his plea.

Fuller v. Maxus Energy Corp.


No. 10-91-239-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


841 S.W.2d 881; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2714



October 21, 1992, delivered  
October 21, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 74th District Court. McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 90-825-3



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of child that was killed in an auto accident, challenged an order of the 74th District Court of McLennan County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, store owners and manager, in appellants' dram shop wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, store owners and store manager, sold a quart of beer to an 18-year old who later was involved in an accident. Appellant parents' son was killed in the accident, and they filed a wrongful death dram shop action against appellees on the basis that appellees were negligent in selling alcohol to a minor. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees, and appellants sought review. The court held that Chapter 2 of the Alcoholic Beverage Code provided the exclusive cause of action for providing an alcoholic beverage to a person 18 years of age or older and that liability could only be imposed upon appellees if it was shown that at the time of the sale it was apparent to appellees that the individual being sold the alcoholic beverage was obviously intoxicated to the extent that he presented a clear danger to himself and others, and the intoxication of the recipient of the alcoholic beverage was the proximate cause of the damages suffered. Because appellants failed to present an issue of fact regarding either of these elements, appellees were properly granted summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment to appellees, store owners and manager, on the basis that there was no genuine issue of fact as to at least one element of each of the causes of action filed by appellants, parents of child that was killed in an auto accident.

Houston v. Anderson


NO. 01-91-00137-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


841 S.W.2d 449; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2571



October 1, 1992, rendered and delivered  
October 1, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 164th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 85-25574. E.W. Patterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the 164th District Court, Harris County (Texas), reversing the civil service commission's suspension of appellee police officers from appellant city's police department for using excessive force in handling a suspect in custody.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the trial court reversing the civil service commission's (commission) order that affirmed the suspension of appellee police officers from appellant city's police department. The court reversed and held that there was substantial evidence to support the suspension and the commission's order should have been affirmed. The court held that appellant timely perfected its appeal by filing it within 10 days after the commission's final decision and requesting that the decision be set aside. The trial court erred in setting aside the commission's order merely because the testimony was conflicting or disputed. The trial court was only required to review the reasonableness of the administrative order, not its correctness. The trial court also erred in ruling that the commission's order was void because it stated that the officer was indefinitely suspended as opposed to permanently dismissed. In addition, the trial court erred in holding that the pretermination and suspension proceedings violated appellees' due process rights because appellees had notice of the charges and opportunity to respond and cross-examine the witnesses against them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held there was substantial evidence to support the civil service commission's order and the trial court erred in reversing the order based on conflicting or disputed testimony. In addition, the commission's order was not void based on its statement that the appellees were indefinitely suspended as opposed to permanently dismissed. Finally, the trial court erred in holding that appellee' due process rights were violated.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 140TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 91-412,925; HONORABLE WILLIAM R. SHAVER, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, indicted with the offense of possession of a counterfeit Texas driver's license, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 44A (1992), sought review of a decision from the 140th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for possession of a counterfeit Texas driver's license, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 44A (1992). His petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied. He sought review, contending that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 44A and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 32A, which also pertained to counterfeit driver's licenses, were in conflict, that he had a constitutional right to be prosecuted under the statute with the lesser penalty, that Tex. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, finding that the rule of in para materia did not apply because the two statutes alleged by appellant to be in conflict had different purposes or objectives.

State v. Taylor

September 24, 1992, filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Motion for Leave to File Petition for Writ of Mandamus granted, Writ of Mandamus conditionally granted in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an extradition matter, relator state sought a writ of mandamus and a writ of prohibition after a decision from the District Court of Galveston County, Texas, which granted habeas corpus relief to the real party in interest.


OVERVIEW: The real party in interest failed to pay child support and Wisconsin requested extradition. The real party in interest filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, and the trial court granted the writ. The relator state then filed a petition for a writ of mandamus or a writ of prohibition to compel the respondent trial court to dissolve the writ of habeas corpus. The court granted the writ of mandamus in part. It found that relator showed that there was no other adequate remedy available, and that the act sought to be compelled is a ministerial act. It further found that the trial court abused its discretion when it granted habeas corpus relief to the real party in interest because in an extradition request, the trial court was limited to determination of whether the extradition documents on their face were in order; whether petitioner had been charged with a crime in the demanding state; whether petitioner was the person named in the request for extradition; and whether petitioner was a fugitive.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus in part because the relator showed that there was no other adequate remedy and because the trial court abused its discretion when it granted habeas corpus relief to the real party in interest.

R Communications v. Sharp


NO. 3-91-390-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


839 S.W.2d 947; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2533



September 23, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-4893, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING

Original Opinion of August 26, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2290.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the 345th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which dismissed its action for want of jurisdiction against appellee state comptroller who assessed a sales tax deficiency.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state comptroller assessed a sales tax deficiency against appellant corporation. Appellant challenged the decision without first paying the tax allegedly owed. The trial court dismissed the action for want of jurisdiction. The court affirmed the decision and held that the Administrative Procedure and Texas Register Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 19 (1992), did not confer a direct right of appeal to taxpayers because the law did not repeal the jurisdictional requirements of the tax code, which required payment of the tax. The court held that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 112.051 did not violate appellant's due process rights or equal protection rights under the federal constitution. The court held that the right to challenge taxing authorities derives from statute and was not a common law cause of action, and thus, failure to pay the tax before appealing did not offend the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court held that the restrictions placed on equitable relief or declaratory judgments did not offend due process or equal protection provisions because no cause of action existed at common law to challenge the collection of tax revenues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that dismissed the cause because of a lack of jurisdiction and held that the trial court did not have jurisdiction because the Administrative Procedure and Texas Register Act did not provide a direct right to appeal a tax matter without first paying the tax before bringing a legal challenge.

Dalon v. Desoto


No. 05-91-01548-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


852 S.W.2d 530; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3309



September 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by, 04/21/1993


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 116th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-14681-F



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a grant of summary judgment from the 116th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), against them and in favor of appellee city in an action arising from alleged water erosion of appellants' property. Appellants alleged negligence, inverse condemnation, and violations of the Texas Water Code resulting in damage to and loss of their real property.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment against appellant property owners and in favor of appellee city in an action arising from alleged water erosion of appellants' property. On appeal, appellants contended that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment against them on their claim of negligence. The court found that appellants' property damage claim was governed by the two-year statute of limitations pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(a) (1986). Appellants first experienced and discovered water erosion in 1986, but did not file suit until December 13, 1990, well outside of the limitations period. Appellants' appearance before the city council did not constitute actual notice under the Texas Tort Claims Act. Because appellants failed to meet the notice-of-claim requirements under both the city charter and the Texas Tort Claims Act, their claims were barred as a matter of law. The maintenance of the storm sewer of which appellants complained was a governmental function. Consequently, appellee was not liable for alleged negligence because the claim did not arise under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.021 (1986). The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment below against appellant property owners and in favor of appellee city, on the grounds that appellants' negligence claim was barred by the statute of limitations. Appellants failed to meet the notice-of-claim requirements under both the city charter and the Texas Tort Claims Act, thus their claims were barred as a matter of law. Appellee also had governmental immunity against appellants' claim.

 

1462 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tanner v. State


No. 08-91-00248-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


838 S.W.2d 302; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2357



September 2, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 56th District Court of Galveston County, Texas (TC# 89CR1631). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Allen Stilley



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 56th Court of Galveston County, Texas, that convicted appellant, under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126 (1992), for the offense of illegal investment to further the offense of aggravated possession of cocaine. Appellant contended that the statute was void for vagueness and for overbreadth.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested after he arranged for and purchased $ 6,000 worth of cocaine from undercover officers. Appellant was convicted under Tex. Health & Safety Code § 481.126 (1992), which made it illegal for a person to expend funds, finance, or invest in certain controlled substances transactions. Appellant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and conviction and held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that persons of ordinary intelligence could readily understand the terms "funds," "invests," and "finance," so that one could determine with reasonable precision what specific conduct was prohibited. The court held that the statute also gave sufficient notice to law enforcement personnel so as to prevent arbitrary enforcement. The court held that the statute was not facially overbroad as there was nothing to show that it penalized speech or conduct which was protected by U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment and conviction of appellant for illegal investment to further the offense of aggravated possession of cocaine, and held that the statute which set forth the offense could be readily understood and was not unconstitutionally vague. The statute also did not prohibit constitutionally protected activity and was therefore not overly broad.

Powell v. State


NO. 01-91-00325-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


837 S.W.2d 809; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2284



August 26, 1992, rendered and delivered  
August 26, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 20,080. Robert May, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery with two enhancement paragraphs. Appellant argued that an out-of-court identification was overly suggestive, that the state used peremptory challenges to eliminate minority jurors, and that appellant should have been granted a directed verdict on the enhancement paragraphs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of his conviction in the lower court for aggravated robbery with enhancements. The evidence showed appellant had pointed a gun at a man, taken his checkbook, and then fled. Appellant was apprehended, and the man was taken to identify him at a single showup. The court examined whether the single showup was unnecessarily suggestive and conducive to irreparable misidentification. The court found that the witness' opportunity to view appellant at the time of the offense, the degree of attention, accuracy of prior description, level of certainty, and length of time between the offense and confrontation were sufficient that the identification did not result in irreparable misidentification. The court held that although the state's use of peremptory challenges did present a prima facie case of discrimination, the lower court's denial of appellant's Batson motion was not clearly erroneous because the state offered explanations for its challenges. The court found that the lower court properly limited the jury's consideration of enhancement paragraphs to those containing the date of the offense. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because the single showup identification was not unnecessarily suggestive and was not conducive to irreparable misidentification, the state's peremptory challenges of minority jurors were explained, and the jury's consideration of enhancement paragraphs was appropriately limited.

North Alamo Water Supply Corp. v. Texas Dep't of Health


NO. 3-91-534-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


839 S.W.2d 455; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2285



August 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 7, 1992. Released for Publication October 7, 1992.
Writ denied by, 01/20/1993
Related proceeding at BFI Waste Sys. v. North Alamo Water Supply Corp., 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 1282 (Tex. App. Corpus Christi, Feb. 24, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 454,715-A, HONORABLE JOE DIBRELL, JUDGE PRESIDING
North Alamo Water Supply Corp. v. Texas Dep't of Health, 839 S.W.2d 448, 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2566 (Tex. App. Austin, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In action under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.001-011 (1986 & 1992), appellant water supply corporation contested a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed its action against appellees, health department and solid-waste disposal operator, in which appellant claimed appellee department amended a permit without a public hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant water supply corporation sought review of the lower court's dismissal of its cause of action against appellees, Texas Department of Health and a solid-waste disposal operator, claiming appellee department amended a permit without a public hearing. The lower court severed appellant's claim for judicial review of the permit pursuant to the Administrative Procedure and Texas Register Act (APTRA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a (1992), and appellant brought the remaining cause pursuant to the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.001-011 (1986 & 1992), on the issue of the amended permit. The court held that judicial review was available after final agency decisions but not before. The court found appellee department had made no decision regarding the alleged amendments to the permit, and had jurisdiction to enforce the terms of its permits, to review disputed design revisions, and to determine when a proposed modification would require amendment. Because there had been no final administrative finding, the court held that appellant was not entitled to judicial review, and affirmed the lower court's dismissal.


OUTCOME: The lower court's dismissal of appellant water supply corporation's claim against appellees, Texas Department of Health and a solid-waste disposal operator, was affirmed because appellant could not seek judicial review under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act until all administrative remedies were exhausted, and appellant had not presented its complaint to appellee department prior to its request for judicial review.

 

1467 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Thweatt v. Jackson


NO. 3-91-364-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


838 S.W.2d 725; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2332



August 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled September 23, 1992. Released for Publication September 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BELL COUNTY, 146TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 132,787-B, HONORABLE RICK MORRIS, JUDGE

Original Opinion of June 3, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1415.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the District Court of Bell County, 146th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee debtor in appellant's action to recover on a note that he purchased from the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee debtor defaulted on a note that he executed to a bank. The Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC) closed the bank and became holder of appellee's note. The FDIC sold the note to appellant. Appellant demanded payment from appellee and initiated a recovery action. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee on the grounds that appellant's action was barred by the four-year limitations period found in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.004 (1986). Appellant contended the action was controlled by the six-year limitations period found at 12 U.S.C.S. § 1821(d)(14) because he purchased the note from the FDIC. On appeal, the court reversed the decision and remanded for further proceedings. When appellant purchased the note from the FDIC, he became vested with the same rights as the FDIC on the note. The six-year limitations period granted to the FDIC was therefore extended to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded for further proceedings. Appellant's recovery action was controlled by the six-year limitations period found in the Financial Institutions Reform, Recovery, and Enforcement Act of 1989 because appellant purchased the note from the FDIC. Appellant was vested with the same rights as the FDIC.

R Communications, Inc. v. Sharp


NO. 3-91-390-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2290



August 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled September 23, 1992. Released for Publication September 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-4893, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Corporate appellant challenged an order of the 345th District Court of Travis County (Texas), dismissing its complaint in which appellant sought a review of a sales tax deficiency without first paying the taxes allegedly owed. Appellant argued that the authorizing legislation, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 112.051(a), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Corporate appellant sought review of a sales tax deficiency assessed by appellee comptroller without first paying the taxes allegedly owed. Appellant argued that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 112.051(a), requiring appellant to make payment before filing the suit, was unconstitutional in that it imposed an impossible condition on an insolent taxpayer. Appellant contended that payment presented an impossible condition that foreclosed the opportunity for a meaningful appeal. The court determined that the jurisdictional requirements of the legislation did not offend appellant's other constitutional rights to open court. The court further determined that no classification of taxpayers was imposed that denied equal protection. The court held that the government had found it necessary to adopt stringent measures for the collection of taxes and that the statutory scheme was rationally related to government's legitimate interest in securing its finances. The court affirmed the order of the lower court dismissing appellant's action.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing corporate appellant's complaint was affirmed because the tax scheme requiring payment of an assessed tax before a judicial review was not unconstitutional. The court held that the statutory scheme was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest in securing finances.

1985 Cadillac Limousine v. State


NO. 01-91-00684-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


835 S.W.2d 822; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2152



August 13, 1992, rendered  
August 13, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 333rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-06882. Richard P. Bianchi, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of forfeiture entered by the 333rd District Court of Harris County (Texas), on grounds that there was no evidence or insufficient evidence that his Cadillac was used to facilitate any drug trafficking offense, and that the trial court improperly admitted and relied upon ex parte, self-serving hearsay statements.


OVERVIEW: The state brought an action to obtain forfeiture of a 1985 Cadillac limousine owned by defendant. Police officers inventoried the limousine because they were going to have the vehicle towed after determining that the vehicle had been used by several people who appeared to be intoxicated on a substance other than alcohol. Officers found a prescription bottle containing tablets, a baggie containing a white powdery substance, a piece of foil containing a brown powdery substance, a metal measuring spoon containing a white powdery substance, and other assorted drug paraphernalia. Field tests showed the brown substance was heroin and the white substance was cocaine. A judgment of forfeiture was ordered. Defendant appealed on grounds of insufficiency of evidence. The court found the evidence adduced at trial showed it was more probable than not that the limousine was instrumental in the possession and abuse of cocaine by a number of individuals, including defendant. The court affirmed the judgment of forfeiture and held that the trial court did not err admitting into evidence the affidavits of co-arrestees, which contained statements against penal interest.


OUTCOME: Judgment of forfeiture was affirmed because the trial court did not err in admitting the affidavits of defendant's co-arrestees which were against penal interest, and where it was more probable than not that the limousine was instrumental in the possession and abuse of cocaine by a number of individuals.

Crawford v. State


No. 14-86-00230-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2209



August 13, 1992, rendered  
August 13, 1992, filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 25, 1992. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 434,200.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the trial court, claiming that his statement was improperly excluded to preserve the codefendant's right to confrontation. The court affirmed and the Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) remanded to the court to determine the admissibility of appellant's tape-recorded statement and whether appellant was harmed by the parole charge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder after being tried jointly with his codefendant. On remand, the court addressed the admissibility of a tape-recorded statement and the harm appellant may have suffered by the parole charge. The court held that the tape recorded statement could not be redacted to exclude references to codefendant because the statement was 26 minutes long and contained 24 references to codefendant, expressly implicated codefendant, and was highly inculpatory of both defendants; therefore, the tape was properly excluded because admission would have violated codefendant's confrontation rights. The court also held that it was harmless error to give the parole charge. Although the statute on which the instruction was based was declared unconstitutional after appellant's trial, a new version was enacted and therefore appellant would receive the same jury instruction at any new punishment hearing. The court also determined that the jury assessed punishment based on the aggravating circumstances of the crime because it was particularly heinous and concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole law instruction did not contribute to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of murder because the parole law instruction did not contribute to the punishment assessed and the taped statement of appellant was properly excluded when it was impossible to redact to exclude references to codefendant.

OVERVIEW: After issuing its opinion, the court granted the motions for rehearing filed by appellee engineers and appellant municipal utility district. The matter before the court involved the parties' appeal and cross appeal of the judgment rendered in appellees' favor in their suit to recover sums allegedly due under a written contract to provide appellant with engineering services. August 12, 1992, filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Original Proceeding on Writ of Habeas Corpus is Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought a writ of habeas corpus from an order that held her in contempt of a temporary injunction and assessed punishment of three days of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Relator was punished with three days' imprisonment for being in contempt of court when she violated a temporary injunction. Appellant sought a writ of habeas corpus and requested early release for good behavior. The court determined that pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.032, § 2, the sheriff had the discretion to grant commutation of time for good conduct, and that it would have been improper for either the trial court or the court to have substituted its judgment for that of the sheriff. The court denied relator's request for a writ of habeas corpus and ordered relator to report to the sheriff.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator's request for a writ of habeas corpus, having determined that the commutation of time was within the sole discretion of the sheriff and that neither the trial court nor the court could have impinged on that discretion.

Bullin v. State


NO. B14-91-00422-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


836 S.W.2d 305; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2161



August 6, 1992, rendered  
August 6, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled September 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 522191-A. Curt Steib, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety challenged a final judgment from the 177th District Court, Harris County, Texas, finding that the appellant was jointly and severally liable for paying the forfeited bail bond plus court costs.


OVERVIEW: An individual was charged with a felony, and individual as the principal, with appellant as surety executed a bail bond conditioned upon the individual's subsequent appearance. When the individual failed to appear, the bond was declared forfeited, and an interlocutory judgment of forfeiture was signed. The trial court overruled appellant's request for a remittitur holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(a) (1989) was unconstitutional and that Mexico was not within the meaning of "jurisdiction" under art. 22.16(a)(2). Final judgment was entered against appellant finding that he was jointly and severally liable to pay the bond plus court costs. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment for two reasons. First, appellant was not entitled to a remittitur under art. 22.16(a) because it was unconstitutional, and under the constitutional portion of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(d) (1989), the trial court acted within its discretion when it denied to remit the forfeited bond prior to entry of a final judgment of forfeiture. Second, even though bail bond forfeiture was a criminal matter, the trial court had authority to assess civil court costs under art. 22.16(d).


OUTCOME: Appellant surety's judgment to pay the forfeited bail bond plus court costs was affirmed for two reasons. First, under the constitutional portion of the statute, the trial court had discretion to deny remittitur of the forfeited bail bond before it entered final judgment. Second, even though bail bond forfeiture was a criminal matter, the trial court had statutory authority to assess civil court costs.

 

1474 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Angel v. State


No. C14-92-00108-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2269



August 6, 1992, Rendered  
August 6, 1992, filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 555,839


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus challenging a judgment from the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of a child. Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 21.02(6) and 20.03 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment convicting appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child and denied habeas corpus relief on appellant's claims that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 21.02(6) and 20.03 were unconstitutional. Appellant argued that article 21.02(6), allowing the use of the term "on or about" in an indictment, was void on vagueness grounds and that article 20.03, authorizing the state to present offenses to the grand jury at any time except during their discussions of indictments, denied him an examining trial. The court noted that a law was vague only if it failed to give a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice that his contemplated conduct was forbidden. The use of the term "on or about" sufficiently alerted appellant to prepare his defense for any time within the applicable five-year statutory period. Although Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 16.01 provided the right to an examining trial before indictment, it did not preclude the presentation of a case to a grand jury without an examining trial. The purpose of an examining trial, to determine probable cause, was as timely accomplished by presenting evidence to the grand jury as by an examining trial.


OUTCOME: The court denied habeas corpus relief and affirmed appellant's aggravated sexual assault conviction. The court concluded that the laws at issue were constitutional. One law was not vague because it sufficiently apprised appellant of the need to prepare his defense for any time during the statutory period. The other law did not deprive appellant of an examining trial right because such a right was not implicated in a grand jury indictment.

Murdock v. State


No. 6-91-070-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


840 S.W.2d 558; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2042



August 4, 1992, Decided  
August 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 528,128



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the 232nd Judicial District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendant of illegal investment and assessed punishment at 25 years confinement and $ 300,000.00 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of illegal investment and on appeal argued that he was denied his right of confrontation, that the trial court committed reversible error by admitting evidence of extraneous offenses, that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence seized in violation of his constitutional rights, that the trial court failed to instruct the jury of the permissible conditions of probation, that he was denied his right to due process of law and a fair trial. The court affirmed and held that confrontation was never considered as an absolute and that hearsay testimony by a co-conspirator may be admitted if other evidence presented sufficiently substantiated its content. The court held that the trial court did not err by failing to include all statutory terms of probation over objection. The court held that absent a showing of good cause, the trial court correctly refused to consider defendant's motion for new trial because it was filed untimely. The court held that extraneous, unadjudicated offenses were admissible during the punishment phase of defendant's trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of illegal investment because a recorded statement by co-conspirators was admissible when the proponent of the statements showed by preponderance of the evidence that a conspiracy existed. The court held that where officer made legitimate stop for actual violation of law, officer was free to enforce law and detain defendant for violation, and after impoundment of vehicle, inventory search was legal.

Hooten v. Fleckenstein


NO. 12-91-00180-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


836 S.W.2d 300; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2093



July 31, 1992, delivered  
July 31, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 145TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NACOGDOCHES COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought relief from a judgment which granted appellee doctor's motion for summary judgment entered by the 145th Judicial District Court, Nacogdochies County, Texas, in appellant's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient was injured in an automobile accident, and he was treated by appellee doctor for various injuries. Within weeks after appellant was discharged from the hospital, he went to see another physician concerning problems with his right arm. Appellant found out at that time that he had suffered a fractured right elbow and would require surgery. More than two years later, appellant was told that he had suffered loss of mobility in his right elbow due to the failure of appellee doctor to diagnose properly his broken elbow. Appellant sued appellee doctor for medical malpractice. The court held that appellant knew within weeks of his discharge that appellee had breached the required standard of care resulting in injuries, which was well within the two-year statute of limitations under the medical liability and insurance improvement act. The court held that appellant had a reasonable opportunity to discover the wrong and bring suit, therefore the granting of summary judgment by the trial court was proper since there was no genuine issue of material fact concerning the time when appellant discovered the nature of the injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's granting of appellee doctor's motion for summary judgment because appellant patient did not file his lawsuit until after the statute of limitations for filing medical malpractice actions had past.

Cain v. State


NO. 09-91-118 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


834 S.W.2d 628; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2351



July 31, 1992, Delivered  
July 31, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion dated June 10, 1992 is Withdrawn and Substituted by the Court. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 258th District Court. Polk County, Texas. Cause Number 12,435. O'Neal Bacon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff challenged a conviction from the 258th District Court, Polk County, Texas, for nepotism under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5996a, based upon the assertion that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and violative of the Fifth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V, because art. 5996a criminalized any act taken by appellant with respect to his two children who were employed by the sheriff's department.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sheriff's two children were employed with the sheriff's department before appellant was elected to be sheriff. Appellant promoted one child and gave both raises. Appellant was convicted of nepotism under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5996a. The appellate court reversed. The court observed that § 1(a) of art. 5996a generally prohibited appellant from employing family members. But § 1(b) of art. 5996a excepted family members that were previously employed, than § 1(c) of art. 5996a prohibited appellant from participating in any decision regarding the employment status of a family member. The appellate court held that as applied to a sole officeholder, like appellant, the statute was unconstitutionally vague, because it criminalized any act taken by appellant with respect to employed family members including decisions to dismiss family members for criminal conduct. The appellate court indicated that while the legislature may not have intended that result, a literal reading of the statute required that result.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant sheriff's conviction for nepotism because the statute under which appellant was convicted was unconstitutionally vague because the statute prohibited appellant, as a sole officeholder, from participating in any decision regarding the employment status of a family member.

Garrett v. State


NO. 01-90-00492-CR, NO. 01-90-00493-CR, NO. 01-90-00494-CR, NO. 01-90-00495-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


834 S.W.2d 605; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1953



July 23, 1992, rendered and delivered  
July 23, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 525,804, Trial Court Cause No. 526,467, Trial Court Cause No. 526,468, Trial Court Cause No. 555,853. GINA BENCH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him under four separate indictments for aggravated robbery, robbery, and theft. The trial court instructed the jury in one cause about the possibility of parole in accordance with Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(d) (Supp. 1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under separate indictments for aggravated robbery, robbery, and theft. The trial court charged the jury with a parole instruction pursuant to Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1992). The instruction was about the possibility of parole. Defendant appealed. On appeal, defendant argued that the instruction violated his constitutional rights including his right to due process guaranteed by U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV. The court affirmed. The court held that the Texas Constitution had been amended to permit the legislature to pass laws that required or permitted the courts to tell juries about the effect of good conduct time and eligibility for parole. Tex. Const. art. 4, § 11 (a). The court held further that a jury's consideration of parole and commutation laws did not violate federal due process. The court rejected defendant's argument that he had to be given an opportunity to present evidence on the parole laws in light of the instruction. The court held that federal due process was not violated when defendant was denied the opportunity to present evidence about the parole law at art. 37.07, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the statute under which the parole instruction was given by the trial court to the jury was not unconstitutional either under the state constitution or the federal constitution. Furthermore, the court held that defendant's due process rights were not violated when he was denied the opportunity to present evidence about the parole laws.
