State v. Bankerd


Appeal No. 04-91-00653-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


838 S.W.2d 639; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2608



July 22, 1992, Delivered  
July 22, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied September 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 166th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 89-TA1-4088. Honorable Charles Gonzalez, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxing authorities sought review of a decision by the 166th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted judgment for personal liability against appellee property owner and found that appellee receiver's lien interest was property and that 12 U.S.C.S. § 1825(b)(2) (1989) prohibited the foreclosure of the property, the deed of trust lien, without appellee receiver's consent.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxing authorities filed suit against appellee property owner and a bank. The trial court granted judgment for liability against appellee property owner and found that appellee receiver's lien interest was property and that 12 U.S.C.S. § 1825(b)(2) (1989) prohibited the foreclosure of the property, the trust lien deed, without appellee receiver's consent. The court affirmed the judgment against appellee property owner and for appellee receiver's lien interest because the lien was owned by appellee receiver for a bank pursuant to § 1825(b)(2), 28 U.S.C.S. § 2410 (1978) did not operate to bar the trial court from ordering the property to be sold subject to appellee receiver's lien, foreclosure of appellant's lien would have extinguished appellee receiver's lien, and appellant was not deprived of its property right. The court held that appellee receiver's lien was property under § 1825. Appellee receiver succeeded to all rights, title, powers, and privileges of the failed bank under 12 U.S.C.S. § 1832(d)(2)(A)(i) (1989). Section 1825 did not operate as a complete bar to foreclosure by appellant because it prohibited foreclosure without appellee receiver's consent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellee property owner and for appellee receiver's lien interest because the lien was owned by appellee receiver for the bank, the statute did not operate to bar the trial court from ordering the property to be sold subject to appellee receiver's lien, foreclosure of appellant taxing authorities' lien would have extinguished appellee receiver's lien, and appellant was not deprived of its property right.

Texas Dep't of Corrections v. Sisters of St. Francis of St. Jude Hosp.


NO. 01-91-00503-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


836 S.W.2d 719; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1871



July 16, 1992, rendered and delivered  
July 16, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 21st District Court. Washington County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 28,464



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Texas Department of Corrections and the State of Texas, sought review of the judgment from the 21st District Court, Washington County, Texas, that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital and held appellants liable under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann., arts. 6166g and 6184n, § 5 (1979), for expenses incurred by an inmate released on emergency medical reprieve.


OVERVIEW: Appellee brought suit against appellants, Texas Department of Corrections (TDC) and the State of Texas, to recover expenses incurred by an inmate released on emergency medical reprieve. Appellee's sole contention was that appellants were liable under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 6166g and 6184n, § 5 (1979). Both sides sought summary judgment, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Appellants sought review and argued that while on reprieve the inmate was not considered a prisoner and as such, appellants were not liable for the expenses. The court held that under art. 6184n, § 5, the inmate was a prisoner of appellant TDC while released on emergency reprieve and appellant TDC was responsible under art. 6166g for treatment. Further, appellants knew the inmate needed medical care and were not harmed by appellee's lack of notice. The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee because appellants had a statutory duty to provide medical care to an inmate on emergency medical reprieve and that duty was not excused by appellee's lack of notice of the inmate's admission or the inmate's financial responsibility provision in the governor's proclamation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital because appellants, Texas Department of Corrections and the State of Texas, had a statutory duty to provide medical care to an inmate on emergency medical reprieve and that duty was not excused by appellee's lack of notice of the inmate's admission or the inmate's financial responsibility provision in the governor's reprieve.

Porter v. State


NO. 01-91-00454-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1977



July 16, 1992, rendered and delivered  
July 16, 1992, filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 14, 1992.
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by Ex parte Porter, 2010 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 712 (Tex. Crim. App., Dec. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 582820



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 248th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault, found defendant guilty, and assessed punishment at confinement for life. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, a statement made during the state's closing argument, and a jury charge on parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at life imprisonment. Defendant appealed contending that there was insufficient evidence, prosecutorial misconduct in the nature of a statement made to the jury outside the record, and an improper jury charge on parole. The court found that the evidence, viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, indicated that a rational trier of fact could have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The prosecutor's comment on defendant's written statement which was never admitted into evidence was permissible closing argument and the jury could properly consider the existence of good conduct and parole time but could not consider how it could be awarded or forfeited. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction was affirmed because the trial court properly concluded that a rational trier of fact could find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The state's comments regarding defendant's statement, which had not been admitted into evidence, were permissible closing argument and the charge was proper because the jury was not permitted to calculate the effect any good time conduct and parole had on defendant's sentence.

Chauncey v. State


No. 08-91-00367-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


837 S.W.2d 179; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1902



July 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 2, 1992. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 238th District Court of Midland County, Texas (TC# CRB-17,170[2]). Trial Court Judge: Hon. John G. Hyde



DISPOSITION: Having overruled each of Appellant's points of error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 238th District Court of Midland County (Texas) that convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in striking a prospective juror for cause because the veniremember was unable to remain unequivocal when stating that sympathy would not play a part in her decision. The court held that appellant was not entitled to have the jury indicate whether guilt was due to loss of physical or loss of mental facilities. The court determined that the imposition of dual jail and restitution center terms was not unconstitutionally excessive since the combined total amount of time did not exceed the maximum sentence allowed by law. The court held that the imposition of 180 days detention as a condition of probation pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Pro. Ann. art. 42.12, § 12 (1992) was proper. The court also held that it was not unreasonable for the trial court to order appellant to pay the cost of alcohol and drug testing every day while he was on intensive probation and that the trial court was not required to make an express finding of appellant's ability to pay for the testing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in striking a prospective juror for cause, the general verdict was supported by the evidence, appellant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, and the trial court did not err in requiring appellant to pay the cost of alcohol and drug testing while he was on intensive probation.

Bidelspach v. State


No. 05-91-00796-CR, No. 05-91-00797-CR, No. 05-91-00798-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


840 S.W.2d 516; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2964



July 14, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petitio for Discretionary Review Refused November 25, 1992. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted February 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 1. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MC91-A1427-D, MC91-A1428-D, MC91-A1429-D



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part. Reversed and Remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 1, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him for transporting liquid waste without a valid permit and for failing to complete a trip ticket.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for transporting liquid waste without a valid permit and for failing to complete a trip ticket. The court held that the city ordinance prohibiting the affirmative act of operating a vehicle for the purpose of transporting liquid waste without obtaining a permit did not conflict with Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 6.01 (1974), which provided that only a statute could make failure to perform an act a criminal offense, and was not unconstitutional because it did not impose liability for the failure to obtain a permit. The court held that the city ordinance requiring completion of a four-part trip ticket to document the generation, transportation, and disposal of liquid waste conflicted with § 6.01 and Tex. Const. Art. XI, § 5, and was unconstitutional because it imposed criminal liability for an omission. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for transporting liquid waste without a permit, and reversed and remanded his conviction for failing to complete a trip ticket.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for transporting liquid waste without a permit because the city ordinance was not unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for failing to complete a trip ticket because the city ordinance was unconstitutional.

Moore v. State


No. C14-91-00327-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1830



July 2, 1992, rendered and delivered  
July 2, 1992, filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 591,255



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged an order of the 262nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, appellant criminal defendant was convicted of murder. Appellant made three statements to the officers, but refused to sign them. After he contacted a lawyer, appellant stated he wished to waive his right to counsel, made a statement, and signed it. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the statements. The appellate court disagreed, and affirmed his conviction. In so ruling, the court held that the first two statements were non-custodial, as the officers were simply making inquiries as to what happened. The third statement, although made while in custody, was admissible as appellant waived his Miranda rights, and evidence at the scene corroborated his statement. The admission of appellant's fourth statement did not violate U.S. Const. amend. V, even though appellant had contacted a lawyer, because appellant initiated contact with the officers and unequivocally expressed his desire to give an additional statement. The court held that the punishment instruction on parole followed the precise language of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1991) and thus did not violate Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's conviction for murder, because his first two statements were admissible as they were non-custodial, his third statement was corroborated by evidence after appellant waived his Miranda rights, and his fourth statement was admissible even though he contacted a lawyer, because he initiated contact with the officers and unequivocally expressed a desire to give an additional statement.

State v. Manning


No. 10-91-221-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


833 S.W.2d 322; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1788



July 1, 1992, delivered  
July 1, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 52nd District Court. Coryell County, Texas. Trial Court # 12,311



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the 52nd District Court, Coryell County (Texas), contending that the trial court erred in sustaining defendant's objection to the state's exhibits, a security agreement and a loan agreement.


OVERVIEW: The state charged defendant with the offense of hindering a secured creditor, a jury was empanelled and sworn, defendant pleaded not guilty, and during testimony of the first witness, defendant objected to two exhibits, a security agreement and loan agreement. State challenged the trial court judgment, contending that it erred in sustaining defendant's objection. The court dismissed the state's appeal, finding that jeopardy attached when the jury was empanelled and sworn, preventing the state's appeal. Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 44.01(a)(1), which permitted state to appeal any trial court order concerning an indictment or information that effectively terminated the prosecution in favor of the defendant, did not apply to this appeal because jeopardy had attached. The court also noted that the indictment was dismissed on the state's motion, and the state should not be able to take advantage of a resulting error on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the state's appeal, finding that the state had no right to appeal once jeopardy had attached, and jeopardy attached when the jury was empanelled and sworn.

Valles v. Texas Com. on Jail Standards


NO. 3-91-017-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


845 S.W.2d 284; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 3166



July 1, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 12, 1992. Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 3, 1993. Released for Publication February 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 444,497, HONORABLE BOB JONES, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged a summary judgment for appellees, Texas Commission on Jail Standards and executive director, in appellants ' lawsuits for injunctive and declaratory relief and damages under the Texas Wrongful Death Act, the Survival Statute, and the Texas Tort Claims Act alleging acts that were negligent, reckless, and violative of the Texas Constitution when their son committed suicide in the Tom Green County Jail.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees, Texas Commission on Jail Standards (Commission) and executive director in appellant parent's lawsuits for injunctive and declaratory relief and for damages under the Texas Wrongful Death Act, the Survival Statute, and the Texas Tort Claims Act arising out of their son's suicide in Tom Green County Jail. Appellant alleged negligent and reckless acts and violation of the Texas Constitution for failing to adequately supervise, to maintain standards and to take preventive measures to diminish a life-endangering situation. The court affirmed the summary judgment for appellees because the jail system structure and the applicable statutes vested responsibility and supervisory duty for county jails with the county commissioners' courts, not the Commission. The court held the Commission did not owe a duty to appellant and successfully negated an element of appellant's claim. The court concluded that the legislature enacted Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 511.009 (1990) and other statutes with full knowledge of the existing law and responsibilities and purposefully withheld mandatory enforcement duties from the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for appellees, Texas Commission on Jail Standards and Executive Director in appellant parents' lawsuit for declaratory and injunctive relief and damages arising out of their son's suicide in a county jail. The court found that under the jail system and the applicable statute, the Commission did not owe a duty to the parents and conclusively negated an element of appellant's case.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS

June 30, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 162nd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 86-07704-I



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the 162nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees and denied appellants' motions for partial summary judgment in an action that sought a bill of review and collaterally attacked a prior judgment against appellants. Appellants had also filed and lost two previous actions in federal court that attacked the prior judgment.


OVERVIEW: In a prior action, the trial court entered judgment in favor of appellees and against appellants in an action that alleged appellants wrongfully shut in oil and gas wells. After appellants filed and lost two separate federal court actions attacking the prior judgment, appellants filed the present collateral attack and bill of review. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees and denied appellants' motions for partial summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the present action was barred by res judicata and could not be asserted in an equitable bill of review because it arose out of the same facts and involved the same parties as the federal court actions, the judgments in the federal court actions were final and on the merits, and the claims asserted in the present action were or could have been asserted in the federal court actions. The court also affirmed the trial court's order that permanently enjoined one of the appellants from initiating any additional challenges to the prior judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees and denied appellants' motions for partial summary judgment because appellants' claims were barred by res judicata. The court also affirmed the order of the trial court that prohibited one of the appellants from initiating or continuing other attacks on the prior judgment.

Lyons v. State


No. 6-91-059-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


835 S.W.2d 715; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1607



June 23, 1992, Decided  
June 23, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law. Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court No. 902-90



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction, by the County Court at Law, Brazos County (Texas), of criminal nonsupport, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motions to dismiss and to quash the information, in refusing to submit a requested special charge to the jury, and in denying a request for a directed verdict, and further contending that the verdict was contrary to the law and the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of criminal nonsupport of his minor child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.05 (1989). He argued that because the court refused to grant his motion to dismiss the information, he was denied due process and equal protection and was ordered imprisoned for debt. He also urged that, because the information failed to define the word "support," the court erred in denying his motion to quash. The court affirmed his conviction. It held that the information was sufficient to charge the commission of the offense in ordinary and concise language and in such a manner as to give a person of common understanding notice of the particular offense with which he was charged and to enable the court, on conviction, to pronounce the proper judgment. The court further held that imprisonment assessed as punishment for violation of a statute was not an unconstitutional imprisonment for debt, that the trial court's jury instruction that did not require appellee state to prove ability to pay was a correct statement of the law as amended, and that the jury verdict was not contrary to the law or the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that an information failing to define the term "support" was sufficient to charge the commission of the offense as to give a person of common understanding notice of the particular offense with which he was charged. The court further held that imprisonment for violation of the nonsupport statute was not an unconstitutional imprisonment for debt.

Morris v. State


NO. C14-91-00444-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


833 S.W.2d 624; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1506



June 11, 1992, rendered  
June 11, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 16, 1992. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9040405. David Mendoza, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11, Harris County (Texas) of failure to report child abuse under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 34.01, 34.02 (1992). She contended that the statutes were unconstitutionally vague, that the trial court erred in admitting photographs of the child, that the jury charge failed to set out all elements of the offense, and that the information was defective.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a teacher of retarded children, was convicted of failure to report child abuse after two aides held a child's hand under hot water as punishment. She sought review, contending that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 34.01, 34.02 (1992) were unconstitutionally vague, and that the trial court erred in admitting photographs of the child's hand, that the jury charge failed to set out all elements of the offense, and that the information was defective. The court affirmed, holding that the statutes were not unconstitutionally vague because they gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice of the requirement to file a report with the appropriate agencies when he had cause to believe that a child was being abused. The court further held that the photographs were properly admitted because they were relevant to the attending physician's testimony and were not unduly prejudicial. The court also held that the jury charge did not fail to set out all essential elements of the offense merely because it did not specify every agency to which a person could report suspected child abuse, and that the information was not defective because it tracked the language of the applicable statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the reporting statutes were not unconstitutionally vague because they gave an ordinarily intelligent person fair notice of the requirement, that the photos were relevant to a physician's testimony and not unduly prejudicial, that the jury charge was not incomplete by failing to name all agencies to which abuse could be reported, and that the indictment sufficiently tracked the statutory language.

Rentz v. State


NO. A14-92-00136-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


833 S.W.2d 278; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1512



June 11, 1992, rendered  
June 11, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 208th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 622,584. John H. Kyles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged denial of his request for a writ of habeas corpus, through which he sought relief from extradition, from the 208th District Court, Harris County (Texas), arguing that probable cause had never been adequately established and that the state had not shown that the person in custody was the same person wanted in the requesting state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review from denial of a writ of habeas corpus, with respect to his request for relief from extradition to Florida for the offense of trafficking in cocaine, contending that the affidavit and descriptors from the demanding state were insufficient to establish probable cause against appellant and that the state never proved the person in custody was the same person wanted in Florida. On appeal, lower court judgment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that once a governor had granted extradition, a court considering release on habeas corpus could do no more than decide whether the extradition documents were in order on their face, whether the petitioner had been charged with a crime in the demanding state, whether the petitioner was the person named in the extradition request, and whether the petitioner was a fugitive. With respect to the instant case, the court noted that the state met its burden of proving that a judicial determination of probable cause had been made. The court further found that appellant failed to show through sworn affidavits that his identity was in issue.


OUTCOME: Denial of the writ of habeas corpus was affirmed because the state met its burden of demonstrating that a judicial determination of probable cause had been made, while appellant did not sufficiently show that his identity was at issue.

 

1493 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. State


NO. 3-90-271-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


832 S.W.2d 719; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1491



June 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 87,403, HONORABLE BOB PERKINS, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the sentencing decision from the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District No. 87403 (Texas), which on remand for resentencing of appellant's sexual assault conviction admitted evidence of appellant's "prior conviction" for burglary. The burglary conviction arose from actions after the sexual assault, and the evidence was entered after the first sexual assault sentence but before resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced on remand to 80 years for aggravated sexual assault. As his main challenge to the resentencing decision, appellant argued that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence of appellant's conviction for burglary, which arose out of actions after the sexual assault and which was entered after the original sentencing for sexual assault. The court rejected appellant's argument, finding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 44.29(b) & 37.07, § 3(a) (1992) worked together to render admissible evidence of a final conviction occurring before the date of the punishment retrial. The court also denied appellant's request for reversal based on prosecutorial comments. First, the trial court had sustained appellant's objection to some of those comments, and appellant had not requested any additional relief below. Second, appellant had not even objected to other comments, which were therefore waived on appeal. The court also rejected appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims addressed to the merits of the original guilt determination, as they had already been denied in the first appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence, imposed upon appellant pursuant to resentencing, of 80 years for aggravated sexual assault. The trial court did not err when it admitted, during the punishment retrial, evidence of a burglary conviction arising from acts committed after the assault and entered after the original assault sentence. Appellant's remaining arguments had been either waived or addressed in the first appeal.

State v. Clouse


NO. 09-91-219 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


839 S.W.2d 459; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2920



June 3, 1992, Delivered  
June 3, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 9th District Court. Montgomery County, Texas. Cause No. 90-11-01301-CR. Lynn Coker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the 9th District Court of Montgomery County (Texas), which granted appellee's motion to suppress evidence in a case for the first degree felony offense of engaging in organized criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an interlocutory appeal after appellee's motion to suppress evidence was granted in the state's case charging appellee for the first degree felony offense of engaging in organized criminal activity. At issue was the search of a wrecker service which contained an office, residence, garage, and apartment. On appeal, the court affirmed and was unwilling to conclude that the trial court abused its discretion based upon controverted evidence because the regulatory inspection authorized by the licensing scheme extended only to documentation. The search conducted by the officers in this case was not in furtherance of the regulatory scheme and exceeded the scope of a legitimate search. Appellee's cross-point regarding the court's failure to grant appellee's request to suppress evidence from two subsequent searches of the property was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction because in an appeal by the state under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.01 (1992), appellee had no right to an interlocutory appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of appellee's motion to suppress evidence because the search of wrecker service property was not in furtherance of a regulatory scheme and exceeded the scope of a legitimate search.

In re D.S.


NUMBER 13-91-199-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


833 S.W.2d 250; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1327



May 28, 1992, delivered  
May 28, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled July 30, 1992. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of the decision of the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas) which adjudicated appellant guilty of murder.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellant challenged an adjudication and disposition of a juvenile court action alleging appellant committed murder. Appellant was adjudicated under the state's determinate sentencing statutes. The jury found appellant used a deadly weapon and assessed disposition at 30 years. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the determinate sentencing statutes and asserted that the several actions by the trial court constituted reversible error. Appellant specifically complained that the determinate sentencing scheme provided that a person could serve time in the penitentiary or be punished without ever being convicted of a crime, it denied appellant bail, and that it violated the separation of powers doctrine. The court noted that appellant did not argue impropriety, only the potential for impropriety. No error was shown to have occurred, and thus, nothing was presented to the court for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court finding appellant used a deadly weapon and assessing disposition at 30 years when appellant did not preserve certain issues for review on appeal and the determinate sentencing statutes furthered a compelling state interest.

Wynne v. State


NO. 07-89-0221-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


831 S.W.2d 513; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1314



May 27, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 24, 1992. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 14, 1992. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied December 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 47TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 21,507-A; HONORABLE DAVID L. GLEASON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 47th Judicial District Court of Potter County (Texas), which convicted appellant for murder after denying his motion to change venue.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for murder by motion and points of error. The motion was based on appellant's failure to provide a complete statement of facts, and the points were that the trial court erred in denying his motion to change venue, in allowing his cross-examination on certain matters, and in its factual and legal conclusions concerning the venue hearing. The court affirmed, holding that appellant failed to timely prosecute his appeal, because he absented himself for more than three years from the jurisdiction, and the court reported had already destroyed any notes concerning appellant's case. Appellant had not showed compliance with the requirements to obtain a reversal of his conviction due to the incomplete statement of facts. He used all his peremptory challenges, did not request additional challenges, and did not challenge any of the selected jurors for cause. Additionally, there was no evidence that, despite publicity, appellant was denied the right to a fair trial or that the trial court abused its discretion in denying his motion for change of venue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Defendant's conviction for murder was upheld, because appellant failed to timely prosecute his appeal, he had not obtained a complete statement of facts, and the trial court had not abused its discretion in denying appellant's motion for change of venue.

 

1497 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Grigsby v. State


No. 05-91-00728-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


833 S.W.2d 573; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 2193



May 21, 1992, Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 30, 1992.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals of Texas, Fifth District Dallas, which convicted defendant for aggravated robbery, alleging the state made an improper jury argument and the jury charge was erroroneous.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant were charged with aggravated robbery by indictment, which alleged a prior conviction for enhancement purposes and both pled true to the enhancement paragraphs. Evidence of co-defendant's prior conviction and the date of the offense were presented, showing the present offense was committed before co-defendant's sentence for the prior conviction expired. Both were tried and convicted in the same trial. Defendant alleged state's argument during the punishment stage was improper since it invited the jury to consider parole laws in assessing punishment and the trial court's denial of a jury charge on parole was reversible error. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that since prior enhancement convictions must occur sequentially, state was allowed to argue the date of indictment and prior sentences but it did not directly mention or allude to the parole laws and merely summed up the evidence, and that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07(4)(a) required a parole charge and the failure to give the charge was harmless error since it was not calculated to injure defendant's rights and defendant suffered no actual harm from the omission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that state's jury argument during the punishment phase was proper since it did not allude to or mention parole laws and the trial court's denial of a mandatory jury charge on parole was erroneous but harmless error since it was not calculated to injure defendant's rights and he did not suffer actual harm resulting therefrom.

 

1498 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Shoberg v. Shoberg


NO. B14-91-00473-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


830 S.W.2d 149; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1205



May 14, 1992, rendered  
May 14, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Withdrawn on Grant of Rehearing May 14, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1205.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 165th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-54269. Kenneth Harrison, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of February 27, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 505.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of the grant of summary judgment to appellee ex-husband and the denial of her motion for summary judgment by the 165th District Court, Harris County (Texas), in a suit to cancel and to hold of no force or effect a promissory note and deed of trust executed as part of a divorce decree.


OVERVIEW: In their divorce decree, appellant ex-wife received the couple's home in return for the execution of a promissory note and deed of trust to appellee ex-husband. Appellant made very few payments under the original agreement and two subsequent modifications, and appellee sought to foreclose on the home. The court found that the parties' agreement incorporated into the divorce decree constituted part of a valid and binding final judgment. The court held that appellant's claim that the lien was unconstitutional was an impermissible collateral attack on a final judgment because it claimed the judgment debt was rendered voidable by an erroneous interpretation of substantive law. The court found appellant's assertion that the interest charged in the modified agreements was usurious to be meritless. The court noted that interest charged on past due interest was not usurious and appellant's forbearance from seeking additional child support was not a "charge" within the meaning of the usury statutes. The court affirmed the award of summary judgment to appellee and the denial of appellant's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of summary judgment to appellee ex-husband and the denial of appellant ex-wife's motion for summary judgment because appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of the lien was an impermissible collateral attack on a final judgment and the interest charged in the modified agreements was not usurious.

 

1499 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Mayo v. State


No. A14-91-00325-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1213



May 7, 1992, Rendered  
May 7, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Appellants' Petition For Discretionary Review Refused October 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 263rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 530,604



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 263rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), that convicted him of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Complainant testified that she awoke to find appellant holding his hand over her mouth. He held a gun to her temple and said that he might not kill her if she was quiet. Appellant tied complainant up, sexually assaulted her, and kidnapped her at gunpoint. Complainant was returned to her home. She reported the incident to the police and rode with an officer to retrace where appellant had taken her. DNA evidence established that appellant raped her. Appellant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault. He appealed his conviction. The court found that a conviction for aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault required proof that appellant used or exhibited a firearm. There was sufficient evidence that appellant used or exhibited a firearm because complainant testified that appellant pointed a gun at her and threatened to kill her, and a gun was found in appellant's possession. The court found the jury instruction as to good conduct time and parole was proper because Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a) allowed a jury to be instructed as to the existence of good time and parole.


OUTCOME: A judgment of the lower court that convicted appellant of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault was affirmed because complainant's testimony that appellant pointed a gun at her and threatened to kill her was sufficient to find that appellant used or exhibited a firearm during the commission of the crime.

 

1500 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. A14-91-00689-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1216



May 7, 1992, Rendered  
May 7, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 540,558



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for the offense of murder and his sentence to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for the offense of murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02, and his sentence to life imprisonment. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury regarding good conduct time and parole in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4(a). Appellant claimed that the instruction violated his right to due process. The court disagreed and affirmed the conviction. The court held that the jury instruction provided the jury with relevant information and eliminated the risk that the jury would be misled by the usual meaning of phrases such as "20 years" and possibly assess punishment at a meaninglessly low level. The court held that the constitution did not prohibit the state from accurately characterizing its sentencing choices. Appellant objected to the instruction regarding a deadly weapon. The court noted that appellant was indicted for causing the death of the complainant by shooting him with a deadly weapon, namely, a firearm and, therefore, when the jury found appellant guilty as charged in the indictment, they necessarily found that he used a deadly weapon in the commission of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder and his sentence to life imprisonment. The trial court did not err in instructing the jury regarding good conduct time and parole violation because the state was not prohibited from characterizing its sentence choices. The instruction did not violate appellant's right to due process.

Fidelity & Deposit Co. v. Concerned Taxpayers of Lee County, Inc.


NO. 3-90-281-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


829 S.W.2d 923; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1099



May 6, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 479,553, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety challenged the decision of the 167th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted summary judgment on appellee taxpayers' motion requesting the trial court to find appellant liable for attorney fees awarded in an earlier case against trustees bonded by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant surety provided statutory public official bonds for the trustees of a hospital district that was declared unconstitutional in an action filed by appellee taxpayers. Appellees were awarded attorney fees and sought to collect them from the bonds. On cross-motions for summary judgment, the trial court ordered appellants to pay the attorney fees. Appellants claimed no liability because the bond did not explicitly provide for attorney fees and the trustees did not perform any acts unfaithfully. The court affirmed, finding that the bond was broadly worded to include any damages awarded against the trustees in the unfaithful performance of their official duties. In addition, the court found that the trustees had held meetings in violation of the Open Meetings Act, which supported the trial court's finding that the trustees had unfaithfully performed their duties and thus triggered the bond. On appellees' cross-motion for attorney fees under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 38.001(8) (1986), the court found that appellees were incidental beneficiaries at best to the surety contract, so they were not entitled to additional attorney fees based upon the contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of summary judgment finding appellant surety liable for attorney fees based upon the bond provided to trustees because the language of the bonds covered any damages awarded against the trustees in the unfaithful performance of their official duties and the acts of the trustees in holding meetings in violation of the Open Meetings Act was unfaithful performance.

Landers v. State


NO. C14-91-00453-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1075



April 30, 1992, rendered  
April 30, 1992, filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 553,156



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of burglary of habitation, with the underlying felony of aggravated assault, and asserted that there were numerous procedural errors at trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for burglary of habitation with the underlying felony of aggravated assault. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that both the indictment and the jury instructions were proper, despite appellant's contention that they failed to require a culpable mental state on the element of entering complainant's habitation knowing that it was without effective consent. The court found that there was no implied consent to break and enter an apartment merely because appellant and complainant had dated. Additionally, no egregious harm resulted from the omission of the word "intentionally" from the jury charge because there was no evidence that appellant did not intend to enter the apartment. The trial court did not err in limiting cross-examination of the complainant because evidence regarding the intimacy of her relationship with appellant was not relevant to appellant's right to break into her apartment. The limitation of appellant's cross-examination of a witness was proper because that testimony was not relevant as to whether appellant had consent to enter the apartment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's burglary conviction because there was no error in the indictment or jury charge as to his culpable mental state, and the trial court's limitation of the cross-examination of two witnesses was not in error where neither witnesses' testimony was relevant to the issue of the complainant's consent to appellant's entry into her apartment.

 

1503 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brand v. State


NO. 2-90-208-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


828 S.W.2d 824; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1035



April 28, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW #2 OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE HON. VIRGIL VAHLENKAMP, JR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a conviction for speeding by the County Court at Law #2 of Denton County (Texas). Based upon religious beliefs, appellant contended that the fine assessed in Federal Reserve Notes consisted of unlawful money and, as such, the Texas state laws imposing fines payable with Federal Reserve notes for traffic violations violated the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The jury found appellant guilty of speeding and assessed a $ 200.00 fine. Appellant's religious convictions led him to believe that Federal Reserve Notes were not lawful money. Thus, on appeal, appellant asserted that the trial court erred when it imposed a fine, based upon state law, that consisted of appellant paying a fine using Federal Reserve Notes because it was unconstitutional. Appellant also asserted that the trial judge and the prosecutor violated their oaths of office in enforcing unconstitutional statutes. The court affirmed. The court ruled that Congress had the power under the United States Constitution to establish a national paper currency; had delegated this power to the Federal Reserve System; and had designated the Federal Reserve Note as legal tender. Thus, the court held that Federal Reserve Notes were lawful money, and Texas statutes and the Texas State officers that imposed fines payable with Federal Reserve Notes for traffic violations were constitutional. The court stated that although appellant was entitled to his personal opinions, he was not entitled to set himself up as separate and apart from the laws of the land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that assessed fines in Federal Reserve Notes against appellant for speeding. Appellant was denied relief because there was no violation of appellant's constitutional rights when he was assessed a fine payable in Federal Reserve Notes.

St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co. v. Bjornson


NO. 12-90-00274-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


831 S.W.2d 366; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1178



April 24, 1992, delivered  
April 24, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 2ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. CHEROKEE COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment on verdict by the 2nd Judicial District Court of Cherokee County (Texas) that awarded appellee worker's compensation benefits on the basis that appellee was injured in the course of his employment on May 8, 1989, and that such injury produced total incapacity from said date until July 24, 1989, and partial incapacity from July 25, 1989 until July 25, 1993.


OVERVIEW: The trial court awarded appellee workers' compensation benefits for an injury that occurred in the course of his employment. The jury found for appellant insurer on its affirmative defense that appellee unjustifiably refused employment that was reasonably suited to his incapacity and physical condition and had been secured for him in the locality where he was injured. Appellant sought review, claiming that the trial court improperly entered a judgment on the jury's verdict by including an award of partial incapacity benefits during the period of unjustified refusal found by the jury. The court held that that there was ample evidence of probative value to support each element of the affirmative defense pleaded by appellant, and that it was reversible error under Tex. R. Civ. P. 301 for the trial court to disregard the jury's findings in regard to appellant's affirmative defense absent a motion to disregard a jury finding and/or render a judgment non obstante veredicto.The trial court judgment was reversed and set aside to the extent it awarded appellee workers' compensation benefits for the period in which the jury determined that he unjustifiably refused to return to work.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and set aside the trial court judgment to the extent that it awarded appellee worker's compensation benefits during the period of time in which the jury determined he had unjustifiably refused work, holding that the trial court abused its discretion by disregarding the jury's findings absent a motion to disregard or for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The case was remanded to for entry of appropriate judgment.

 

1505 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnican


NO. C14-91-00753-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


830 S.W.2d 215; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 964



April 16, 1992, rendered  
April 16, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the County Court No. 2. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90fd2199. Ronald L. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment from the County Court No. 2, Galveston County (Texas), which denied appellant reimbursement under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 14.062 for child support of appellee's child. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in construing Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.42(a) to bar collection of reimbursement for a period prior to the date of filing suit to establish paternity.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed and remanded a judgment denying appellant state's claim for retroactive child support reimbursement pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 14.062. The trial court construed Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.42(a) (statute) to restrict collection of retroactive support under § 14.062 to the date of filing of a suit to establish paternity. The court disagreed with this construction. Interpreting the statute in such a manner would lead to unconstitutional discrimination against illegitimate children because they would be denied support from their natural fathers that legitimate children received. Therefore, upon a finding of paternity, temporary orders for child support could be awarded retroactive to the date of filing of the petition, and upon final adjudication, the trial court could award child support retroactive to the time of birth. The judgment was reversed, child support reimbursement was awarded to appellant, and the cause was remanded for a determination of the amount of post-judgment interest and an appropriate amount of periodic or lump sum payments on that judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment denying appellant state reimbursement for child support of appellee's child for the time prior to the filing of the paternity suit. The court concluded that the trial court erred in construing a statute to bar such reimbursement because it would unconstitutionally deprive illegitimate children of support from their natural fathers.

 

1506 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. State


No. 05-91-01217-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


829 S.W.2d 894; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1347



April 16, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from County Criminal Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MB89-52627-E



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the County Criminal Court No. 4, Dallas County (Texas) for driving while intoxicated. Defendant claimed, among other things, that the state failed to establish probable cause to arrest him and, therefore, the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence of his intoxication.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for driving while intoxicated (DWI). The court affirmed the conviction. The court addressed only defendant's claim that the state failed to establish probable cause to arrest him and, therefore, the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence of his intoxication. Defendant was arrested after he was observed accelerating his car from a stop light to the point that the tires were unable to grab onto the pavement, thereby making a screeching noise burning off, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 185(a) (1977). The trial court concluded that because defendant was not in any "drag racing" type of competition at the time, section 185 did not apply. The court ruled that section 185 did apply to the case, and that defendant's warrantless arrest fell within one of the enumerated exceptions to the warrant requirement, in that he was observed while in the commission of a misdemeanor offense committed in his presence. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 14.01(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated. The arresting officer had probable cause to arrest defendant for violating the statute that barred the exhibition of acceleration; the trial court erred in holding that the statute did not apply. Thus, because both the initial stop of defendant and his subsequent arrest were lawful, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his intoxication.

 

1507 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Swinney v. Mosher


NO. 2-91-198-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


830 S.W.2d 187; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 966



April 14, 1992, Decided  
April 14, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 19, 1992. Attorney Ad Litem's Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 325TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Mary Sean O'Reilly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the 325th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), terminating her parental rights and appointing appellee adoptive parents as joint managing conservators of the child.


OVERVIEW: Appellee adoptive parents filed an action seeking termination of appellant birth mother's parental rights and an order of adoption. The trial court terminated appellant's rights and appointed appellees as joint managing conservators. Appellant sought review. The court reversed. The court held that appellant's actions in executing an affidavit of relinquishment of her parental rights, in accordance with her earlier decision to give up the child for adoption, did not constitute evidence under the abandonment statute of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.02(1)(A) (1992). Appellant was not disregarding her parental obligations, but was instead attempting to affirmatively provide for the child's welfare through others. To hold that her actions constituted abandonment would cause § 15.02(1)(A) to be unconstitutionally overbroad and a violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.03(d) applied to allow appellant to revoke the affidavit of relinquishment after the 60-day irrevocability clause had expired and before her parental rights were terminated. The court remanded for a determination as to conservatorship.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered in part and remanded in part the judgment of the trial court that terminated appellant birth mother's parental rights. The court also reversed the judgment of the trial court that terminated the father's parental rights. The court remanded for a determination of conservatorship of the child and attorney ad litem fees. The court found that execution of affidavit of relinquishment was not evidence of abandonment.

Shands v. State


No. A14-90-00844-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1282



April 14, 1992, Rendered  
April 14, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 284th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 569,131.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 284th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of two counts of tampering with a governmental record in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.10(a), (c) and sentencing him to four years probation. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and a charge to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, as superintendent of a school district, executed a document purporting to amend a lease/purchase agreement to a lease agreement for a climate control system. By doing so, he hoped to avoid questions about whether he had complied with statutory competitive bidding dictates required for purchase agreements. Defendant was convicted of two counts of tampering with a governmental record in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.10(a),(c). On appeal, the reviewing court rejected his claim that the state failed to prove that he acted with the specific intent to defraud or harm. The court found that a rational trier of fact reasonably could have concluded that defendant intended to defraud or harm the school district to protect himself and the district from being accused of violating the competitive bid statute. The court also rejected defendant's claim that a jury instruction unconstitutionally limited his mistake-of-fact defense to only mistakes formed through a reasonable belief. The court noted that the definition of reasonable belief incorporated a subjective element requiring the jury to consider the facts from defendant's perspective. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of tampering with a governmental record. The court found that a jury reasonably could have concluded that defendant intended to defraud or harm the school district. The court also found that the jury instruction requiring that any mistake in fact be formed through a reasonable belief was proper given the definition of reasonable belief.

 

1509 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Holloway v. Butler


NO. 01-91-00299-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


828 S.W.2d 810; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 910



April 9, 1992, rendered and delivered  
April 9, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 61st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 80-59586. SHEARN SMITH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing denied, Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff defamation litigant appealed an order from the 61st District Court, Harris County (Texas), denying his motion to retax costs and to enjoin a clerk's execution to collect court and appellate costs upon reversal of a judgment for plaintiff. Plaintiff claimed that the statute allowing for transcription costs, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 52.047 (1988), was unconstitutional and that there was insufficient evidence to support the award.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individual brought suit against defendant individuals for slander and libel. The appellate court reversed and rendered judgment that plaintiff take nothing. Defendant obtained a writ of execution upon plaintiff for court costs and transcription fees. Plaintiff brought a motion to retax costs and to enjoin the clerk from collecting the fees. The trial court denied the motion. Plaintiff appealed. Plaintiff claimed that the statute allowing for transcription costs, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 52.047 (1988), was unconstitutional because it was an improper delegation of legislative power. Plaintiff also claimed the fees were unsupported by the evidence and law. The court found that the constitutionality of trial court's setting fees for attorneys and guardians ad litem was unquestioned. The appellate court found little distinction between the setting of those fees and that for transcription. Thus, because the trial court set a reasonable fee, the fees were upheld. Because the transcription work was difficult and the fees were in line with fees charged by local court reporters, there was sufficient evidence to uphold the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of plaintiff defamation litigant's motion to retax costs and to enjoin a clerk's execution to collect court and appellate costs. Because the court found the setting of other attorney fees and the like was constitutional, transcription fees were held similarly constitutional. Because the fees were reasonable and in line with fees set by local court reporters, the fees were upheld.

Grimes v. Corpus Christi Transmission Co.


NUMBER 13-91-101-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


829 S.W.2d 335; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 979



April 9, 1992, delivered  
April 9, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion Withdrawn and Substituted February 6, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 348.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 319th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.

Original Opinion of February 6, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 348.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners brought a motion for rehearing, requesting that the court reconsider its judgment, which affirmed the trial court's order that granted summary judgment to appellee utility pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1436, § 1 (1951), in appellants' action for trespass or an unconstitutional taking of their property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee utility laid a gas pipeline beneath a highway right-of-way easement that had been granted to the state by appellant landowners' predecessor in title. Appellee received permission to lay this pipeline from the Texas Highway Department under the authority of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1436, § 1 (1951). Appellants brought an action against appellee for trespass or, alternatively, an unconstitutional taking of their property without just compensation. The trial court awarded summary judgment to appellee. On appeal, the court held that the grant of right-of-way for highway purposes included within that grant other compatible uses. The court held that state officials could authorize the use of the subsurface for pipelines that serve the public interest. The court held that appellee was covered by art. 1436, § 1, as a matter of law, because it established that it operated for a public use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order awarding summary judgment in favor of the appellee utility in appellant landowners trespass action concerning the gas pipeline appellee laid beneath a highway right-of-way easement. The legislature authorized the use of the subsurface of easements for a pipeline that served the public interest, and appellee operated for a public use.

Ramos v. State


No. 08-91-00174-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


831 S.W.2d 10; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 906



April 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Overruled June 3, 1992. Released for Publication July 13, 1992. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 171st District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 59895-171). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Honorable Peter S. Peca, Jr.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the 171st Judicial District Court of El Paso County (Texas), which convicted him for aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at 40 years' imprisonment, claiming that the court failed to properly instruct the jury during the penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at 40 years' imprisonment. The trial court failed to instruct the jury not to consider the extent or manner in which the parole law might affect the punishment assessed. During the jury's deliberation of the punishment stage, the jury sent a note to the trial court specifically requesting information on the percentage of time assessed as punishment which would actually have to be served before defendant would be eligible for parole. The trial court overruled defendant's objection that the jury should be instructed not to consider the effects of parole in their deliberations. The court reversed the judgment of punishment and remanded the case for a new punishment trial because the trial court should have given the jury a curative instruction when it became obvious that is was considering the effects of the parole law. The court concluded that the record did not establish beyond a reasonable doubt that the trial court's refusal to instruct the jury to disregard any parole law consideration did not contribute to the assessment of a 40-year sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court imposing punishment of 40 years' imprisonment, holding that the jury should have been given a curative instruction even though defendant had arguably waived any error by not requesting inclusion of that instruction at the time the jury charge was initially submitted.

Turner v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of felony possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, and assessed punishment at 45 years confinement with a $ 5,000 fine.

The case was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the case finding that a good conduct and parole instruction did not violate appellant's rights because it was authorized by statute and that a prior conviction was not facially void.

PUC OF TEXAS v. GTE-SW


NO. 3-90-084-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


833 S.W.2d 153; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1005



April 1, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 406,115, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 19, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1579.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part with Instructions


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants filed an appeal from a judgment of the 201st District Court of Travis County (Texas), which in a suit for judicial review authorized by the Public Utility Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, § 69 (Supp. 1992), affirmed in part and reversed in part a final order issued by the Public Utility Commission of Texas in a telecommunication rate proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellee applied to appellant commission, the Public Utility Commission of Texas, for an order increasing the rates it was permitted to charge its customers for intrastate telecommunication services. Five years later, after an intervening lawsuit, appellant commission ordered appellee to reduce its rates to diminish its annual revenues. Appellant commission purported to make the new rates retroactive two years by requiring refunds to customers through credits on future invoices. After a suit for judicial review and an appeal, the court rejected appellant commission's order and remanded, by affirming that part of the district court's judgment that reversed the required refund, and by reversing the district court's judgment to the extent it affirmed the order. The court found that appellant commission could not fix the effective date of appellee's rate retroactively. The court also found, among other things, that appellant commission failed to make the required subsidiary findings for each finding that appellee's payments to affiliates were reasonable and necessary, and erroneously calculated appellee's federal income-tax liability in estimating its operating expenses.


OUTCOME: The court rejected appellant commission's order and remanded, by affirming that part of the district court's judgment that reversed the order, and by reversing the district court's judgment to the extent it affirmed the order, because the court found, among other things, that appellant commission could not fix the effective date of appellee's rate retroactively, and failed to make certain required findings.

Chavez v. Hannah


NO. 3-91-182-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


827 S.W.2d 100; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1255



April 1, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 6, 1992. Released for Publication May 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 494,841, HONORABLE F. SCOTT MCCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant write-in candidate and voters sought review of a judgment of the 147th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), finding for appellee county, which refused to count write-in votes for appellant based on his failure declare himself a write-in candidate for justice of the peace as required by Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 146.025 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant write-in candidate and voters sued appellee county when appellee refused to count votes for appellant candidate because appellant candidate had not registered according to the requirements under Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 146.022-.023, .024(2), .025(A), .029, and .031 (1992). The trial court found for appellee. The court affirmed, finding that requiring write-in candidates to register with the county 60 days before the general election was constitutional, because the state legislature had many legitimate interests in formulating election policies and the statutes at issue only required the candidates to register 15 days before early voting began. Texas' due process requirements were not violated. The limited, if any, impingement of the right to vote, combined with the legitimacy of the state's interests, compelled the court to uphold the constitutionality of those provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellee count properly refused to count appellant candidate's write-in votes, because the statutes requiring registration of write-in candidates were constitutional, in that they significantly furthered legitimate state goals.

Medina v. State


Appeal No. 04-91-00329-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


828 S.W.2d 268; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1167



March 31, 1992, Delivered  
March 31, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 187th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 90-CR-1754-A. Honorable Pat Priest, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 187th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) which convicted him of murder and attempted murder. Appellant contended on appeal that the trial court had erred by refusing to allow appellant to impeach the complainant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and of attempted murder. The court affirmed. The court overruled appellant's fourth point of error, which asserted that the trial court erred by denying appellant the opportunity to impeach the complainant and by not permitting appellant to show that complainant had "malice " toward appellant and had a malevolent motivation to testify against appellant. Appellant, after the state had rested, attempted to show through another witness that complainant, who testified against appellant on direct examination, "always carried a pistol." Appellant contended that complainant testified at trial that he never carried a gun. Complainant's cousin testified that complainant's reputation in the community for truth and veracity was bad. The court held that under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 608(b) the trial court properly sustained the state's objection to the cousin's testimony regarding whether she ever saw complainant carrying a gun. The trial court's instructions on parole and good conduct time were not unconstitutional. Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37, on which the trial court had based its jury instructions, did not constitute an ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for murder and attempted murder because the trial court did not err in denying appellant the opportunity to impeach the complainant where the complainant did not make a general statement that he never carried a gun.
