Dannelley v. Almond


NO. C14-91-00747-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


827 S.W.2d 582; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 799



March 26, 1992, Rendered  
March 26, 1992, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law and Probate Court Number One. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 183022. Anthony Willy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant common-law wife sought review of an order from the County Court at Law and Probate Court Number One, Brazoria County (Texas), granting appellee mother's summary judgment motion and dismissing a plea in intervention in a probate matter. Appellant claimed summary judgment was improper because Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 1.91(b) was unconstitutional and violated equal protection and an open courts provision, Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3 and 13.


OVERVIEW: Appellant common-law wife and her husband were divorced. The husband later died. Appellant filed an affidavit of heirship. Appellee mother filed an application to determine heirship, alleging that the decedent fathered her two sons. Appellant brought a plea in intervention, contending she was married to the decedent at the time of his death and denying appellee's paternity claims. Appellee brought a partial summary judgment motion to dismiss the plea. The trial court granted the motion, finding appellant lacked standing. Appellant sought review, claiming a one-year statute of limitations period to establish an informal marriage under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 1.91(b) (1991) violated the state constitution's equal protection and open courts provisions. The appellate court affirmed. Because the state had a legitimate and reasonable interest in requiring claimants to timely prove the existence of alleged informal marriages in order to facilitate divorce and probate proceedings, the statute did not violate equal protection or the open courts provision. Because appellant failed to comply with the statute, she was precluded from claiming as an heir.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's grant of appellee mother's partial summary judgment motion and denial of appellant's common-law wife's plea in intervention in a probate matter to determine heirship. Appellant's failure to timely establish her informal marriage to decedent precluded her from claiming as an heir. Thus, appellee was allowed to claim her sons, fathered by decedent, as heirs to his estate.

Dyke v. State


NO. B14-90-00437-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 845



March 26, 1992, rendered  
March 26, 1992, filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 483,890



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted her of the felony offense of possession of less than 28 grams of methamphetamine and sentenced her to 10 years in prison, probated.


OVERVIEW: A police officer received a tip from a reliable informant that defendant was about to leave an apartment to deliver some drugs. Officers in a marked police car followed defendant, pulled her over, and noticed that defendant leaned over to the floorboard of the passenger seat. An officer conducted a search of the car, and found a bag containing drugs on the floorboard. Defendant was convicted of the felony offense of possession of less than 28 grams of methamphetamine. On appeal, defendant argued that the search of her vehicle was unconstitutional because it was conducted without a warrant. However, the court found that the police received a tip from a reliable informant regarding defendant's unlawful possession and sale of drugs, which validated the search of the car incident to the arrest. Defendant's argument that the trial court committed reversible error in denying the disclosure of the informant was without merit because the argument was not properly preserved for review. Furthermore, the burden was on defendant to show that the informant's identity was material to the defense of her case, which she failed to do. The decision of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision that convicted defendant of possession of less than 28 grams of methamphetamine was affirmed because the police had information from a reliable informant that defendant was about to sell drugs, which gave the police probable cause to search defendant's car incident to her arrest.

Taylor v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 174th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of cocaine following a jury verdict and enhanced his sentence following his plea of true to one enhancement paragraph of the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought relief from his conviction of delivery of cocaine. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that appellant did not raise the issue of improper proof of character on allegation of improper impeachment of his niece because the trial objection differed from the complaint made on appeal; therefore, no error was preserved for review. OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant offender's conviction for delivery of cocaine, finding that appellant failed to preserve error on his allegation of improper proof of character, that the jury charge's mandatory parole law instruction was constitutional, and that appellee state's reference to a prior parole was not improper because its implication was admitted through the pen packet.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:

Hemphill v. State


NO. B14-90-01120-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON

March 5, 1992, Rendered  
March 5, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 56th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89CR1615. H. G. Dalehite, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 56th District Court, Galveston County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a) (1983). Appellant contended that the trial court committed error when it admitted a videotape of the child's testimony under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of a conviction for aggravated sexual assault, pursuant to Tex. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071 (1989), and the outcry statements of the victim. Appellant also contended that the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction. Appellant's objections to the outcry statements of the victim were insufficient to preserve the issue for appeal. Finally, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault, finding that the trial court did not commit fundamental error by admitting into evidence a videotape of the victim's prior testimony. Appellant failed preserve for appeal his objections to the outcry statements of the victim, and the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction.

State v. Jimenez


No. 08-91-00095-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


828 S.W.2d 455; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 550



March 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law #2 of Midland County, Texas. (TC# 52,379). Trial Court Judge: James Fitz-Gerald, III


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the County Court at Law of Midland County (Texas), granting appellee's motion to dismiss the information charging appellee with unlawfully, intentionally, and knowingly damaging, defacing, and mutilating the United States flag in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.14. The trial court ruled the statute was unconstitutional and dismissed the information against appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.14 with unlawfully, intentionally, and knowingly damaging, defacing, and mutilating the flag of the United States of America. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss the information. The trial court ruled the statute prohibiting destruction of the flag was unconstitutional. The trial court determined that it was bound to follow the mandate of precedent involving a similar statute. Finding Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.14 similarly flawed, the trial court ruled it unconstitutional and dismissed the information. The state contended that the strong presumption in favor of constitutionality of statutes was not rebutted by appellee's argument and that the flag represented a symbol of national history and unity worthy of protection through the exercise of proper police power of the state. The appellate court affirmed the decision because it was bound to follow the decisions of all higher courts in their interpretation of the laws. Thus, the assailed statute was held impermissibly violative of an individual's freedom of expression.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting appellee's motion to dismiss the information charging appellee with unlawfully, intentionally, and knowingly damaging, defacing, and mutilating the United States flag. The trial court properly ruled the penal statute was unconstitutional; thus, the information filed by the state against appellee was correctly dismissed.

Fanning v. Fanning


No. 10-90-112-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


828 S.W.2d 135; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 718



March 4, 1992, delivered  
March 4, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] From the 19th District Court. McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 88-4480-1



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a divorce proceeding, appellant husband sought review of a decision from the 19th District Court, McLennan County (Texas), which granted the final decree and which awarded the majority of the assets and custody of the children to appellee wife.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband and appellee wife executed a premarital agreement prior to marriage. After the marriage began to fail, appellant had appellee sign a second partition agreement. The parties petitioned for divorce, and the trial court granted a final decree which awarded the majority of the assets and the custody of the children to appellee. Appellant sought review and contended that the trial court erred when it failed to enforce the premarital agreement, when it failed to enforce the second partition agreement, and when it awarded custody and child support to appellee. The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part. The court reversed the trial court's invalidation of the premarital agreement because the majority of the agreement was not contrary to Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 15 and because the portion that was invalid was severable. The court affirmed as to the second partition agreement, finding that it was unconscionable when it was executed because of the circumstances that surrounded the execution. The court affirmed the child support and custody award because the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support the award.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's invalidation of the premarital agreement because the invalid portion was severable. The court affirmed the invalidation of a second partition agreement because it was unconscionable when executed. The court affirmed the child support award because it was supported by the evidence.

 

1525 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Shoberg v. Shoberg


NO. B14-91-00473-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 505



February 27, 1992, Rendered  
February 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Granted May 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 165th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-54269. Kenneth Harrison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged an order from the 165th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that granted appellee husband summary judgment and allowed appellee to foreclose on the homestead because appellant failed to make any payments on a promissory note pursuant to an agreement, which was incorporated in to the final divorce decree, in return for appellee giving up his interest in the homestead.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife and appellee husband entered into an agreement, which was incorporated into the final divorce decree, that required appellant to execute a promissory note and deed of trust in favor of appellee, and appellee in turn to convey his undivided one-half interest in the homestead to appellant. When appellant failed to make any payments on the note, appellee sought to foreclose by forced sale of the homestead. The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of appellee. The agreement constituted a valid and binding final judgment that precluded appellant from raising a claim under Tex. Const. art. 16, § 50. While § 50 protected the homestead from a forced sale for payment of all debts, it allowed a lien placed on the residence to secure a payment by appellant to appellee for the value of appellee's homestead interest. The interest rate on the promissory note was not usurious under Tex. R. Civ. P. 93(11) because interest on past due interest was not usurious. Further, even assuming that appellant's forbearing from seeking child support constituted a charge under the usury statutes, the amount of child support was too speculative to make a usury determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee husband because appellant wife could not collaterally attack an agreement incorporated into the final divorce decree, and in any event the agreement neither violated the Texas constitution's protections against a forced sale of the marital home upon a former spouse's lien, nor charged usurious interest.

OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with robbery but was found not competent to stand trial, sent to a mental health facility, found competent, returned to stand trial, and again found not competent but was not subsequently returned to a mental health facility for treatment. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus after he was charged with robbery, because appellant did not present a sufficient record for review, provided no evidence to show that he was denied admittance into a mental health facility, and should have pursued other remedies.

Smallwood v. State


NO. 01-90-00511-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


827 S.W.2d 34; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 518



February 27, 1992, Rendered and Delivered  
February 27, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 553,224



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for third degree felony theft of property having a value of less than $ 750, pursuant to the third offender provision. Appellant was assessed punishment as a habitual offender. Appellant was arrested for shoplifting three packages of meat having a combined value of less than $ 30, normally a class B misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for third degree felony theft of property having a value of less than $ 750, pursuant to the third offender provision. Appellant was assessed punishment as a habitual offender. Appellant was arrested for shoplifting meat having a value of less than $ 30, normally a class B misdemeanor, which was upgraded to a third degree felony when the value of the property stolen was less than $ 750 and the offender had been convicted two or more times of any grade of theft. The court held that the enhancements did not violate due process or double jeopardy. Appellant was properly charged, and the state was entitled to enhance appellant's punishment, as long as the offenses were prior felony convictions for nontheft offenses. Since appellant had the possibility of parole and good time credits, and he had been incarcerated five times and had nine felony convictions, the court held that his punishment was not cruel and unusual. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Since appellant had been incarcerated five times and had nine felony convictions, and as there was a possibility of parole and good time credits, his punishment was not cruel and unusual. The court held that sentencing enhancements were properly applied.

Mayfield v. State

1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 520



February 27, 1992, Rendered  
February 27, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

Appellant raised points of trial error including denial of his motion to suppress the fruits of his allegedly illegal detention, the frisk and search of his person and the truck.

The court found that appellant's detention was legal, based on reasonable suspicion of surrounding circumstances and probable cause of criminal activity. The court found evidence could be admitted when the officer took reasonable measures to protect from a possible threat of physical harm.

Zarsky v. State


NUMBER 13-91-111-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


827 S.W.2d 408; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 443



February 20, 1992, Delivered  
February 20, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled March 26, 1992. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3 of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the County Court at Law No. 3 of Nueces County, Texas, which convicted him of criminal trespass. Appellant contended that his conviction violated the free-speech and assembly provisions of the United States and Texas constitutions, that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, and that the trial court erred in failing to submit his requested instructions to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for criminal trespass. Appellant asserted that his conviction violated the free-speech and assembly provisions of the United States and Texas constitutions, that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction, and that the trial court erred in excluding evidence and failing to submit his requested instructions to the jury. The court concluded there was no first amendment protection for appellant's activities because the complex had not assumed the functional attributes of public property devoted to public use. The court determined there was sufficient evidence to support appellant's conviction because he was prosecuted for remaining on the property after being notified to leave. The court held that appellant was not entitled to the mistake of fact charge requested because appellant believed he was not trespassing because the location was a public place which was a mistake of law rather than a mistake of fact. The court concluded that appellant's mistaken belief did not negate the culpability required for trespass and he was not entitled to a mistake of fact charge. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because there was no first amendment protection for appellant's activities because the complex had not assumed the functional attributes of a public property devoted to public use. The court held that appellant's mistaken belief had not negated the culpability required for trespass therefore the trial court's refusal to give a mistake of fact charge was proper.

Newsome v. State


No. 05-87-00276-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


829 S.W.2d 260; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1250



February 19, 1992, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 291st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F86-92820-LU



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 291st Judicial District Court. Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment, enhanced by one prior felony conviction.


OVERVIEW: In this appeal, appellant challenged his conviction alleging improper use of peremptory challenges by the prosecutor and improper jury instructions. Appellant alleged the prosecutor had used his peremptory challenges to discriminate on the basis of race and he requested a copy of the prosecutor's handwritten note made in preparation for his testimony at the first Batson hearing on the issue. The court held that the prosecutor's notes were not a "statement" by a witness, subject to discovery. The court also held that it was appellant's responsibility to be sure the notes and been sealed and included in the record for review. Appellant failed to do so. The prosecutor was allowed to make peremptory strikes based on his legitimate hunch, so long as it was not racially motivated. Appellant failed to meet his burden of proving discrimination. Appellant argued the trial court erred in not sustaining his objection to the court's jury instruction on the law of parole, because the statute authorizing it had been declared unconstitutional. The court found the instruction did not contribute to appellant's punishment and the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which convicted and punished appellant for aggravated sexual assault because he failed to meet his burden of proving the prosecutor had used his strikes in a racially motivated way, that he was entitled to see the prosecutor's Batson hearing notes, or that the jury instruction on the law of parole contributed to his punishment.

Madison v. State


NO. 01-90-00962-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


825 S.W.2d 202; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 327



February 6, 1992, Rendered  
February 6, 1992 Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 561,648. Don Humble, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas) that convicted him of delivery of cocaine. Appellant complained that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction and that the trial court erred in instructing the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1992), that they could consider good conduct time and parole in determining his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Finding that the state presented adequate chain of custody evidence to link appellant to the cocaine police bought from him, and rebuffing appellant's constitutional challenge to the charge on good conduct time and parole, the court affirmed the conviction. The court emphasized that objections concerning chain of custody went to the weight rather than the admissibility of evidence. The identification of the cocaine and police testimony about it were sufficient to permit the trier of fact to find this element beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the trial court properly instructed the jury at the penalty phase under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1992) that it could "consider" parole and good conduct time in setting appellant's sentence. There was no material difference between permitting the jury to consider these factors, and the constitutional basis for this instruction, Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a), which authorized courts to "inform" juries of these factors. Furthermore, § 11(a) was itself constitutional, and did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 13, 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for delivery of cocaine. The court found sufficient evidence of chain of custody to sustain the verdict. The court also held that a statutory charge that the jury could consider parole and good conduct time when assessing sentence was authorized by the constitution and that this authorization was in itself constitutional.

Grimes v. Corpus Christi Transmission Co.


NUMBER 13-91-101-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 348



February 6, 1992, Delivered  
February 6, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 16, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 979. Second Rehearing Overruled May 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 319th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the decision of the 319th District Court, Nueces County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee utilities in a suit brought by appellants for trespass related to the construction of a gas pipeline under a highway when the original right-of-way grant was limited to highway purposes. Appellees sought the award of attorney fees from the court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owners held fee title to the middle of a state highway abutting their property, which was on a right-of-way that was expressly limited to the construction and maintenance of a permanent road. Appellants brought suit for trespass when appellee utilities built a gas pipeline under the highway. Appellants challenged the trial court's denial of its summary judgment motion and the grant of appellees' summary judgment motion. Appellees sought an award of attorney fees. The court noted that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1436b, § 1, allowed any person engaged in transportation of gas for public consumption to build gas pipelines within a highway right-of-way. The court determined that appellees were engaged in the required activities. Accordingly, the grant of summary judgment to appellees was affirmed. With regard to appellees' request for attorney fees, the court found that the request had not been made, nor was proof of the requested fees submitted, with the motion for summary judgment. As a result, the court overruled appellees' request since it was not presented to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed because, under applicable statutes, appellee utilities operated for public use and were, therefore, permitted to use the state's highway right-of-way for the attendant purpose of transporting gas through construction of a pipeline under the highway. Appellees' request for attorney fees, however, was denied because it had not been presented to the trial court with the motion for summary judgment.

Petition for discretionary review refused by, 04/15/1992
Appeal after remand at Yu Chi Chuang v. State, 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 3315 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., June 26, 1997)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Ex parte Pan Yaw Chen, 2015 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 742 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 14, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 559,677 and 559,676

On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No 550,496



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged their conviction of unlawful redemption of food stamps, from the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), arguing that the statute under which they were convicted, Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann § 33.011(b) (1990), was unconstitutionally vague pursuant to both the U.S. and Texas Constitutions and that it was error for the lower court to have failed to admonish appellants regarding their non-citizenship status.

Code Ann. § 33.011(b) (1990), was unconstitutionally vague under the U.S. and Texas Constitutions and that the lower court erred in failing to admonish them as to the consequences of guilty pleas entered by non-citizens. Accordingly, the court held that it could not rule on the merits of appellants' pre-trial motions to quash the indictment. The court further held that the lower court did not commit reversible error as the record did not reflect any objection to the omission of admonishments regarding appellant's citizenship, nor any evidence that appellants were misled or harmed by the absence of such admonishments.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed because the issues of constitutionality of the statute in question were not preserved for review, and because the failure of the lower court to admonish appellants regarding the effect of their non-citizen status on their guilty pleas was harmless error.

State v. Garcia


Appeal No. 04-90-00319-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


823 S.W.2d 793; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 672



January 31, 1992, Delivered  
January 31, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellees' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 438,819. Honorable Timothy F. Johnson, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: CAUSE REMANDED AND DISMISSAL ORDER SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed an order from County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County (Texas) dismissing complaint charging appellee with owning or operating a sexually oriented commercial enterprise outside the corporate limits of a city. The trial court found the violation was unconstitutionally vague, unreasonable, and overbroad. The prosecution argued trial court erred in granting appellee's motion to dismiss the prosecution's pleadings.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution appealed an order dismissing complaint which charged appellee with offense of owning or operating a sexually oriented commercial enterprise outside a city. The trial court found the violation was unconstitutionally vague, unreasonable, and overbroad. The court held a facial challenge to a legislative act, ordinance or order was difficult, since the challenger must establish that no set of circumstances existed under which the act, ordinance or order would be valid. In a facial challenge to the overbreadth and vagueness of a law, a court determined whether enactment reached a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. The court should then examine the facial vagueness challenge and, assuming the enactment implicated no constitutionally protected conduct, should uphold the challenge only if enactment was impermissibly vague. Further, an attack as being overboard was reserved for complaints concerning U.S. Const. amend. I violations. The court held that an ordinance was not invalid merely because it subjected the commercial exploitation of materials protected by the U.S. Const. amend. I to licensing or zoning requirements.


OUTCOME: The cause was remanded and the dismissal order was set aside in appeal by the prosecution from dismissal of its complaint against appellee for owning or operating a sexually oriented commercial enterprise outside a city. The court held the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.

Harding v. State


NO. 01-90-00994-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


822 S.W.2d 817; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 240



January 30, 1992, Delivered and Rendered  
January 30, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 209th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 427327. Hollis D. Harmon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the 209th District Court for Harris County (Texas) for aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of aggravated robbery and he was sentenced to 60 years' imprisonment. The court of appeals reversed the conviction for error during the punishment phase of the trial. Prior to the state's petition for discretionary review, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.29(b) was passed. The rule provided that when an error occurred during the punishment phase of trial, on remand, the matter was to be treated as though a defendant's guilt was already established. Appellant's punishment phase was retried and he was sentenced to 80 years' imprisonment. The court of appeals affirmed. Contrary to appellant's assertion, the rule was not a violation of the ex post facto prohibition in U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9 and 10. The rule merely affected the mode procedure and not appellant's substantive rights. No ex post facto violation occurred if the law was merely procedural.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery was affirmed because the trial judge was not required to retry the entirety of the case when the error causing reversal occurred during the punishment phase of trial.

Hansel v. State


NO. 01-91-00128-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 256



January 30, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 230th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 507,687



DISPOSITION: Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the conviction entered on a deferred adjudication of guilt by the 230th District Court of Harris County (Texas) for a sexual assault on a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for sexual assault on a child and entered a guilty plea. The trial court deferred adjudication and placed him on probation. A motion to adjudicate guilt was filed when appellant was alleged to have committed another sexual assault on a child. The trial court found appellant had violated the terms and conditions of his probation by committing a subsequent offense of sexual assault on a minor and adjudicated appellant guilty. Appellant asserted that the trial court erroneously adjudicated his guilt on the basis that the new allegation of sexual assault was not proven by sufficient evidence. Further, appellant asserted that the trial court adjudicated his guilt based upon improper use of extraneous offense evidence. The court held that, under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 42.12, § 5(b), no appeal could be taken from the trial court's decision to adjudicate. If final adjudication was deferred, the decision to finally enter judgment was not reviewable. The remainder of the proceedings were subject to ordinary review. Therefore, the court lacked authority to review appellant's points of error. The appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction because appellant's points of error related to the trial court's decision to adjudicate guilt on a deferred adjudication on appellant's guilty plea to sexual assault on a child, but the trial court's decision to adjudicate was not appealable.

 

1539 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hoang v. State


NO. C14-90-01017-CR, NO. C14-90-01020-CR, NO. C14-90-01023-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


825 S.W.2d 729; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 167



January 23, 1992, Rendered  
January 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 230th District Court, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 559685, 559686 & 562812



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant store employee challenged a conviction from the 230th District Court, Texas, for unauthorized redemption of food stamps based upon complaints that the trial court erred by overruling appellant's motion to quash the indictment, that appellant was denied his constitutional right to a trial by jury, and that appellant had ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant store employee on different occasions redeemed food stamps from an undercover police officer for cash only, contrary to Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 33.011(b) (1990). The court affirmed appellant's conviction for unauthorized redemption of food stamps. Section 33.011(b) was not unconstitutionally vague where its language specifically prohibited redeeming food stamps for cash only and appellant signed an authorization application that verified that appellant read and understood 7 C.F.R. § 278.2 (1989) which also proscribed redeeming food stamps for cash only. Appellant was not denied a right to a jury trial where in open court and in writing with the consent of the court, the prosecution, and after discussing the pros and cons of waiver, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.13 (1977), appellant waived jury trial. Appellant's counsel was not ineffective regarding appellant's waiver of jury trial where counsel testified that he informed appellant of the right to a jury trial. Counsel was also not ineffective for failing to call witnesses at the punishment phase of trial where there was no proof that witnesses were available or their testimony could aid appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant store employee's conviction for unauthorized redemption of food stamps because the statute which proscribed redeeming food stamps for cash only was not vague, therefore appellant's motion to quash was properly denied. Appellant was not denied a right to jury trial because appellant waived a jury trial in writing in open court, and appellant's counsel did not render ineffective assistance.

Wilson v. State


No. 05-89-01481-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


825 S.W.2d 155; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 696



January 22, 1992, Filed and Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 282nd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F89-71729-PS



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 282nd District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of unlawful delivery of a simulated controlled substance. Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.06 was unconstitutional because it allowed the state to allege that an offense occurred in one county and to prove that it occurred in another county.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of unlawful delivery of a simulated controlled substance. Appellant argued that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.06, which allowed the state to allege that an offense occurred in one county but prove that it occurred in another county, was unconstitutional. The court held that art. 21.06 did not violate appellant's right under U.S. Const. amend. VI to be informed of the nature of the accusation against him because the location of the offense was not an element of the offense charged. The court also concluded that the indictment was not unconstitutionally misleading because appellant received adequate notice of his alleged criminal acts. The court held that appellant had constructive notice that he would have to defend against proof that the offense occurred outside the prosecuting county's boundaries. The court ruled that the indictment sufficiently apprised appellant of the offense he was to defend against and did not violate his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. V.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for unlawful delivery of a simulated controlled substance. The court held that the indictment that averred that the offense was committed in a different county than was proven at trial did not violate appellant's constitutional right to be informed of the nature of the accusation against him and was not misleading.

State v. Toone


No. 05-91-00414-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


823 S.W.2d 744; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 458



January 17, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied March 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 199th Judicial District Court. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 199-80110-90


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged judgment of the 199th Judicial District Court, Collin County (Texas), which granted appellee individuals' motion to suppress evidence of cocaine possession obtained while a federal search warrant was being executed, on the ground that the an anticipatory search warrant was not per se invalid and that a federal warrant permitted introduction of the evidence even if it violated state law.


OVERVIEW: Appellee individual was investigated by federal authorities that thought he might have child pornography. They obtained a search warrant and in the course of executing it discovered cocaine. Appellee was charged under state law with that offense. The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress which asserted that officers seized the cocaine in violation of state statutory laws as well as both the United States and the Texas Constitutions. Appellant state sought review of the adverse ruling, arguing that the suppression was erroneous. In reversing the decision of the trial court, the court held that anticipatory language in the warrant that contraband "would be" at the specified location did not invalidate the warrant; and evidence lawfully obtained by federal officers acting under a valid federal search warrant was admissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's suppression order and remanded the cause to the trial court because an anticipatory warrant was not per se invalid and evidence obtained under a valid federal search warrant was admissible in a state case even if it would not be under state law.

Decker v. Lindsay


NO. 01-91-01299-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


824 S.W.2d 247; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 210



January 15, 1992, Delivered  
January 15, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Original Proceeding on Petition for Writ of Mandamus



DISPOSITION: Petition for Writ of Mandamus conditionally granted


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators husband and wife sought mandamus relief against respondent judge of the 280th District Court, Harris County (Texas), who ordered that their negligence action against the real party in interest be submitted to mediation under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 154.021(a) (Supp. 1992).


OVERVIEW: Respondent judge ordered relators husband and wife to mediate under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 154.021(a) (Supp. 1992), their negligence action against the real party in interest. Relators sought mandamus relief, and the court conditionally granted the petition, finding that respondent's order was void insofar as it directed relators to negotiate in good faith a resolution of their dispute through mediation, despite their objections. The court found that a trial court was authorized to refer a dispute to an alternative dispute resolution on its own motion under § 154.021(a); however, if a party objected, and there was a reasonable basis for the objection, under Tex. Civ. Rev. Code Ann. § 154.022(c) (Supp. 1992), the trial court may not order the parties to mediate. The court found that the trial court's order requiring the parties to negotiate in good faith and attempt to reach a settlement did not comport with the legislative intent to compel referral, but not resolution.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted relators husband and wife's petition for writ of mandamus and ordered respondent judge to vacate those portions of the order requiring relators and the real party in interest to participate in mediation. The court would issue the writ only in the event that respondent failed to comply.

Harris County v. White


Case No. 06-91-00040-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


823 S.W.2d 385; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 102



January 14, 1992, Decided  
January 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant s Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 61st Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 85-49658


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment from the 61st Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), entered in favor of appellee beneficiaries in their suit under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.002, et seq. (1986 & Supp. 1992), and the wrongful death statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.002, et seq. (1986).


OVERVIEW: Decedent inmate was killed when appellant county's sheriff's department van overturned. Appellee beneficiaries brought suit against appellant under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.002, et seq. (1986 & Supp. 1992), and the wrongful death statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.002, et seq. (1986). The trial court reduced the jury awards to individual appellees to not more than $ 100,000 each. On review, the court found that Tort Claims Act limited appellant's liability for damages for bodily injury or death to $ 100,000 for each person and $ 300,000 for each occurrence. Appellant contended that the phrase "each person" referred only to the person who was physically injured or killed, and because appellees claimed loss because of the death of one person, their recovery was limited to an aggregate of $ 100,000. The court found that appellant's total liability was limited to $ 100,000, apportioned among appellees pro rata. Accordingly, the judgment was modified to establish a pro rata recovery. As modified, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment entered in favor of appellee beneficiaries was modified to reduce their recovery the statutory limit of $ 100,000 and apportion appellant county's liability on a pro rata basis. As modified, the judgment was affirmed.

Morris v. State


No. 08-91-00237-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


823 S.W.2d 695; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 46



January 8, 1992, Decided  
January 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 70th District Court of Ector County, Texas. (TC# A-86,698). Gene Ater, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bond sureties sought review of a bail bond forfeiture judgment of the 70th District Court, Ector County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant bail bond sureties provided bond for the release of defendant principal. When defendant principal failed to appear for a pretrial hearing, a judgment nisi was entered, followed by a judgment for the total amount of the bond. The trial court took judicial knowledge that defendant principal was again released on another bond in the same cause, signed by someone else, and made subsequent to the judgment nisi forfeiture. Appellants unsuccessfully requested a remittitur, and challenged the judgment. The court reversed, holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(a)(3) (1989) complied with the general rule of law that bail will be discharged where new bail is given for the future appearance of the accused on the same charge. The court also found that the unconstitutionality of the mandated judgment delays in art. 22.16(c) did not render the entire statute unconstitutional as Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 54.01 (1979) provided for a severability clause in the event that a portion of the legislative act was declared invalid.


OUTCOME: The bail bond forfeiture judgment was reversed because the applicable statute complies with the general rule of law that bail would be discharged where new bail was given for the future appearance of the accused on the same charge.

Weaver v. State


No. 05-90-01277-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


823 S.W.2d 371; 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 450



January 6, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 203rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F89-67924-P



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 203rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), convicting him of aggravated assault and assessing punishment of three years and a $ 1,000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated assault and he sought review. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not err in failing to find unconstitutional, under U.S. Const. amend VI or Tex. Const. art. 1, § 3, the statutory exemption from jury service for persons over 65 years of age of Tex. Gov't Code § 62.106 (1988). The court found that appellant failed to show that persons over 65 were a distinctive group with some common thread of shared experience or political, social, or religious viewpoint. The court found that even if persons over 65 were held to constitute a distinctive group, appellant failed to establish the fair cross-section requirement that the percentage of the community made up of the group was underrepresented. The court found that age was not a suspect classification requiring strict scrutiny under an equal protection analysis, and because the age-based classification was based upon a reasonable and substantial classification of persons and was rationally related to its objective, it was constitutionally permissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated assault, finding that the statutory exemption from jury service for persons over 65 years of age was constitutional.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partner sought review of an order from the 152nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which dismissed appellant's cause of action regarding ownership of the land in question, and resulting and constructive trusts, granted appellee partners' motion for instructed verdict, withdrew appellant's case from the jury, and rendered judgment that appellant take nothing.

Appellant contended that the partnership owned the land and sued appellee partners for breach of fiduciary duty. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in dismissing his cause of action regarding ownership of the land and constructive and resulting trusts. The court reversed the judgment. OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which dismissed appellant partner's cause of action regarding ownership of the land in question, and resulting and constructive trusts. The court found no support in the law or in the record for dismissal of the ownership and resulting and constructive trust theories of recovery against appellee partners for failure to join a third party with a one-sixth mineral interest in the property.

Dallas v. Dallas Merchants & Concessionaires Ass'n


No. 05-91-00449-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


823 S.W.2d 347; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3238



December 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 31, 1992. Application for Writ of Error Granted June 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 134th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-7493-G



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review from the 134th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which issued a declaratory judgment in favor of appellee store owners and an injunction on the ground that an ordinance which zoned the location of alcohol-related businesses was unconstitutional. Appellant argued error in finding the ordinance in conflict with the code and in failing to find legislative validation of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellee store owners owned and operated stores which sold alcohol. Appellant city passed an ordinance which zoned the location of alcohol-related businesses which adversely affected appellees. Appellees sought and were granted declaratory judgment and an injunction on the ground that the ordinance was unconstitutional. Appellant sought review and asserted the trial court erred in finding the ordinance in conflict with the code, failing to find that the Texas Legislature validated the ordinance, allowing and finding standing for intervention, and failing to require a supersedeas bond. On review, the court found that the ordinance did not preempt appellant's power to zone the location of alcohol-related businesses. Further, the ordinance was within appellant's home-rule power as a city and was a valid exercise of appellant's police power. Thus, the trial court erred when it held that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court then determined that the other arguments did not need to be reviewed due to these initial findings. The court concluded that the ordinance was facially constitutional and reversed the trial court's judgment accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment and injunction issued by the trial court in favor of appellee store owners because the ordinance was facially constitutional and the ordinance was within appellant city's home-rule power as a municipality and was a valid exercise of appellant's police power.

Dallas Market Center Dev. Co. v. Beran & Shelmire


No. 05-91-00372-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


824 S.W.2d 218; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3272



December 20, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 116th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-01700-F



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant development company challenged a judgment of the 116th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, engineering, contracting, and masonry companies, in a suit sounding in breaches of contract, warranties, negligence, and fraudulent concealment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant development company brought suit against appellees, engineering, contracting, and masonry companies, for breach of contract and warranty, negligence, and fraudulent concealment arising out of defects in a recently constructed hotel. Appellees were overseeing the construction project. The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment based on 10-year statutes of repose, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 16.008-.009. Appellant challenged the grant of summary judgment, arguing that the statutes of repose did not bar contract claims, and the court affirmed. With the statutes of repose, the time period began running when the improvement was substantially completed rather than when a cause of action accrued. The court held that the statutes of repose did prevent appellant's contract claims. The court deferred to the legislative recognition of the vulnerability to lawsuits of building professionals and contractors. The court also held that appellant's affirmative defense of fraudulent concealment did not apply to the statute of repose to extend appellant's time for filing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, engineering, contracting, and masonry companies, because the applicable statutes of repose barred appellant development company's contract claims. The court also held that appellant's defense of fraudulent concealment was inapplicable to the statute of repose.

Turner v. State


NO. A14-89-00835-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3191



December 19, 1991, Rendered  
December 19, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 450,479



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 337th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of capital murder pursuant to an intentional killing in the course of a robbery under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant killed a cashier while attempting to rob a convenience store. The court affirmed appellant's conviction of capital murder for an intentional killing in the course of a robbery under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1989). Appellant's right to due process and right to a trial by jury were not violated under U.S. Const. amend. V and Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 10,19 because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.04 was not unconstitutional since it was based on sound public policy that allowing intoxication to negate intent would excuse the commission of a crime by a person who voluntarily ingested alcohol or drugs and then felt free to violate the law. Appellant failed to make a prima facie case of purposeful discrimination by the state in its exercise of peremptory challenges because the record contained sufficient nonracial reasons for all three peremptory strikes. A juror who said that he would make sure appellant got a fair trial and that he would meet his civic responsibility did not demonstrate an abuse of discretion on the part of the trial court by not dismissing him. The words "know" and "wrong" did not need to be defined for the jury because they were easily understand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant for capital murder and held that the voluntary intoxication statute was constitutional based on public policy and the compelling interest of protecting citizens because evidence of voluntary intoxication to negate mens rea would create a high risk of perjury.

Harbison-Fischer Mfg. Co. v. Mohawk Data Sciences Corp.


NO. 2-90-260-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH

1556 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Weatherford v. State


No. 11-90-172-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


822 S.W.2d 217; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3058



December 12, 1991, Decided  
December 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Vacated April 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Scurry County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of theft of oil field property, a felony, on appeal from a trial court in Scurry County, Texas, on grounds that appellee state's authority to conduct an administrative search could not be an adequate substitute for a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of felony theft of oil field property, a trailer. The record showed that a security guard suspected appellant of taking a roll of cable from a job site and reported it. Appellee state searched appellant's business premises, an oil and gas lease, pursuant to Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 88.092(4), which provided for access to the records of a person engaging in the oil and gas business for inspection and audit. In that search for a business record, a bill of sale for the cable, appellee discovered a stolen trailer. Appellant raised the issue whether the authority to conduct an administrative search pursuant to Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 88.001 et seq. (1978 & Supp. 1991) could be an adequate substitute for a search warrant. The court held that it could not. Therefore, the court reversed the conviction and remanded the cause for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court found that statutory authority to conduct an administrative search was not an adequate substitute for a search warrant. Accordingly, the court reversed appellant's conviction for theft and remanded the cause for a new trial.

Harvey v. State


NOS. B14-90-00647-CR, B14-90-00650-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


821 S.W.2d 389; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3060



December 12, 1991, Rendered  
December 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 29, 1992. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 29, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 517,873 & 539,346. Woody Densen, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Reformed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from two separate judgments of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting appellant of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle (UUMV) and was given five years of probation. While still on probation, appellant was indicted for murder and placed in jail. The trial court revoked appellant's probation on the same evidence heard by the jury in the murder trial and assessed punishment in the UUMV case at five years in prison. A jury convicted appellant of murder and sentenced him to 35 years in prison. The trial court granted the state's motion and cumulated the 35 years on the five years assessed previously. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions but reformed the judgment in the UUMV case to credit appellant's five-year sentence with the days already spent in jail and the judgment in the murder case by deleting the finding that appellant used a deadly weapon. The court also found that failure of the trial judge to include a voluntariness instruction in the charge was harmless error, that the use of the same evidence to revoke appellant's probation as was offered in the murder trial was not unconstitutional, and that double jeopardy did not apply to bar the use of the same evidence in the two proceedings.


OUTCOME: Judgments convicting appellant of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and murder were affirmed as reformed. Judgment in the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle case was reformed to credit appellant's five year sentence with days already spent in jail; judgment in the murder case was reformed to delete the finding that appellant used a deadly weapon during the commission of the crime.

Williams v. State


NO. 01-86-00379-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


821 S.W.2d 403; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3062



December 12, 1991, Rendered and Delivered  
December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 413,770. Hon. A. D. Azios.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of October 10, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2504.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On motion for rehearing after remand, appellant challenged the order of the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas) which gave a parole instruction to the jury that assessed punishment at 85 years' confinement following appellant's conviction for forgery.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of forgery, found two enhancement paragraphs true, and assessed punishment at 85 years confinement, though the punishment range was 25 years to life under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (1989). On a motion for rehearing following remand, appellant requested a new trial on punishment alleging that he was harmed by a parole instruction that had been held unconstitutional, but was later codified as Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1991). The court reviewed the factors in determining whether harm had occurred and found that the prosecution's argument that indirectly invited the jury to consider parole law in assessing punishment was the only factor supporting appellant's claim of harm. The court concluded that the error in giving the parole instruction had not contributed to appellant's punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for forgery was affirmed because the jury was unlikely to have assessed a sentence greater than the state requested as a result of the parole instruction, and giving the parole charge made no contribution to appellant's punishment.

Auzenne v. State


No. C14-90-01092-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3115



December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] On Appeal from the 177th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 558,241



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), overruling his pretrial motions to quash the first and third paragraphs of appellee state's indictment for engaging in organized criminal activity and to suppress his confession.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted by appellee state for engaging in organized criminal activity. The trial court overruled appellant's motions to quash the first and third paragraphs of the indictment and to suppress his confession. The trial court's decision was affirmed on appeal. The court held that the first paragraph of the indictment conveyed sufficient information about the charges to enable appellant to adequately prepare his defense. The court also held that the language of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 71.01, 71.03 was not confusing or vague, but rather sufficiently clear to give appellant fair notice regarding the conduct forbidden by the statutes. Lastly, the court found that the trial court had not abused its discretion in admitting appellant's confession as it was in the unique position to determine whether appellant's confession was voluntary and admissible.


OUTCOME: Judgment overruling appellant's motions to quash certain portions of his indictment for engaging in organized criminal activity and to suppress his confession was affirmed. The indictment gave appellant fair notice of the charges against him to adequately prepare his defense, statutory language was clear in stating what conduct was forbidden, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting appellant's confession.

 

1560 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Engle v. Coker


NO. 09-91-202 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


820 S.W.2d 247; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3220



December 5, 1991, Delivered  
December 5, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDINGS



DISPOSITION: WRIT CONDITIONALLY GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought a writ of mandamus to compel the dismissal of the charges against him by respondent trial judge on the grounds that he had not been brought to trial within the 180 day limit imposed by the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 (1979).


OVERVIEW: Relator was incarcerated in Nevada. Based on an indictment in Texas, a detainer was filed and relator was transferred to Texas. After relator filed a request for final disposition, relator filed a motion to dismiss the indictment for the state's failure to bring the case to trial within 180 days as required by the Interstate Agreements on Detainers Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 (1979). The trial court denied the motion and set the case for trial. Relator requested a writ of mandamus from the appellate court to require respondent trial judge to dismiss the indictments. The appellate court granted the writ and found that respondent's duty to dismiss was ministerial rather than discretionary. The court also found that, contrary to state's argument, direct appeal was not an adequate remedy because relator would first be forced to undergo a trial, which would be a useless act. Also, the appellate court refused to find the Interstate Agreements on Detainers Act to be unconstitutional and rejected state's contention that relator was produced for trial prior to the expiration of the 180 day limit because state was required to bring relator to trial, not merely produce him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the writ of mandamus, requiring respondent trial judge to dismiss the charges against relator because respondent had no discretion to refuse to dismiss the charges and direct appeal was not an adequate remedy.

Gonzales v. State


Appeal No. 04-89-00393-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


822 S.W.2d 189; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3244



December 5, 1991, Delivered  
December 5, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Discretionary Review Reversed and Cause Remanded April 15, 1992. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 227th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 88-CR-61092. Honorable Mike M. Machado, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for aggravated sexual assault by the 227th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) after the child victim was permitted to testify using closed-circuit television.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried for sexual assault, and the trial court permitted the child victim to testify via closed-circuit television. Appellant was convicted and filed this appeal. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. The court determined that the testimony by closed-circuit television was permissible because the trial judge made findings of fact and conclusions of law that showed the child would suffer undue psychological harm if forced to testify in court and that the system provided for two-way communication, which satisfied appellant's right of confrontation and cross-examination. The appellate court agreed that the procedure protected appellant's due process rights. The court pointed to an instruction by the trial judge stating that no adverse inference was to be drawn from the fact that the child testified using the closed-circuit system. Finally, appellant's argument that evidence of extraneous offenses was improperly admitted was not preserved for review. Appellant did not make a specific objection in accordance with Tex. R. Evid. 403 that the probative value of the evidence was outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault because the testimony of the child victim via closed-circuit television did not violate appellant's due process rights, and appellant's objection concerning the admission of extraneous offenses was not preserved for review.

State v. Szela


Nos. 13-91-290-CR, 13-91-291-CR, 13-91-292-CR, 13-91-293-CR, 13-91-294-CR, 13-91-295-CR, 13-91-296-CR, 13-91-297-CR, 13-91-298-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


820 S.W.2d 200; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2951



November 27, 1991, Delivered  
November 27, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled December 30, 1991. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 29, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from County Court at Law No. 1 of Calhoun County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the County Court at Law No. 1 of Calhoun County, Texas, which granted appellee individuals' motion to quash on constitutional grounds the state's charge of taking oysters from polluted waters, a violation of Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 76.116(a) (1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellees were charged with taking oysters from polluted waters but the trial court dismissed the charges, finding the statute unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court's order could not have been based on the statutes' application to the individuals charged, as none of the appellees testified or presented any evidence to show their particular situation. The court held that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 436.012(d) did not shift the burden of proof to a defendant, but to one who seeks to take oysters and to determine whether an area is open or closed and concluded that the state was still required to show in a prosecution that a defendant was taking oysters from a closed are. The court found Tex. Health & Safety Code § 436.012 and Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 76.116 constitutional and not void for vagueness because one statute permits the Health Commissioner to declare areas polluted, and the other statute prohibited the taking of oysters from these waters. The court found that on their face, these statutes provided notice of the forbidden conduct in terms which persons of common intelligence could reasonably understand.


OUTCOME: The court held that the sections of the statutes in question were constitutional and reversed and remanded the causes to the trial court because one statute permitted the health commissioner to declare areas polluted and the other prohibited the taking of oysters from the prohibited areas.

El-Ahmad v. General Mills, Inc.


NO. 01-91-00281-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2959



November 27, 1991, Delivered  
November 27, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 234th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-56676



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the decision of the 234th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in appellant's cause of action against appellee for employer's negligence, gross negligence, intentionally failing to furnish a safe workplace, and intentionally inflicted emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee brought an action against appellee employer for personal injuries sustained when she slipped and fell at her workplace, a restaurant owned by appellee. Appellant received workers' compensation benefits for the injuries she sustained in the fall, and she also sued appellee for gross negligence and asserted an intentional tort claim. The court affirmed the summary judgment on the negligence cause of action because pursuant to the exclusive remedies doctrine, an employee who received workers' compensation benefits could not bring suit for injuries caused by an employer's negligence or gross negligence, but only for the employer's intentional torts. The court reversed and remanded on the intentional tort cause of action. Since an intentional tort claim was not alleged until after the motion for summary judgment was filed, and appellee failed to amend its motion for summary judgment to include this cause, appellee did not specifically address or dispose expressly of the intentional tort cause of action. Thus, appellee did not sustain its burden with respect to the intentional tort claim, and final summary judgment was improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment on appellant employee's negligence cause of action and reversed and remanded on the intentional tort cause of action. The trial court erred in granting summary judgment in favor of appellee employer on the tort cause of action because it was not addressed in the summary judgment proceeding.

Wendt v. State


NO. A14-90-00160-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2987



November 27, 1991, Decided  
November 27, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 518,949.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 339th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for three counts of the offense of indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11 with an enhanced sentence of concurrent imprisonment for 45 years, 45 years, and 20 years under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(b). Appellant argued many points of trial error including misjoinder, denial of a speedy trial, and finding complainant competent to testify.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted on three counts of indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11 and received an enhanced concurrent prison sentence under Tex. Penal Code Ann § 12.42(b) of 45 years, 45 years and 20 years. Appellant raised numerous points of error at trial including misjoinder of offenses, denial of speedy trial rights and finding complainant competent to testify. The court affirmed the conviction and sentencing and on appellant's speedy trial point found that he filed numerous pre-trial motions, was notably uncooperative with two different court-appointed attorneys and had ample time to prepare a defense around possible testimony of complainant's mother who died in an accident several days before trial. The court held joinder of offenses was proper because two or more of the offenses arose out of the same criminal episode under Tex. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.24 (1989), Tex. Penal Code Ann. §3.01and § 21.11(a)(1)(2). The court found no abuse of discretion in determining complainant competent to testify but disallowing appellant to examine her during competency hearing because competency is a question for the court, not for the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for indecency with a child and his enhanced sentence. The court found no misjoinder of offenses when they arose out of the same criminal episode. The court found no abuse of discretion in finding complainant was competent to testify and no violation of speedy trial rights because of appellant's many pre-trial motions and inability to work with two different court-appointed attorneys.
