Texas Educ. Agency v. Leeper


NO. 2-87-216-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


843 S.W.2d 41; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3290



November 27, 1991, Decided  
November 27, 1991, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 17TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Charles J. Murray



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state education agency and various local school districts, sought review of the judgment of the 17th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which found in favor of appellees, home school parents, in a class action suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 37.001 (1986), and awarded appellees a declaratory judgment, a permanent injunction, and attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: After appellants, state education agency and various local school districts, had prosecuted over 150 parents as violators of the state's compulsory attendance law, appellees, home school parents, brought suit. The trial court issued declaratory relief by construing the compulsory exemption statute to include home schooled children and permanently enjoined any further prosecutions and awarded attorney's fees to appellees. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgments, finding that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to construe and enjoin enforcement of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 37.001 (1986), because it was a criminal statute; but that appellees' equal protection rights were violated, because the difference between a student receiving a private education from a "private school" environment versus a "home school" environment was not rationally related to the state's compulsory education law. Consequently, the court held that appellants were not immune from suit under 42 U.S.C.S. 1983, and that the evidence was sufficient to support the class-wide injunctive relief, the declaratory judgment, and the attorney's fees award pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory, injunctive, and attorney's fee awards in favor of appellee home school parents, because appellants, state education agency and various local school districts, had violated appellees' equal protection rights, by holding, in essence, that home schools were not exempt from compulsory public education, and because the evidence was sufficient to support the foregoing awards.

Owens v. State


No. 01-90-01093-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


820 S.W.2d 912; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2788



November 21, 1991, Rendered  
November 21, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 578,354; Norman Lanford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant suspect sought review of his conviction in the 339th District Court, Harris County (Texas), pursuant to a plea agreement, for delivery of a simulated controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant suspect argued that his conviction, entered pursuant to a plea agreement, for delivery of a simulated controlled substance was improper because the statute on which the charge was based, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 482.002(a)(1)(2) (1991), was unconstitutional. He claimed that because the substance he delivered was not contraband, he was being punished solely for speech, i.e., for falsely representing to a buyer that it was contraband. The reviewing court upheld the conviction. When challenging the constitutionality of a statute, it is incumbent upon a defendant to show that in its operation the statute is unconstitutional to him in his situation; that it may be unconstitutional to others is insufficient. Here, appellant's judicial confession included one method of committing the offense that did not involve speech. Thus, his right to free speech was not infringed.


OUTCOME: Appellant suspect's conviction pursuant to a plea agreement for delivery of a simulated controlled substance was affirmed because his judicial confession included one method of committing the offense that did not involve speech, so his right to free speech was not infringed.

Guerrero v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the County Court of Bee County (Texas), where a jury found him guilty of unlawful assistance to a voter. Appellant argued insufficient evidence, unconstitutionally overbroad and vague language in the charging statute, a defective jury charge, error in the admission of evidence, and improper jury argument.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a campaign worker and assisted someone in filling out an absentee voting ballot. Appellant was charged and found guilty of unlawful assistance to a voter. Finally, the court found that the state's argument was a reasonable deduction from the evidence and there was no improper jury argument. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant campaign worker of unlawful assistance to a voter was affirmed because sufficient evidence existed to support the jury's verdict of guilty, the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, and appellant did not suffer egregious harm from any error in the jury charge. Also, any error as to the admission of extraneous evidence was waived and there was no improper jury argument in the state's closing.

Fleming v. State


No. 3-87-060-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


819 S.W.2d 237; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2717



November 6, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 10, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Bastrop County, 21st Judicial District; No. 6838, Honorable Harold R. Towslee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded on Remand


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas), defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence received for the offense of aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: A child said that defendant sexually abused her. Several witnesses testified that the child showed symptoms of sexual abuse and that she said that defendant abused her. Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. Defendant objected to the admission of video interviews of the child, hearsay, and jury instructions. The court overruled the evidence objections and remanded due to punishment phase errors. On reconsideration of the evidentiary complaints, the court held that defendant was not deprived of any constitutional rights because the state admitted videos and presented the child for cross-examination in accord with 1983 Tex. Gen. Laws, ch. 599, § 1. The aunt's testimony was inadmissible hearsay because a proper predicate was not laid to admit the statements as the first statements made by a victim to an adult. Statements to the mother were not admissible as prior consistent statements because they were not made prior to alleged improper influence. Statements to the pediatrician and therapist were admissible as pertinent to diagnosis and treatment. The court held the hearsay errors did not affect conviction or punishment and again remanded for a punishment hearing.


OUTCOME: The court remanded defendant's criminal case for a new punishment hearing in accord with a prior ruling by the court. The court held that harmless error occurred when the trial court erroneously admitted the hearsay testimony of the mother and aunt, which did not affect defendant's conviction and punishment due to the same evidence being properly admitted through other witnesses.

Hamilton v. State


No. A14-90-00754-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


818 S.W.2d 880; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2654



October 31, 1991, Rendered  
October 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 559,596.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 178th District Court, Harris County (Texas) of voluntary manslaughter. Appellant pled not guilty on an indictment for murder, and the jury found him guilty of voluntary manslaughter and assessed punishment at 20 years' confinement. Appellant asserted error based on the state's closing argument during the punishment stage of trial, and the trial court's jury instruction on the law of parole.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his jury conviction for voluntary manslaughter for shooting the victim during the course of an argument. He claimed that that the trial court committed reversible error by denying his motion for a mistrial after the state invited the jury to speculate on extraneous offenses during summation. The court rejected the argument, noting that the trial judge sustained two objections to the summation and issued a curative instruction to the jury to disregard the improper argument. The court also rejected appellant's argument that the jury charge on parole was unconstitutional because it invited the jury to base its punishment decision on the possibility of parole, relying on a 1987 judicial decision. The court noted that Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a), approved in 1989, authorized legislation to permit courts to instruct juries regarding the possibility of parole. In this case, the court held that the jury instruction on parole was in complete compliance with the constitutional amendment and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1990), which was enacted to implement the constitutional amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence, holding that the trial court's jury instruction cured any harm arising from the prosecutor's improper summation during the punishment phase of trial, and that the jury instruction on parole was entirely consistent with applicable statutory and constitutional provisions.

Spellmon v. Sweeney


No. 10-91-165-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


819 S.W.2d 206; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2649



October 30, 1991, Delivered  
October 31, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 52nd District Court; Coryell County, Texas; Trial Court # 26,081.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the dismissal of his pro se action in forma pauperis, pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001 (1991), in the 52 District Court, Coryell County, Texas. Appellant argued that the dismissal was erroneous and violated his rights under Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 13, 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a pro se action in forma pauperis claiming that defendants, employees of the department of criminal justice, used prison regulations to deny him "legal visits" with other prisoners and the use of a law book. Before defendants were served with process the trial court dismissed the cause as frivolous pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001 (1991). The court held that the trial court properly dismissed appellant's claims based on the state statutes because the action's realistic chance of ultimate success was slight. However, the court found that appellant's petition had raised a potential 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim for a violation of his rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and it was impossible to tell from appellant's petition whether his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim had a realistic chance of success. Because prison inmates' complaints were to be construed liberally, the court held that appellant's allegations were sufficient to allege a violation of his constitutional rights and summary dismissal without affording him a hearing was unreasonable. Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001(b)(1) (1991). Accordingly, the judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment because dismissal of appellant's denial-of-access claim without a hearing was unreasonable because it was impossible to tell from his petition whether his constitutional claim had a realistic chance of success.

Collier v. Firemen's & Policemen's Civil Service Com.


No. 2-90-182-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


817 S.W.2d 404; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2575



October 22, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled November 20, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied March 11, 1992. Motion for Rehearing Application for Writ of Error Overruled April 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 30th District Court of Wichita County; Hon. Calvin Ashley.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the 30th District Court of Wichita County (Texas), in favor of appellees, city firemen's and policemen's civil service commission and the city, that the nepotism amendment to Wichita Falls, Tex., Civil Service R. V, § 7, did not violate Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. ch. 143 (1988) or Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, who submitted applications for entry level firefighter positions with appellee city, were excluded from the eligibility list due to an amendment to Wichita Falls, Tex., Civil Service R. V, § 7, providing that no person could be employed by the fire department if a member of his immediate family was so employed. Appellants filed suit, and the trial court entered judgment in favor of appellees, the city and the city firemen's and policemen's civil service commission. Appellants sought review, contending that the nepotism amendment set up nonmerit requirements at odds with the Civil Service Act, Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 143.025(a), and with their equal protection rights under the state constitution. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees. It held that Tex. Loc. Gov't Code ch. 143 did not specifically preempt the field in the area of what a qualified, competent, and suitable fire department applicant may be. The court further held that the nepotism regulation furthered a legitimate state interest and thus did not violate appellants' equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court' s judgment, holding that the civil service rules did not preempt the field in the area of what a qualified, competent, and suitable fire department applicant may be, and that the nepotism regulation did not violate appellants' equal protection rights because it furthered a legitimate state interest.

HL Farm Corp. v. Self


No. 05-90-01390-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


820 S.W.2d 372; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3075



October 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated August 28, 1991. Application for Writ of Error is Granted March 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 86th District Court. Kaufman County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 34,414


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the summary judgment rendered in favor of appellee county tax appraisal unit, by the 86th District Court, Kaufman County (Texas), in appellant's suit contesting the denial of its open-space land application. Appellant argued that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.56(3) (1982) violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1-d-1, Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1, and the equal protection clauses of the United States and Texas Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was denied, by appellees, the county tax appraisal unit, an open-space land designation, which would have reduced the taxes on the property, on the grounds of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.56(3) (1982), which denied the favorable qualification to land owned by a corporation required by federal law to register its ownership of the land and whose majority interest was owned by a non-resident alien. Appellant sought review, contending that § 23.56(3) violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1-d-1, Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1, and the equal protection clauses of the United States and Texas Constitutions. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the eligibility limitation excluding non-resident aliens from qualifying for the open-space land designation furthered § 1-d-1's goal of preserving and benefiting the family farm. The court further held that the classification for tax purposes did not result in the denial of equal protection where it rested upon policy considerations having a fair and substantial relation to the object of the legislation and where a rational basis existed for assessing the value of agricultural land owned by non-resident aliens differently.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the eligibility limitation excluding non-resident aliens from qualifying for the open-space land designation furthered the statutory goal of preserving and benefiting the family farm, and did not cause denial of equal protection because it rested upon a ground of difference having a fair and substantial relation to the object of the legislation.

Turner v. State


No. 01-90-00496-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2535



October 17, 1991, Delivered  
October 17, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINION SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 549664.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order by the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which entered a jury conviction for the offense of murder and assessed punishment at confinement for life and a fine of $ 7,500.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was convicted of murder. The court affirmed the conviction because the record revealed sufficient evidence to establish that immediately after the appellant shot at a man four times, the decedent was found lying in the street. The record contained no evidence that the decedent was shot by someone other than appellant. Several neighborhood kids saw appellant shoot the victim or observed him running away from the scene. Furthermore, appellant had previously been identified in a police line-up. Therefore, the court held that the trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant committed the offense of murder of the victim. The court further held that the trial court did not err in instructing the jury that they could consider the existence of good conduct time and parole in determining appellant's sentence because under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.03, §4 a jury charge that included a parole instruction was no longer unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment for conviction was affirmed because a rational trier of fact could have determined beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant committed the offense of murder. Furthermore, a jury instruction including a parole instruction was no longer considered unconstitutional under Texas statute.

Rougeau v. State


Nos. C14-90-00834-CR, A14-90-00835-CR, B14-90-00836-CR, C14-90-00837-CR, A14-90-00838-CR, B14-90-00839-CR, C14-90-00840-CR, A14-90-00841-CR, B14-90-00842-CR, C14-90-00843-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2488



October 10, 1991, Rendered  
October 10, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 528,542; 529,753; 529,754; 529,755; 573,729; 573,730; 573,731; 573,732; 574,282; 574,283. 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment from the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting defendant upon his plea of guilty to 12 separate aggravated robberies and for escape while being confined on the robbery cases.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to 12 separate charges of aggravated robbery and for escape while being confined on the robbery cases. Defendant subsequently appealed his conviction challenging the validity of his plea, the jury charge, a defect in the escape indictment, and error in the prosecutor's jury argument. The appellate court found that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(c) (1989) required substantial compliance by the court with, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13 (1989), admonishment requirements. Defendant signed a document containing admonishments and orally acknowledged that he understood the consequences of his plea. Substantial compliance was satisfied. Defendant did not raise the issue of his competency at the time of his plea and because the court had no reason to question competency, the court was not obligated to make an inquiry into mental competency. A jury instruction regarding consideration of good conduct and application of the parole law complied with Tex. Const. art. 17, § 1. The prosecutor's jury argument was a reasonable deduction from the evidence and an appropriate plea for law enforcement. Therefore, defendant's convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for 12 counts of aggravated robbery and for escape while he was confined for the robbery charges was affirmed. The trial court substantially complied with statutory admonishment requirements, defendant's competency was not raised as an issue nor was there reason for the court to consider it an issue, jury instructions were constitutional, and the prosecutor's jury argument was appropriate.

Oak Forest Civic Club v. Duke


No. 01-89-01230-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2493



October 10, 1991, Delivered  
October 10, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 129th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 85-18874-CV.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of January 31, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 256.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city, civic club and its president, sought review of a judgment from the 129th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which dismissed their action against appellee property owners regarding violation of a deed restriction on the grounds of waiver, laches, and lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, city, civic club and its president, sued appellee property owners for using their property for commercial purposes when a deed restriction limited the property to residential use. A jury found that appellees were in violation of the deed restriction, but that appellants' action was barred by the affirmative defenses of waiver and laches. The trial court also granted appellees' motion for partial summary judgment against appellant civic club, finding it had no standing to sue. The court reversed, finding that appellant civic club had standing to sue under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 202.004(b) (1991) because members of the club were property owners covered by the dedicatory instrument containing the deed restriction. Additionally, the court rejected appellees affirmative defense of waiver, finding there was no evidence to support the jury's finding because other deed restriction violations alleged by appellees could not be evidence of waiver as a matter of law. The laches defense was rejected because the instruction to the jury failed to require the jury to find that appellees detrimentally relied on appellants' delay. The court remanded the cause for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that dismissed the action of appellants, city, civic club and its president, against appellee property owners for violation of a deed restriction. The court held that appellant civic club had standing to sue because members of the club were property owners covered by the dedicatory instrument containing the deed restriction. The court rejected waiver and laches defenses and remanded the cause for a new trial.

Stevens v. State


No. 2-90-119-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


817 S.W.2d 800; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2452



October 9, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 213th District Court of Tarrant County; Hon. George S. Kredell.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the 213th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.052(a)(2) (1989) of the offense of illegal investment of funds to further the commission of the offense of aggravated possession of marihuana. Appellant alleged that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of illegal investment of funds to further the commission of the offense of aggravated possession of marihuana, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.052(a)(2) (1989), after buying marihuana from an undercover officer. The conviction was affirmed on appeal. The court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.052(a)(2) was not unconstitutionally vague because the conduct proscribed was stated in terms that could be readily understood by a person of common intelligence, and when applied to appellant's specific conduct, the terms were not vague at all. The statute furthermore provided sufficient notice to law enforcement personnel so as to prevent arbitrary enforcement. The court likewise held that the indictment, which tracked the statutory language, sufficiently alleged enough to enable appellant to prepare a defense. The indictment's supposed deficiencies were merely evidentiary facts the state was not required to plead. Finally, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain his conviction because a rational trier of fact could find appellant invested funds and thereby intended to further possession of the marihuana.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The statute proscribing the investment of funds to further the possession of marihuana was not unconstitutionally vague because it was stated in terms readily understood by a person of common intelligence and provided sufficient notice to prevent arbitrary enforcement. The indictment sufficiently alleged enough to enable appellant to prepare a defense. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction.

In re T.D.


No. 01-90-00670-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged an order of the 314th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which transferred jurisdiction over appellant from the district court sitting as a juvenile court to the criminal district court under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.02(a) (1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was 17 when he was referred to the juvenile probation department for selling cocaine. This was his sixth referral. Previously, he had been referred for possession and delivery of drugs, indecent exposure, and robbery. The state filed a motion requesting to waive jurisdiction of the juvenile court. The juvenile court ordered a diagnostic study, social evaluation, and full investigation of appellant, his circumstances, and the circumstances of the alleged offense under Tex. Fam. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order transferring jurisdiction of appellant juvenile from the juvenile court to the criminal district court because there was sufficient evidence to support the conclusion that there was little likelihood that the facilities available to the juvenile court could have reasonably been expected to rehabilitate appellant.

Crooks v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2382



September 26, 1991, Delivered  
September 26, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 527797.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 338th District Court; Harris County (Texas), for murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 19.02(a) (1), (a)(2) (1989), and asserted that the trial court improperly denied his request for a jury instruction on voluntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 19.02(a) (1), (a)(2) (1989). He challenged his conviction, asserting that the trial court erred in refusing his request for a voluntary manslaughter instruction, he was denied effective assistance of counsel, a witness' prior conviction was improperly excluded, and the parole charge on punishment was improper. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the trial court did not error in refusing the voluntary manslaughter instruction because the evidence introduced in the case did not support a finding that, if appellant were guilty, he was only guilty of the lesser-included offense. The court held that a witness' prior conviction was properly excluded and that the parole charge was proper and that did not contribute to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on involuntary manslaughter because the evidence did not support a finding that, if appellant were guilty, he was only guilty of the lesser charge. The court found that counsel's failure to object to charge was harmless error and did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel.

Dickey v. State


No. 11-90-035-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


816 S.W.2d 832; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2399



September 26, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Galveston County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her conviction by the District Court of Galveston County, Texas, after the trial court denied her motion to suppress evidence. Appellant waived her right to a jury trial, entered a plea of not guilty, and stipulated to the evidence. The district judge found her guilty of possession of more than 28 grams of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, and sentenced her to confinement for eight years.


OVERVIEW: In an affidavit submitted in support of a search warrant, a city peace officer asserted he had credible information that appellant had methamphetamine in her home, located outside city limits. The judge issued a search warrant for the premises, which was executed by the affiant and other officers, who found methamphetamine. Appellant was convicted of possession of more than 28 grams of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, and contended on appeal that her motion to suppress the evidence was denied in error. She argued that the search warrant was issued to and executed by a peace officer acting outside his jurisdiction, and was not supported by probable cause. The court disagreed, holding that it made no difference that the affidavit was signed by a city police officer rather than a county deputy sheriff. Further, the warrant named a location outside city limits in the county, and at least one of the peace officers who executed the warrant, and whose name was listed in the return, was a sheriff's deputy with jurisdiction to execute the warrant. Finally, the court rejected appellant's argument that the warrant was not supported by probable cause, and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of more than 28 grams of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, holding that the search warrant could properly be issued on a city police officer's affidavit, that the search warrant was properly executed with the assistance of peace officers having county-wide jurisdiction, and that the warrant was sufficiently supported by probable cause.

Durish v. Texas State Bd. of Ins.


No. 6-90-039-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


817 S.W.2d 764; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2357



September 24, 1991  
September 24, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 261st Judicial District Court, Travis County, Texas; Trial Court No. 471,261.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment from the 261st Judicial District Court, Travis County, Texas, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee State Board of Insurance on the basis that Tex. Ins. Code. Ann. art. 21.79D (1991) was unconstitutional in appellant's action to recover offsets under the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer sought certification under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.79D (1991) to recover offsets against its state obligations for expenses incurred in bringing antifraud actions. A trial court held that article 21.79D was unconstitutional, granting appellee State Board of Insurance's summary judgment motion. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because article 21.79D violated the retroactive law prohibition of Tex. Const. art. I, § 16, and was void. By its plain language, article 21.79D imposed on the state the obligation to offset debts that an insurer owed to the state, by the amount of costs and attorney's fees incurred by the insurer with respect to transactions, which occurred before the passage of the statute. The court found that the assessments and debts owed by the insurer to the state were vested rights of the state, which could not be impaired by a retroactive law. Appellee adequately and thoroughly presented the various legal reasons why article 21.79D was unconstitutional in its motion for summary judgment. The court rejected appellant's contention that appellee did not have standing to contend that article 21.79D was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court's judgment granting summary judgment in favor of appellee State Board of Insurance in appellant insurer's action to recover offsets under the insurance code because the insurance statute, under which appellant's sought certification, violated the retroactive law prohibition of the Texas constitution. Thus, the insurance statute was void.

Zimmelman v. Harris County


No. 01-90-00047-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


819 S.W.2d 178; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2333



September 19, 1991, Rendered  
September 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 270th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 88-051953; Hon. Ann Tyrell Cochran.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the 270th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted defendants, county, corporation, and partnership, summary judgment in plaintiffs' action brought against defendants to stop the construction of a proposed county jail.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers brought an action to stop the building of a jail. Defendants, county, corporation, and partnership, were granted summary judgment, and plaintiffs sought review. The court affirmed and found that while defendant corporation had failed to file an original answer until 4 days before the summary judgment hearing, it had been named a defendant, had appeared in the action and had contested the claims. The court also found plaintiffs lacked taxpayer standing to make attacks on public policy or abuse of discretion grounds. In attacks made on the grounds of illegality, the court found a construction prohibition under Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 361.067 (1991) applied only to municipal jails, not county jails. The court also found a claim of illegality could not be based on Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 351.105 (repealed 1991) because § 351.105 was repealed. Furthermore, the court held a claim of illegality based on the appointment of a private corporation to build the jail was incontestable as a matter of law. Finally, the court overruled plaintiffs' remaining illegality claim because expenditures had not violated Tex. Const. art. 3, § 51 and Tex. Const. art. 11, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment granting defendants, county, corporation, and partnership, summary judgment because defendant corporation's appearance in the suit pursuant to its motion for summary judgment remedied a delayed original answer, and plaintiff taxpayers lacked standing to attack jail construction on public policy and abuse of discretion grounds, while plaintiffs' claims of illegality were overruled.

Texas Educ. Agency v. Stamos


No. 01-86-00939-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


817 S.W.2d 378; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2338



September 19, 1991, Delivered  
September 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 334th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 85-25201.

This Opinion Substituted for Withdrawn Opinion of August 8, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1975.



DISPOSITION: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing denied, Master's Motion for Rehearing dismissed, Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a class of Texas public school children, and defendant education agency both appealed the judgment of the 334th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied plaintiffs' challenge, on federal and state grounds, of Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 21.920 (1987) and the related 19 Tex. Admin. Code § 97.113 (1988) (the "no pass, no play rule"), and assessed defendant costs of the court-appointed master in chancery.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, Texas public school children, filed suit against defendant education agency challenging Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 21.920 (1987) and 19 Tex. Admin. Code § 97.113 (1988) (the "no pass, no play rule"), which plaintiffs argued discriminated against handicapped persons in violation of the Education of Handicapped Act (EHA), 20 U.S.C.S. § 1401, and against minority students in violation of Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000d. The trial court denied the challenge and assessed defendant costs. Both parties appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court lacked jurisdiction to review plaintiffs' injunctive relief application, as they did not exhaust their administrative remedies under the EHA. Because handicapped students who had not met their individual education plan were not a suspect class, the standard of review was rational basis, which the statute satisfied. Plaintiffs' substantive due process claim failed because there was not a constitutional right to participate in extracurricular activities. Plaintiffs were not entitled to injunctive relief because they did not show that the legislature's stated purpose for the rule was merely a pretext.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the challenge by plaintiffs, Texas public school children, to the "no-pass, no play rule" as applied to minority and learning disabled children because they failed to exhaust their administrative remedies under the statute and the statute met the applicable rational basis test. Because defendant education agency failed to preserve its point of error as to the assessment of costs, the court overruled it.

Gibson v. J.W.T.


No. 09-90-245 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


815 S.W.2d 863; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2427



August 29, 1991, Delivered  
August 29, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled October 2, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Granted July 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 1-A Judicial District Court Newton County, Texas; Trial Cause No. 9248.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, putative biological father, sought review of an order of the 1-A Judicial District Court, Newton County, Texas, which sustained appellee parents plea in abatement and dismissed the lawsuit in a suit to establish paternity and gain access to a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, putative biological father, brought an action against appellee parents to establish the paternity of their child and to gain access to the child. The lower court sustained appellees' plea in abatement and dismissed the suit on the grounds that appellant had no standing to bring suit because the child had a presumed father who did not initiate the lawsuit, and appellant did not fall within any of the definitions or classes of parties enumerated in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 11.03 (1991) as being entitled to bring an original suit affecting the parent-child relationship. The court reversed the judgment of the lower court because the requirement of § 11.03, that the child of the putative biological father have no presumed father before the putative biological father could institute a cause of action affecting the parent-child relationship violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The court remanded the case to the lower court for a full trial on the merits.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court that sustained appellees' plea in abatement and dismissed the suit was reversed and remanded to the lower court for a full trial on the merits because the statute that denied appellant, putative biological father, the right to bring a suit affecting the parent-child relationship because the child had a presumed father was unconstitutional.

Lopez v. Public Utility Com.


No. 3-90-178-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


816 S.W.2d 776; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2151



August 28, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication September 25, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Overruled September 25, 1991. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ is Overruled March 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District; No. 479,927, Honorable Paul R. Davis Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Modified and Affirmed and Modified


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, utility customers, sought review of the order of the 53rd Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), which dismissed appellant's causes of action against appellees, city and commission, under the Public Utilities Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c § 26(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, utility customers, filed suit against appellees, city and commission, which challenged an order by the appellee commission issued pursuant to the Public Utilities Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c § 26(c). The lower court dismissed appellant's cause of action for want of subject-matter jurisdiction. Appellant asserted that the lower court erred when it found that appellee commission had exclusive jurisdiction over its claims. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court found that appellant's claims were properly dismissed because appellant failed to exhaust all administrative remedies prior to filing suit. The lower court properly dismissed appellant's claims against appellee city based upon a doctrine that forbade collateral attacks against valid city ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which dismissed the suit of appellant, utility customers, because appellant had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies prior to filing suit against appellees, city and commission.

 

1587 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Sabine Consol., Inc. v. State


Nos. 3-87-051-CR, 3-87-055-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


816 S.W.2d 784; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2154; 1991 OSHD (CCH) P29,491



August 28, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] Released for Publication November 13, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Overruled November 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court at Law No. 1 of Travis County, Nos. 269,530, 269,532, Honorable Leslie D. Taylor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a corporation and its president, appealed their convictions for criminally negligent homicide under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 19.07 (1989), from the County Court at Law No. One of Travis County (Texas), in an action that arose from a breach of a duty under the Texas Occupational Safety Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5182a (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, a corporation and its president, were convicted of criminally negligent homicide under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 19.07 (1989) after two workers were killed when a trench collapsed. State alleged defendants violated a duty imposed by The Texas Occupational Safety Act (TOSA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5182a (1987). On the court's first review of the cases it reversed the trial court's judgments based on its conclusion that the Federal Occupational Safety and Health Act of 1970, 29 U.S.C.A. §§ 651-678 (1985), preempted state criminal prosecutions based on the violation of state or local standards for working conditions. On remand from the Court of Criminal Appeals the court affirmed the convictions and held that a corporation could be convicted for criminally negligent homicide. The court held that the TOSA was not unconstitutionally vague, and it was sufficient to give an employer notice of its duty to keep employees reasonably safe. The court also held that the informations were not defective because they were not required to allege the specific statute that was violated or the manner and means of the death of the victims.


OUTCOME: The convictions for criminally negligent homicide from the trial court for defendants, a corporation and its president, were affirmed because the statute that was violated was not unconstitutionally vague and the informations were not defective and adequately alleged an offense for which a corporation could be held liable.

 

1588 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. State


No. 09-89-293 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


814 S.W.2d 874; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2400



August 28, 1991, Delivered  
August 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 12, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 2nd 9th Judicial District Court; Polk County, Texas; Trial Cause No. 12146; John C. Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of aggravated possession of a controlled substance, appealed his conviction from the Second Ninth Judicial District Court, Polk County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of aggravated possession of a controlled substance, was arrested after police conducted a traffic stop pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6675a-3e, § 5 (1977) because they believed defendant's vehicle was not displaying license plates. Defendant consented to a search of his vehicle. Defendant appealed his conviction and argued that there was no probable cause to stop his vehicle because a car dealer was not required to display license plates and he did not freely consent to a search of his vehicle. The court affirmed the conviction because the officers had probable cause to stop defendant based on their reasonable belief that there had been a traffic violation, even if their belief was not true, and their initial detention gave rise to other facts that supported a finding of probable cause. The court found no evidence that defendant's consent was the result of coercion or duress. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, and since there was no factual dispute as to how the evidence was obtained, defendant was not entitled to a limiting instruction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23.


OUTCOME: The conviction of defendant of aggravated possession of a controlled substance, was affirmed because adequate probable caused existed to stop his vehicle, and defendant freely and voluntarily consented to a search of his vehicle.

State v. Flood


No. 01-90-01055-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


814 S.W.2d 548; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2112



August 22, 1991, Delivered  
August 22, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 185th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 157078; Hon. Carl Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the resentencing of appellee suspect by the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellee suspect was originally sentenced to four years confinement after his conviction for possession of marijuana. Appellee filed a petition for resentencing under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.110 (1991). Appellant state argued that the reduced sentence was improper because Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.110 (1991) was an unconstitutional recodification of another statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.06, which had been held to be unconstitutional. The reviewing court agreed and overturned the reduced sentence. Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.110 (1991) was unconstitutional because only the governor, not the legislature or the judiciary, has the power of clemency under the Texas Constitution.


OUTCOME: The resentencing of appellee suspect was reversed and remanded because only the governor, not the legislature or the judiciary, has the power of clemency under the Texas Constitution.

Coleman v. State


No. 01-85-00976-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2069



August 15, 1991, Delivered  
August 15, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 435,764.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Texas Court of Criminal Appeals remanded a judgment convicting appellant of aggravated robbery for a determination of whether the trial court committed reversible error in instructing the jury.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted and sentenced for aggravated robbery, appellant argued that the trial court erred in providing a jury instruction on parole, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4, which had been declared unconstitutional. On remand, the court applied a multi-factor test and determined that the trial court's instruction pursuant to the statute was harmless error. In so holding, the court acknowledged that the issue of parole was mentioned several times during the trial, and no curative instruction was given by the trial court. However, the court concluded that the fact that appellant received the minimum possible term of punishment indicated that any error in discussing parole did not contribute to appellant's punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which convicted and sentenced appellant for aggravated robbery, was affirmed because the trial court's jury instruction did not constitute reversible error.

 

1591 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Texas Educ. Agency v. Stamos


No. 01-86-00939-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1975



August 8, 1991, Delivered  
August 8, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn September 19, 1991; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2338. Rehearing Denied September 19, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2338.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Texas Education Agency challenged the judgment of the trial court (Texas), which assessed against defendant costs of the fees and expenses of the court-appointed master in chancery. Plaintiff representatives for a certified class, consisting of all public school children in Texas cross-appealed the judgment that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 21.920 (1987) had a legitimate purpose and denied plaintiffs permanent injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff representatives of certified class of public school children brought an action against defendant Texas Education Agency. Plaintiffs sought injunctive relief from Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 21.920 (1987), known as the "no pass, no play rule" because it required students to maintain a 70 average to join in extracurricular activities. Plaintiffs argued that § 21.920 discriminated against handicapped students, violated the Education of Handicapped Act (EHA), 20 U.S.C.S. § 1401 (1991) and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The trial court denied recovery and ordered that defendant Texas Education Agency pay the master appointed by the trial court to collect data on the impact of § 21.920. The court reversed the order for the master's payment because the trial court lacked good cause. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment and held that administrative remedies had not been exhausted under EHA, and, thus, the court did not have jurisdiction. Further, the court held that § 21.920 was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in providing education and that there was no constitutional right to participate in extracurricular activities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment ordering defendant Texas Education Agency to pay the master's fees and expenses and rendered a judgment that the master take nothing. However, the court affirmed the denial of injunctive relief and the judgment against plaintiff representatives for a certified class consisting of all public school children in Texas that the "no pass, no play rule" statute had a legitimate purpose.

Ex parte Andrews


Nos. 01-90-00788-CR, 01-90-00789-CR, 01-90-00790-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


814 S.W.2d 839; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2000



August 8, 1991, Delivered  
August 8, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Dismissed as Improvidently Granted April 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 571485, 571483, and 571718; Hon. Brian Rains, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgement reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant protesters sought review of a judgment from the 176th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied their request for habeas corpus relief. Indicted for the unlawful use of a criminal instrument, appellants contended their indictments were defective for failing to state an offense.


OVERVIEW: Using ordinary bicycle locks, appellant protesters chained their necks together at an abortion clinic so they could not be moved without being injured. Indicted for the unlawful use of a criminal instrument under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 16.01 (1991), appellants sought habeas corpus relief claiming that the indictments were defective because they did not allege an offense. The trial court denied relief. On appeal, the court found that a bicycle lock did not become a criminal instrument by the context of its use. The court concluded that a criminal instrument was determined by the limited nature and specialized criminal use of its own distinctive properties. In using the phrase "by locking herself up to," the court found that appellee state was describing the conduct of appellants' use of the instrument in the commission of a trespass, rather than charging how the "character" of the instrument was adapted to suit the criminal design. Reversing the denial of relief and ordering the indictments dismissed, the court held that the mere locking of a bicycle lock did not constitute a special adaptation of the lock, as required by § 16.01, and that the indictments were defective.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of habeas corpus relief to appellant protesters because the bicycle locks they had used to chain themselves together at an abortion clinic were not criminal instruments. The court ordered the indictments dismissed as defective because they only described appellants' conduct rather than alleging the use of an instrument that was inherently or physically adapted to be criminal as the charged offense required.

 

1593 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Rudd


Nos. A14-90-00433-CV, A14-90-00964-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


814 S.W.2d 818; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1909



August 1, 1991, Rendered  
August 1, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 88-33631 and 88-33631B; Dan Downey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; Reversed and Remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, appellant, the deceased's husband, sought review of the 295th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee physicians and hospital on the grounds that the claim was barred by the two-year statute of limitations set out in the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellee physicians and hospital were granted summary judgment because the trial court found that appellant, husband of the deceased, did not file his medical malpractice and wrongful death claims within the two-year statute of limitations set out in the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1991). On review, appellant contended that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(b) and § 16.062(a) (1986) suspended the running of the statute until 12 months after his wife's death. The court held that § 16.062(a) was not part of the statutory scheme for medical malpractice claims envisioned by the legislature and thus, appellant's malpractice claim was barred two years from the alleged misdiagnosis and delay in treatment. On the other hand, § 16.003(b) tolled the statute of limitations until the death of appellant's wife seven months after the misdiagnosis, and appellant's wrongful death claim was not barred by the two-year limit. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellees on the malpractice claim and reversed and remanded on the wrongful death claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the grant of summary judgment to appellee physicians and hospital. It held that the two-year statute of limitations barred appellant husband of deceased's medical malpractice claim but did not bar appellant's wrongful death claim.

Waugh v. Dallas


No. 05-90-01086-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


814 S.W.2d 492; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2345



July 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1991. Motion for Writ of Error Denied January 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 162nd Judicial District Court; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 89-12849-I.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded in part, Affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, property owner, sought review of an order of the 162nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which granted summary judgment for appellee city in a declaratory judgment action that sought to set aside a municipal zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, property owner, brought an action against appellee city for a declaratory judgment to set aside a municipal zoning ordinance. The lower court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment and denied appellant's motion for summary judgment. The court reversed and remanded appellant's claim of unlawful gerrymandering because that issue was not addressed by appellee and summary judgment was not proper as to that issue. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment because the Validation Statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 974d-37 (1991), applied to governmental proceedings that occurred between the date that the statute was passed and its effective date, and cured any nonconstitutional defects in the rezoning ordinance at issue. The court held that pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 37.009 (1986), appellee was liable for attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court that granted summary judgment for appellee city in a declaratory judgment action was reversed and remanded in part because appellee did not address appellant, property owner's, claim of unlawful gerrymandering in its motion for summary judgment, summary judgment was not proper. The judgment was affirmed in part because any nonconstitutional defects in the ordinance at issue were cured by a validation statute.

Taub v. City of Deer Park


No. A14-90-00292-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


885 S.W.2d 161; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1893



July 25, 1991, Rendered  
July 25, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 165th Judicial District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 80-35666.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment of the 165th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas) in favor of appellee city, which condemned a portion of his property for street and drainage ditch improvements and denied his application to rezone one of the remaining portions of the property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner contended that appellee city abused its discretion in denying his application to rezone a portion of his remaining property and that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional because it rendered the property worthless. The court concluded that there was a rational basis for denying the rezoning and that the ordinance was not unconstitutional because the evidence was insufficient to prove that multi-family development would be more feasible than single family development. Contrary to appellant's assertion, the court found that Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 21.021 (1984) permitted appellee to deposit the award with the court and fix the date of taking. Appellant also contended that the taking for a drainage ditch decreased the value of his remaining property. The court found no evidence of diminished value and, on the contrary, found that the improved drainage may have made the property more susceptible to development. Last, the court agreed with appellant that the judgment required correction, and a more definite property description, and reversed and remanded for entry of a corrected judgment.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellant landowner's points of error concerning the amount awarded in the condemnation judgment for appellee city, but reversed and remanded the judgment for correction and a more definite description of the property taken.

Gant v. State


Nos. 3-89-150-CR, 3-89-151-CR, 3-89-152-CR, 3-89-153-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


814 S.W.2d 444; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1868



July 24, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 14, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District; Nos. 88,664, 88,665, 88,666, and 88,667, Honorable Tom Blackwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on All Causes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought reversal, on multiple grounds, of his several convictions for securities violations imposed by the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his multiple convictions for securities violations and the resultant punishments. The court affirmed, holding that the evidence was sufficient to convict, given that appellant had failed to disclose to prospective investors that he had used previous investors' funds for unauthorized purposes. It was not necessary that he be charged with having done that in order to trigger his obligation to disclose that fact. The court also held that appellant's indictments sufficiently alleged the elements necessary to charge him with fraud in connection with the sale of securities. The court further held that there was no error in refusing to provide a mistake-of-fact defense instruction, inasmuch as appellant failed to introduce evidence that his mistake was reasonable and negated the culpable mental state required for the crime. Finally, the court held that the Securities Act was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: Appellant's securities convictions were affirmed. His insufficient evidence, inadequate indictments, jury instructional error, and void-for-vagueness challenges were all found lacking in merit.

Burns v. State


No. A14-90-00499-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


814 S.W.2d 768; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1771



July 18, 1991, Rendered  
July 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 133rd District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 498,753-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety challenged a decision from the 133rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which entered summary judgment in favor of the state in its bond forfeiture action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant surety executed a bond on behalf of a client. The client failed to appear at a hearing, so the trial court ordered the bond forfeited. The trial court signed a judgment nisi and issued a citation. After appellant filed an answer, the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the state. Appellant alleged that the client did not receive notice and the trial court did not comply with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.02. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Evidence established that notice of the hearing was sent to appellant. As required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.13, appellant failed to show sufficient cause for the client's failure to appear. The judgment nisi provided sufficient proof that the trial court complied with the requirements of article 22.02. The judgment specifically provided that the client's name was called at the courthouse door.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision. Appellant surety failed to prove that uncontrollable circumstances prevented the client form appearing at the scheduled hearing. The trial court's judgment nisi specifically provided that the client's name was called at the courthouse door as required by the Texas Code of Criminal Procedure.

Pierce v. State


No. C14-90-01047-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1800



July 18, 1991, Rendered  
July 18, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court; Brazoria County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 21,407.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed an order of the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, which denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus. Appellant alleged that his indictment for the offense of possession of a controlled substance while he was in the confines of property belonging to the Texas Department of Corrections was void because the pertinent statute, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 499.004 (1990), violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted of possession of controlled substance in a prison system. Appellant sought a writ of habeas corpus, in which he alleged that the indictment violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 because the statute provision, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 499.004 (1990), contained multiple subjects in one bill. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of his writ of habeas corpus finding that in determining if a bill included more than one subject, the constitutional provision and the statute were to be liberally construed in favor of constitutionality. The court found that it was not unconstitutional in providing for criminal penalties for the possession of controlled substance in the prison system included in an act relating to the management of Texas prisons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus because the statute providing for criminal penalties for the possession of controlled substances in the prison system that included an act relating to the management of Texas prisons did not violate the Texas Constitution.

Kirby v. State


No. 01-90-00421-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1802



July 18, 1991, Delivered  
July 18, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 179th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 551174. 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the 179th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which adjudicated defendant guilty of possession of controlled substance and sentenced defendant to 17 years confinement after a probation revocation hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance, marijuana, and received deferred adjudication and subsequently sentenced to 17 years confinement after probation revocation hearing. On appeal, defendant argued that his right to due process was violated because the trial judge was not neutral and detached magistrate and that he was not afforded effective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed and held that if final adjudication was deferred, the decision to finally enter judgment was not reviewable, and that the remainder of the proceedings were subject to ordinary review. The court held that even if it was error for the trial judge to preside over the part of the hearing dealing with aggravated perjury, such error was harmless. The court held that it would not second-guess trial strategy of defense counsel and that probable harm was not shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of possession of a controlled substance, marijuana, because no appeal could be taken from the trial court's determination after a hearing to proceed with an adjudication of guilt on the original charge. The court held that it would not second-guess trial strategy of defense counsel.

 

1600 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fibreboard Corp. v. Pool


Nos. 6-90-014-CV, 6-90-022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


813 S.W.2d 658; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1773; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,990



July 16, 1991  
July 16, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Withdrawn July 16, 1991; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1773. Application for Writ of Error Granted April 29, 1992. Motion for Rehearing of Point of Error No. 5 in Application for Writ of Error on Behalf of the Flintkote Company Overruled June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of April 30, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1088. On Appeal from the 4th Judicial District Court; Rusk County, Texas; Trial Court Nos. 86-363, 88-08-293.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In asbestos litigation, defendant manufacturers appealed judgment of the 4th Judicial District Court of Rusk County (Texas), which awarded damages to plaintiff workers for defendants' strict liability for failure to warn. Defendants raised 35 points on appeal, arguing that evidence for future medical expenses and punitive damages did not support those awards, and that the trial court erred in not directing verdict or entering judgment n.o.v.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asbestos manufacturers raised 35 points on appeal of the trial court's award of damages to plaintiff workers in plaintiffs' actions for strict liability for failure to warn. Defendants argued that evidence for future medical expenses and punitive damages did not support those awards, and that the trial court erred in not directing verdict or entering judgment n.o.v. The court held that if one plaintiff did not make a remittitur of his future medical expense award, his case would be retried because he failed to show a reasonable probability. The court also ruled that the evidence did not show conscious indifference by one defendant and set aside that portion of the award of punitive damages. The court otherwise affirmed. Plaintiffs established that the dangers of asbestos were reasonably foreseeable or discoverable at the time of exposure. As to the denial of the motion for directed verdict, the court held that the question was whether the evidence adduced at the time the plaintiffs rested, viewed in the light most favorable to the plaintiffs, raised an issue for the jury. The court ruled that sufficient evidence supported the verdict and that other errors were harmless.


OUTCOME: The court set aside award of punitive damages against one defendant asbestos manufacturer and held that if one plaintiff worker refused to make a voluntary remittitur of his award for future medical expenses, his case would be remanded for a new trial. The court otherwise affirmed, ruling that the judgments were supported by the evidence that the dangers of asbestos were reasonably foreseeable or discoverable at the time of plaintiffs' exposure.
